Khums on Rikaz in 'Ushr and Kharaj Land
Ruling on khums for rikaz in 'ushr/kharaj land with exclusions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khums for rikaz found in 'ushr and kharaj land, identify excluded land types, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Rikaz in 'ushr or kharaj land requires khums; houses and Dar al-Harb are excluded.

This lesson examines a key ruling on buried treasure (rikaz) from the chapter on zakat. The matn states simply: 'In kharaj land or 'ushr land, khums.' The commentary unpacks this by clarifying which lands trigger the khums obligation and which do not. Understanding this qualification is essential to correctly applying the hadith 'In rikaz, one-fifth.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is finding rikaz (buried treasure from pre-Islamic times). The ruling is that khums (one-fifth) is wajib on the finder. This is derived from the hadith.
The ruling applies specifically to rikaz, not to other found items (luqata).
2
Identify the qualifying condition
The khums is only due if the rikaz is found on 'ushr land or kharaj land. These are defined in the notes: 'ushr land is land of Muslims or conquered land distributed to Muslims; kharaj land is conquered land left with original owners who pay tax.
3
Note the exclusions
The commentary explicitly excludes a house (dar) — no khums on rikaz found inside a building. It also discusses Dar al-Harb (non-Muslim territory) as excluded, and explains that deserts (mafaza) are included by primary reasoning.
The exclusion of Dar al-Harb is based on the land not being 'ushri or kharaji.
4
Cite the evidence
The primary dalil is the hadith: 'في الركاز الخمس' (In rikaz, one-fifth). This is recorded in the six authentic hadith collections. The Hanafi school applies this hadith to the specific land types as outlined.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning and considered qat'i al-thubut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة باب الركاز
في أرض خراج أو عُشْر خُمس
(1X1)
في أرض خَراج أو عُشْرِ خُمس
[۲]
[1]قوله : في أرض خراج ؛ بالفتح ، أو عُشر بالضم ؛ أي الأرض التي يجب على مالكها فيها أداء عشر ما خرج منها ، والأرض التي فيها على مالكها الخراج، وسيأتي تفصيلهما إن شاء الله، وهذا القيد ليخرج الدار ، فإنه لا شيء فيهما. كذا في «فتح القدير»
لكن يرد عليه الأرض التي لا وظيفة فيها كالمفازة، فيلزم أن يؤخذ شيء من المأخون منها، وليس كذلك إلا أن يقال : يعلم حكم المفازة بالطريق الأولى؛ لأنه إذا وجب في الأرض مع الوظيفة، وهي العشر أو الخراج فلان يجب في الخالية منها أولى. وذكر إسماعيل النابلسي في «شرح الدرر»: إنّه احترازٌ عَمَّا وُجِدَ في دار الحرب، فإن أرضها ليست عشرية ولا خراجية، والمراد بأرض الخراج والعشر أعم من أن تكون مملوكة لأحد أو صالحة للزراعة أو لا، فتدخل فيها المفاوز، وأرض الموات، فإنّها إذا جعلت صالحة للزراعة كانت عشرية أو خراجية.
[٢] قوله : خُمس ؛ مجهول من خَمَسَ الإمام من باب طَلَب، إذا أخذ الخمس. كذا في «المغرب» ، لا من التخميس ؛ لأنه جعل الشيء ذا أخماس، وهو غير مراد، أي أخذ الإمامُ منه خمسه وأدخله في بيت المال وأعطى باقيه وهو أربعة أخماس لمن وجده. والأصل في هذا الباب حديث: «في الركاز الخمس )، وهو مخرج في الصحاح الستة وغيرها .
(1) أرض الخراج: وهي كل ما فتح عنوة، وأقر أهلُهُ عليه، أو صالح الإمام مع أهلها أن يقرهم عليها ولم ينقلهم إلى موضع آخر ؛ لأن اللائق بالكفار ابتداء الخراج، سوى مكة. وسيأتي تفصيله. ينظر : (مجمع الأنهر» (١) : ٦٦٣).
(٢) أرض العشر : هي أرض العرب وما أسلم أهله، أو فتح عنوة وقسم بين الغانمين. وسيأتي تفصيله. وتمامها في (البحر»٥ : ١١٤).
(۳) «فتح القدير (٢) : ٢٣٤).
(٤) «المغرب»(ص١٥٤).
(٥) في (صحيح مسلم (٣: ١٣٣٤) ، و(صحيح البخاري»(٢ : ٥٤٤)، وغيرها.
Book of Zakah, Chapter of Rikaz. In kharaj land or 'ushr land, khums. ... (1X1) In kharaj land or 'ushr land, khums. [2] [1] His statement: 'in kharaj land' with fath, or 'ushr with damm; i.e., the land upon whose owner is obligatory to pay one-tenth of its produce, and the land upon which its owner owes kharaj, and their detail will come if Allah wills. This stipulation is to exclude a house, for there is nothing on either. As in Fath al-Qadir. But there is an objection regarding land that has no function like the desert, so it would be necessary to take something from what is taken from it, but it is not so unless it is said: the ruling of the desert is known by primary reasoning; because if it is obligatory on land with a function, which is 'ushr or kharaj, then it is more appropriate to be required from the empty one. Isma'il al-Nabulsi mentioned in Sharh al-Durar: It is a precaution against what is found in Dar al-Harb, for its land is neither 'ushri nor kharaji. And the meaning of 'ushr and kharaj land is general, whether owned by someone or suitable for cultivation or not, so deserts and barren lands are included, for if they are made suitable for cultivation they become 'ushri or kharaji. [2] His statement: 'khums' is a passive verb from 'khamasa al-imam' from the form of 'talab', when he takes the one-fifth. As in al-Mughrib, not from takhmis because that means making something into fifths, which is not intended. That is, the imam takes its one-fifth and enters it into the treasury and gives the remainder, which is four-fifths, to its finder. The basis of this chapter is the hadith: 'In rikaz, one-fifth', and it is recorded in the six authentic books and others. (1) Kharaj land: every land conquered by force and its people left upon it, or the imam made a peace treaty with its people to let them stay without moving them to another place; because what befits the disbelievers initially is kharaj, except Mecca. Its detail will come. See Majma' al-Anhur (1:663). (2) 'Ushr land: the land of the Arabs and those whose people accepted Islam, or conquered by force and distributed among the warriors. Its detail will come. Its completion is in al-Bahr (5:114). (3) Fath al-Qadir (2:234). (4) Al-Mughrib (p.154). (5) In Sahih Muslim (3:1334) and Sahih al-Bukhari (2:544) and others.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the chapter of Rikaz. The matn states: 'In kharaj land or 'ushr land, khums.' The commentator explains that this means rikaz found in land subject to 'ushr (tithe on produce) or kharaj (land tax) requires the payment of khums (one-fifth). The stipulation excludes found property in a house (dar), which is not subject to khums. It also excludes rikaz found in Dar al-Harb (non-Muslim territory) as per one opinion. However, land that has no tax function like the desert (mafaza) is still considered 'ushr or kharaj land by primary reasoning. The commentator clarifies that 'khums' here means the imam takes one-fifth and gives four-fifths to the finder. The basis is the hadith 'Fi al-rikaz al-khums' (In buried treasure, one-fifth). The Hanafi position is that this applies to rikaz found in these lands, regardless of whether the land is owned or barren.

Key Terms
أرض خراج (arḍ kharāj): Land conquered by force whose inhabitants pay kharaj (land tax).
أرض عُشْر (arḍ ‘ushr): Land on which the owner pays one-tenth of its produce.
خُمس (khums): One-fifth; the share of the state from rikaz.
الركاز (al-rikāz): Buried treasure from pre-Islamic times (or generally, buried wealth).
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory under non-Muslim rule with no treaty of peace.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what type of land is excluded from the khums ruling on rikaz?
A) 'Ushr land
B) Kharaj land
C) A house (dar)
D) Desert (mafaza)

Key Takeaway
Khums on rikaz is wajib only when found on 'ushr or kharaj land; houses and Dar al-Harb are excluded.

Treasure Trove (Rikaz): Khums in Kharaj, Ushr Land, and Private Property
Explains ruling on rikaz in kharaj, ushr land, and private property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rikaz in kharaj, 'ushr, and owned land, identify the two narrations from Abu Hanifa, and explain why the Sahibayn's view is the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
For rikaz in owned land, two narrations exist; the mufta bihi imposes khums due to land's annual burden.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on treasure trove (rikaz) across different land types. The commentator on al-Wiqayah explains that khums is wajib on rikaz found in kharaj or 'ushr land, but no khums is due on treasure found in one's own house. However, a dispute arises regarding owned agricultural land: Abu Hanifa has two narrations, and the later preferred view (mufta bihi) is that khums is due, following the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the land types and baseline ruling
Recognise that the first ruling distinguishes between land with an annual levy (kharaj or 'ushr) and a house: in the former, khums is wajib; in the latter, nothing is due.
The ruling also covers barren land (mafazah) by primary analogy.
2
Understand the house exception
A house has no mu'nah (annual burden), so treasure found in it is considered part of the property; the finder keeps everything.
This is undisputed.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
For owned agricultural land, the text presents two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one (from al-Asl) treats land like a house, the other (from al-Jami' al-Saghir) distinguishes based on mu'nah.
The initial statement in the passage reflects the latter narration, but the commentator clarifies the dispute.
4
Apply the tarjih mechanism
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) prefer the narration imposing khums; this is the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) for fatwa.
The basis: land bears kharaj or 'ushr, so khums applies; the finder then gives the remainder to the landowner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة باب الركاز

في أرض خراج أو عُشْر خُمس

[1]قوله : في أرض خراج ؛ بالفتح ، أو عُشر بالضم ؛ أي الأرض التي يجب على مالكها فيها أداء عشر ما خرج منها ، والأرض التي فيها على مالكها الخراج، وسيأتي تفصيلهما إن شاء الله، وهذا القيد ليخرج الدار ، فإنه لا شيء فيهما. كذا في «فتح القدير»

لكن يرد عليه الأرض التي لا وظيفة فيها كالمفازة، فيلزم أن يؤخذ شيء من المأخون منها، وليس كذلك إلا أن يقال : يعلم حكم المفازة بالطريق الأولى؛ لأنه إذا وجب في الأرض مع الوظيفة، وهي العشر أو الخراج فلان يجب في الخالية منها أولى. وذكر إسماعيل النابلسي في «شرح الدرر»: إنّه احترازٌ عَمَّا وُجِدَ في دار الحرب، فإن أرضها ليست عشرية ولا خراجية، والمراد بأرض الخراج والعشر أعم من أن تكون مملوكة لأحد أو صالحة للزراعة أو لا، فتدخل فيها المفاوز، وأرض الموات، فإنّها إذا جعلت صالحة للزراعة كانت عشرية أو خراجية.

[2] قوله : خُمس ؛ مجهول من خَمَسَ الإمام من باب طَلَب، إذا أخذ الخمس. كذا في «المغرب» ، لا من التخميس ؛ لأنه جعل الشيء ذا أخماس، وهو غير مراد، أي أخذ الإمامُ منه خمسه وأدخله في بيت المال وأعطى باقيه وهو أربعة أخماس لمن وجده. والأصل في هذا الباب حديث: «في الركاز الخمس»، وهو مخرج في الصحاح الستة وغيرها.

وباقيه للواجد إن لم تملك أرضُهُ ، وإلا فلمالكها.

[1]قوله : وإلا فلمالكها ؛ أي إن كانت الأرض التي وجد فيها مملوكة لأحد ، فالباقي بعد أداء الخمس للمالك ، ولا يخفى على الفطن أنَّ هذه الجملة مستدركة لما يأتي من قوله : «وفي أرضه روايتان» ؛ إلا أن يقرّ اقتصرَ هاهنا على رواية واحدة عن أبي حنيفة ، وهي التي اختارها أبو يوسف ومحمد ، ونص عليه في «الجامع الصغير»، وذكر تعدُّد الرواية فيما يأتي.

ولا شيء فيه إن وجده في داره. وفي أرضه روايتان.

[2]قوله : ولا شيء؛ أي لا يجب الخمس على من وجد معدناً في داره المملوكة ؛ لأنه من أجزائها فيملكه من يملكها.

[3] قوله : روايتان ؛ قال في غاية «البيان»: في الأرض المملوكة روايتان عن أبي حنيفة ففي رواية «الأصل»: لا فرق بين الأرض والدَّارِ حيث لا شيء فيهما ؛ لأنَّ الأرضَ لَمَّا انتقلت إليه انتقلت بجميع أجزائها ، والمعدن من تربة الأرض، فلم يجب فيه شيء كالغنيمة إذا باعها الإمام من إنسان سقط عنها حق سائر الناس ؛ لأنه ملكها ببدل، كذا قال الجصاص. وفي رواية «الجامع الصغير»: بينهما فرق ، ووجد أنَّ الدار لا مؤونة فيها فلم تخمس، فصار الكل للواجدِ بخلاف الأرض ، فإنَّ فيها مؤنة الخراج والعشرِ فتخمس. انتهى.

وفي المقام تفصيل ذكرتُ نبذاً منه في «التَّعليق الممجّد على موطأ الإمام محمد».
The Book of Zakat, Chapter on Rikaz

In kharaj land or 'ushr land, one-fifth.

[1] His statement: "In kharaj land" (with fatḥa on the khāʼ) or "'ushr" (with ḍamma on the ʻayn) i.e., the land upon whose owner it is obligatory to pay a tenth of what comes out of it, and the land upon which kharaj is obligatory on its owner. Their details will come later, God willing. This restriction is to exclude the house, for there is nothing in either. Thus in Fatḥ al-Qadīr.

But there is an objection concerning land that has no levy such as the desert wilderness, which would require something to be taken from what is found there, but that is not the case unless it is said: the ruling of the wilderness is known by the primary path, because if it is obligatory in land with a levy—tithe or kharaj—then it is more fitting that it be obligatory in land devoid of them. Ismāʻīl al-Nābulsī mentioned in Sharḥ al-Durar that it is a precaution against what is found in the abode of war, for its land is neither tithe nor kharaj land. And by "kharaj land" and "tithe land" is meant generally, whether owned by someone or suitable for agriculture or not, so it includes wilderness and dead land, for if they are made suitable for agriculture, they become tithe or kharaj land.

[2] His statement: "one-fifth" is a passive verb from "the Imam took one-fifth" from the measure of ṭalaba, meaning he took the khums. Thus in al-Mughrib, not from takhmīs because that is making something into fifths, which is not intended. That is, the Imam takes its fifth and puts it into the public treasury and gives the rest—four-fifths—to the finder. The foundation in this chapter is the hadith: "In rikaz, one-fifth," which is recorded in the six authentic books and others.

And the rest is for the finder if his land is not owned, otherwise it belongs to its owner.

[1] His statement: "otherwise it belongs to its owner" means that if the land in which it was found is owned by someone, then the remainder after paying the fifth belongs to the owner. It is not hidden from the intelligent that this sentence is redundant with what comes later: "and in his land there are two narrations"; unless it is said that he restricted here to one narration from Abū Ḥanīfa, which is the one chosen by Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad, and it is stated in al-Jāmiʻ al-Ṣaghīr, and he mentioned the multiplicity of narrations later.

And there is nothing in it if he finds it in his house. And in his land there are two narrations.

[2] His statement: "and there is nothing" means that khums is not obligatory on one who finds a mine in his owned house because it is part of its components, so he owns it as he owns the house.

[3] His statement: "two narrations"; he said in Ghāyat al-Bayān: concerning owned land, there are two narrations from Abū Ḥanīfa. In the narration of al-Aṣl: there is no difference between land and the house, where there is nothing in both; because when the land is transferred to him, it is transferred with all its components, and the mine is from the soil of the land, so nothing is obligatory on it, like spoils when the Imam sells them to a person, the right of other people drops, because he owns it for a price, as al-Jaṣṣāṣ said. In the narration of al-Jāmiʻ al-Ṣaghīr: there is a difference between them, and it is found that the house has no annual burden so it is not khumsed, so everything goes to the finder, unlike land, for it has the burden of kharaj or tithe, so it is khumsed. End.

And in this context, there is a detail, some of which I mentioned in al-Taʻlīq al-Mumajjad ʻalā Muwaṭṭaʼ al-Imām Muḥammad.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqāyah addresses the chapter on rikāz (treasure trove) within the Book of Zakat. The commentator first explains that the ruling of khums (one-fifth) applies specifically to treasure found in land that is subject to either 'ushr (tithe) or kharaj (land tax). This restriction excludes treasure found in a house, for which no khums is due. A potential objection concerning barren land (mafāzah) is raised; the commentator resolves it by noting that such land is likewise covered by the general rule, and indeed the obligation is more fitting when no levy exists, following the principle of a fortiori reasoning. Alternatively, the restriction is meant to exclude Dār al-Ḥarb (non-Muslim territory) whose land is not subject to these levies. The commentator then explains the linguistic derivation of 'khums' and cites the well-known hadith 'In rikāz, one-fifth' as the foundational proof. The passage then turns to the disposition of the remaining four-fifths: if the land is not owned (e.g., public or dead land), the finder keeps it; if the land is privately owned, the owner takes it. However, a later passage mentions two narrations regarding treasure found in one's own land. The commentator clarifies that the initial statement (that the remainder goes to the landowner) actually represents only one narration—the one preferred by the two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) and recorded in al-Jāmiʻ al-Ṣaghīr. The two narrations are then detailed: according to the narration of al-Aṣl, there is no difference between land and house—both yield nothing beyond the finder's ownership because the land is transferred with all its parts, analogous to spoils purchased from the Imam. According to the narration of al-Jāmiʻ al-Ṣaghīr, a distinction exists: a house has no annual burden (mu'nah), so nothing is taken; but land is subject to kharaj or 'ushr, so the khums is taken. The commentator also refers the reader to his own work, al-Taʻlīq al-Mumajjad, for further detail.

Key Terms
ركاز (rikāz): Treasure trove or buried mineral wealth found in the earth.
خمس (khums): One-fifth (20%) of the treasure that must be given to the Islamic treasury.
أرض خراج (arḍ kharāj): Land upon which the owner must pay kharaj (land tax); typically conquered lands left in the hands of non-Muslims.
أرض عشر (arḍ 'ushr): Land upon which the owner must pay 'ushr (tithe); typically lands of Muslims or conquered lands divided among Muslims.
دار (dār): A house or residential building, as opposed to agricultural land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone finds treasure in their own house, what is the ruling?
A) The finder must give one-fifth to the state.
B) The finder keeps everything because the treasure is part of the house.
C) The finder must give one-fifth to the landowner.
D) The finder must give the entire treasure to the state.

Key Takeaway
Khums on rikaz is wajib in kharaj/'ushr land, but in one's own house there is no khums; for owned agricultural land, the mufta bihi (following Sahibayn) imposes khums.

Rikaz After Khums: Remainder and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Owned Land
Ruling on remainder of rikaz after khums and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the remainder of rikaz after khums, distinguish the two narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding owned land, and apply the preferred view based on the reasoning of expenses (mu'unah).

Core Idea
Khums on rikaz depends on expenses: land incurs kharaj/ushr so khums applies; a house does not, so no khums.

This passage clarifies the distribution of rikaz (buried treasure) after paying the obligatory khums (one-fifth). It presents three scenarios based on land ownership and an important intra-Hanafi dispute: two conflicting narrations from Abu Hanifa himself on whether khums is due on rikaz found in owned land. The commentator explains the reasoning behind each view and identifies the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). Understanding this rule ensures correct payment of zakah obligations on treasure troves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three cases: unowned land, owned land, and owned house. Note the ruling for each: remainder to finder, remainder to owner of land, and no khums if found in one's own house.
The key distinction is whether the land is owned by someone else or not.
2
Locate the two narrations
Find the two narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding owned land: (1) from al-Asl: no difference between land and house, so no khums on land; (2) from al-Jami' al-Saghir: khums is due on land because of expenses.
Both narrations are attributed to Abu Hanifa, but the second is preferred by the Sahibayn.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Understand the illah (effective cause) for each narration. The first: land transfers with all its parts, like a house; thus no khums. The second: land incurs kharaj and 'ushr expenses, so khums is due by analogy to ghanimah.
The presence or absence of mu'unah (expenses) is the distinguishing factor.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine which narration is mufta bihi (relied upon). The commentator states that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad chose the view of al-Jami' al-Saghir, and it is the established position in the school.
The preferred view is that khums applies to owned land.
5
Apply the ruling
Apply the mufta bihi ruling to a new scenario: A treasure found on agricultural land subject to kharaj. The finder must pay khums, and the remainder goes to the landowner.
If the land is not owned, the finder keeps the remainder after khums.

وباقيه للواجد إن لم تملك أرضُهُ ، وإلا فلمالكها ، ولا شيء فيه إن وجده في داره وفي أرضه روايتان . قوله : وإلا فلمالكها ؛ أي إن كانت الأرض التي وجد فيها مملوكة لأحد ، فالباقي بعد أداء الخمس للمالك ، ولا يخفى على الفطن أنَّ هذه الجملة مستدركة لما يأتي من قوله : «وفي أرضه روايتان» ؛ إلا أن يقرّ اقتصرَ هاهنا على رواية واحدة عن أبي حنيفة ، وهي التي اختارها أبو يوسف ومحمد ، ونص عليه في «الجامع الصغير»، وذكر تعدُّد الرواية فيما يأتي. قوله : ولا شيء؛ أي لا يجب الخمس على من وجد معدناً في داره المملوكة ؛ لأنه من أجزائها فيملكه من يملكها. قوله : روايتان ؛ قال في غاية «البيان»: في الأرض المملوكة روايتان عن أبي حنيفة ففي رواية «الأصل» : لا فرق بين الأرض والدَّارِ حيث لا شيء فيهما ؛ لأنَّ الأرضَ لَمَّا انتقلت إليه انتقلت بجميع أجزائها ، والمعدن من تربة الأرض، فلم يجب فيه شيء كالغنيمة إذا باعها الإمام من إنسان سقط عنها حق سائر الناس ؛ لأنه ملكها ببدل، كذا قال الجصاص. وفي رواية «الجامع الصغير» : بينهما فرق ، ووجد أنَّ الدار لا مؤونة فيها فلم تخمس، فصار الكل للواجدِ بخلاف الأرض ، فإنَّ فيها مؤنة الخراج والعشرِ فتخمس. انتهى.
And the remainder is for the finder if his land is not owned, otherwise it belongs to its owner, and there is nothing [i.e., no khums] on it if he finds it in his house, and regarding his land there are two narrations. [Commentary:] 'And otherwise it belongs to its owner' means that if the land in which it was found is owned by someone, then the remainder after paying the khums is for the owner. It is not hidden from the intelligent that this sentence is an insertion because of what is to come in his statement: 'and regarding his land there are two narrations' except that he restricted himself here to one narration from Abu Hanifa, which is the one chosen by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad and stated in al-Jami' al-Saghir, and he mentions the multiplicity of narrations later. [Commentary on 'and there is nothing']: That is, khums is not owed on one who finds a mine in his owned house, because it is part of its components, so its owner owns it. [Commentary on 'two narrations']: He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: concerning owned land, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. In the narration of al-Asl: no difference between land and house, meaning nothing is owed on either, because the land has transferred to him with all its parts, and the mine is from the soil of the land, so nothing is required on it, like spoils if the Imam sells them to a person, the right of other people falls away because he takes ownership in exchange, as said by al-Jassas. In the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir: there is a difference, and it is observed that the house has no expenses (mu'unah) so it is not subject to khums, so everything goes to the finder, unlike land which does have expenses of kharaj and 'ushr, so it is subject to khums. End.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage addresses the distribution of rikaz (treasure) after the khums (one-fifth) has been removed. The author distinguishes three scenarios: (1) If the treasure is found on unowned land, the remainder goes to the finder; (2) if on owned land, the remainder goes to the landowner; (3) if found in one's own house, no khums is due at all. Additionally, there is a disagreement within the Hanafi school regarding land: one narration (from al-Asl) equates land with a house (no khums), while another (al-Jami' al-Saghir) differentiates because land is subject to kharaj and 'ushr expenses, so khums applies. The commentator explains that the phrase 'otherwise to its owner' anticipates the two narrations, and the relied-upon position is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, supporting khums on land. The reasoning for land's khums is based on analogy to ghanimah (spoils) which has expenses, and the absence of expenses on a house is the distinguishing factor.

Key Terms
ركاز (rikaz): Buried treasure from pre-Islamic times, or any mineral deposit subject to khums.
خمس (khums): One-fifth tax due on rikaz.
رواية (riwayah): A transmitted narration from an imam, in this case from Abu Hanifa, representing different opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No khums is due; the finder keeps everything.
B) Khums is paid, and the remainder goes to the landowner.
C) Khums is paid, and the remainder goes to the finder.
D) The landowner pays khums on behalf of the finder.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon ruling is that rikaz found on owned land is subject to khums, with the remainder belonging to the landowner, due to the expenses associated with land.

Khums on Sea Treasures and Stones: The Hanafi Exemption
Ruling with proof on khums exemption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that no khums is due on items from the sea or stones, explain the proof from hadith, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Khums is only on spoils taken by force; sea and stones are not ghanimah.

This passage clarifies the Hanafi position on khums for valuable items like pearls, amber, and precious stones. The key distinction is that khums is derived from ghanimah (spoils of war obtained by force). Since the sea and mountains are not conquered territories, items extracted from them do not qualify. An internal Hanafi dispute is noted: Abu Yusuf held that khums applies to sea items, but the relied-upon position is the majority view. A hadith 'no zakat on stones' provides additional support for stones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items in question
Note the specific items mentioned: pearls (lu'lu'), amber ('anbar), and firuzaj (turquoise) found in mountains. The principle extends to all sea extracts and stones.
The commentary generalizes to anything from the sea or any precious stone.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The ruling is straightforward: no khums is due on these items. Understand why: khums is a right on ghanimah.
3
Understand the rationale
Khums originates from ghanimah, which requires forceful conquest from disbelievers. The sea bottom and mountains have never been subdued by force, so they do not qualify.
Even a treasure of gold at the bottom of the sea is exempt.
4
Examine the hadith proof
For stones, the hadith 'There is no zakat on stones' (reported by Ibn 'Adi) is cited. The word 'hajar' includes all stones, even precious ones.
This hadith reinforces the exemption.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that khums is due on sea items. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) disagree. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
The differing opinion does not affect the operative fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا في لؤلؤ، وعنبر، وفيروزَجَ وُجِدَ في جبل . قوله : ولا في لؤلؤ ... الخ ؛ اللؤلؤ بضم اللامــين ، بينهما وبعدهما واو وهمزة هو يخلق من مطر الربيع إذا وقع في الصدف ، وقيل : إِنَّ الصَّدف حيوان يخلق فيه اللؤلؤ. والعنبر؛ على وزن جعفر، ينبتُ في البحر بمنزلة الحشيش في البر، وقيل: إنّه شجر ينكسر فيلقيها الموجُ إلى الساحل ، وقيل : هي ختى دابة بحرية ، وقيل : إِنَّه زيدُ البحر. والفيروزج ؛ معرَّب فيروزه. والحاصل أنه لا خمس في كل ما يستخرج من البحر، ولو كان ذهباً كُنز في قعرِ البحر، فإنَّ أصل الخمس في الغنيمة، وهي ما كانت للكفرة ثم صارت للمسلمين بحكم القهر والغلبة، وباطن البحر لم يرد عليه قهر أحد، فلم يكن المأخوذ منه في حكـم الغنيمة، وكذا لا خمس في الأحجار كالفيروزج والياقوت والزمرد وغيرها ؛ لحديث : لا زكاة في الحجر»، أخرجه ابن عدي. ويخمس عند أبي يوسف له ما يوجد في البحر أيضاً.
And not on pearls, amber, and firuzaj found in a mountain. [Commentary:] 'And not on pearls...' The pearl is formed from spring rain when it falls in an oyster; it is said the oyster is an animal that creates the pearl. Amber is like jafar [a weight], it grows in the sea like grass on land; it is said it is a tree that breaks and waves throw it to shore; it is said it is sea dung; it is said it is sea foam. Firuzaj is a Persian loanword. The gist: there is no khums on anything extracted from the sea, even if it is gold treasure in the bottom of the sea, because the origin of khums is on spoils, which are what belonged to disbelievers and then came to Muslims by force and domination, and the bottom of the sea has not been subjected to anyone's force, so what is taken from it is not in the category of spoils. Similarly, no khums on stones like firuzaj, ruby, emerald, etc., based on the hadith: 'There is no zakat on stones,' reported by Ibn 'Adi. And according to Abu Yusuf, khums is due on what is found in the sea as well.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage clarifies that items extracted from the sea or precious stones are not subject to khums. The reasoning is that khums is a right derived from ghanimah (spoils of war), which requires forceful acquisition from unbelievers. Since the sea and mountains are not conquered by force, items from them are not like spoils. An exception is noted: according to Abu Yusuf, even sea items require khums, but the Hanafi position is that no khums applies. A hadith is cited: 'No zakat on stones,' supporting the exemption.

Key Terms
لؤلؤ (lu'lu'): Pearls formed in oysters from spring rain.
عنبر ('anbar): Amber, a sea product resembling grass or tree remains.
فيروزج (firuzaj): A kind of stone, Persian loanword for turquoise.
بحر (bahr): Sea; items from the sea are exempt from khums.

D) Because they are subject to zakat instead.

Key Takeaway
Khums on sea items and stones is not wajib in the Hanafi school; only spoils of war by force trigger khums.

Treasure with Islamic Markings is Luqatah, Not Rikaz
Definition and ruling: treasure with Islamic marks is luqatah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that treasure bearing a mark of Islam is treated as luqatah and apply the rules of announcement and disposal.

Core Idea
A treasure bearing a mark of Islam is not rikaz but luqatah — it must be announced, not subjected to khums.

When a treasured item is found, its ruling depends on whether it bears signs of Muslim ownership. A treasure with Islamic markings (like the shahadah) is presumed to belong to a Muslim and thus falls under the rules of luqatah (lost property), not rikaz (pre-Islamic treasure subject to khums). This lesson explains the distinction and the practical steps the finder must take.

Guided Path
1
Identify the item as treasure with an Islamic mark
Look for inscriptions such as the shahadah or other known Muslim symbols that indicate the treasure was buried by Muslims.
The mark must be something specifically Muslim, not just any old marking.
2
Classify the treasure as luqatah, not rikaz
Because the mark suggests a Muslim owner, the treasure is considered lost property (luqatah) rather than rikaz, which would require khums (20% tax).
Rikaz is pre-Islamic treasure without any Muslim mark.
3
Apply the rules of luqatah
The finder must announce the find at mosques and markets for a period until it seems the owner will not claim it. Then, if the finder is poor, he may use it for himself; otherwise, he gives it to another poor person.
The announcement period is typically one year in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Understand the rationale
The mark of Islam is strong evidence that the wealth was owned by a Muslim, so the law presumes it is lost property rather than ownerless rikaz.
This protects the property rights of Muslims even after a long period.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكنز فيه سمة الإسلام كاللقطة . قوله : سمة الإسلام ؛ بكسر السين المهملة، وفتح الميم بمعنى العلامة، وذلك ككتابة كلمة الشهادة أو نقش آخر معروف للمسلمين، يعرف به آنه مال موضوع ومدفون من المسلمين. قوله : كاللقطة؛ هو بالضم ما يلتقط ويؤخذ من موضع لا يعرف مالكه ، وحكمها : أنه ينادى بها في أبواب المساجد والأسواق إلى أن يُظنَّ عدم الطلب، ثمّ يصرفها إلى نفسه إن كان فقيراً وإلا فإلى فقير آخر ، وستطلع على تفصيل ذلك في كتاب اللقطة إن شاء الله تعالى.
And a treasure in which there is a mark of Islam is like luqatah. [Commentary:] 'Mark of Islam' means a sign, such as writing the word of shahadah or another known Muslim inscription, by which it is known that this wealth was placed and buried by Muslims. 'Like luqatah' is what is picked up and taken from a place whose owner is not known. Its ruling is that it is announced at the doors of mosques and markets until non-claim is assumed, then the finder may spend it on himself if he is poor, otherwise to another poor person. The details will come in the Book of Luqatah, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between rikaz (pre-Islamic treasure subject to khums) and treasure bearing Islamic symbols. The latter is treated as luqatah (lost property) because it likely belonged to a Muslim. The finder must announce it publicly for a period; if unclaimed and the finder is in need, may keep it; otherwise, give it to charity. This ruling prevents the application of khums to Muslim-owned wealth.

Key Terms
سمة الإسلام (sibat al-Islam): A mark indicating Muslim ownership, such as the shahadah or other known Muslim inscriptions.
لقطة (luqatah): Lost property picked up from a place whose owner is unknown.

Key Takeaway

No Khums on Pearls, Amber, Turquoise from Sea or Mountain
Ruling with proof on exemption from khums for sea and mountain finds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khums for items found in the sea or mountains, identify the proof (dalil), and explain the exception for treasures with Islamic marks (simat al-Islam).

Core Idea
No khums on sea treasures or mountain stones because khums is tied to conquest and ghanima.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary clarifies that not all found treasures require khums. Pearls from the sea, amber, and mountain gemstones like turquoise are exempt—provided they are not from conquered enemy treasuries. The reasoning hinges on the definition of ghanima and a specific hadith. A nuance is added for items bearing a mark of Islam, which are treated as lost property (luqata).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the specific act or item being ruled upon? The passage states that there is no khums on pearls, amber, and turquoise found in a sea or mountain.
The ruling applies to items extracted from the sea or collected from mountains, not to spoils of war.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites the hadith 'No zakat on stones' (Ibn 'Adi) as evidence that gemstones are not subject to khums.
This hadith is taken as proof that stones, including precious ones, are not considered rikaz for khums.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly excludes stones from zakat, which the Hanafis extend to khums here. Additionally, the origin of khums is ghanima—spoils taken by force. Since the seabed has never been conquered, items from it are not ghanima.
The absence of conquest is the key distinction from land-based rikaz found on conquered territory.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf disagrees: he analogizes sea treasures to those found on conquered land and requires khums. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) maintain the exemption.
This intra-Hanafi difference shows how qiyas can lead to variant positions.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view that no khums is due. The Nihayah and later authorities support this.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the dalil and avoidance of qiyas against a clear textual indication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة باب الركاز
ولا في لؤلؤ، وعنبر، وفَيْرُوزَجَ وُجِدَ في جبل ، وكنز فيه سِمَةُ الإسلام كاللقطة
[1] قوله : ولا في لؤلؤ ... الخ ؛ اللؤلؤ بضم اللامــين ، بينهما وبعدهما واو وهمزة هو يخلق من مطر الربيع إذا وقع في الصدف ، وقيل : إِنَّ الصَّدف حيوان يخلق فيه اللؤلؤ.
والعنبر؛ على وزن جعفر، ينبتُ في البحر بمنزلة الحشيش في البر، وقيل: إنّه شجر ينكسر فيلقيها الموجُ إلى الساحل ، وقيل : هي ختى دابة بحرية ، وقيل : إِنَّه زيدُ البحر.
والفيروزج ؛ معرَّب فيروزه.
والحاصل أنه لا خمس في كل ما يستخرج من البحر، ولو كان ذهباً كُنز في قعرِ البحر، فإنَّ أصل الخمس في الغنيمة، وهي ما كانت للكفرة ثم صارت للمسلمين بحكم القهر والغلبة، وباطن البحر لم يرد عليه قهر أحد، فلم يكن المأخوذ منه في حكـم الغنيمة، وكذا لا خمس في الأحجار كالفيروزج والياقوت والزمرد وغيرها ؛ لحديث : لا زكاة في الحجر»، أخرجه ابن عدي. (٢) قوله : وُجِدَ في جبل ؛ صفةٌ لكلِّ ما ذكر، وهذا احتراز عما وجد في خزائن الكفار فأصيب قهراً، فإنّه يجب فيه الخمس بالاتفاق ، كذا في «النهاية»، ويخمس عند أبي يوسف له ما يوجد في البحر أيضاً.
[٣]قوله : سمة الإسلام ؛ بكسر السين المهملة، وفتح الميم بمعنى العلامة، وذلك ككتابة كلمة الشهادة أو نقش آخر معروف للمسلمين، يعرف به آنه مال موضوع ومدفون من المسلمين. [٤]قوله : كاللقطة؛ هو بالضم ما يلتقط ويؤخذ من موضع لا يعرف مالكه ، وحكمها : أنه ينادى بها في أبواب المساجد والأسواق إلى أن يُظنَّ عدم الطلب، ثمّ يصرفها إلى نفسه إن كان فقيراً وإلا فإلى فقير آخر ، وستطلع على تفصيل ذلك في كتاب اللقطة إن شاء الله تعالى.
Book of Zakat, Chapter of Rikaz. And no (khums) on pearls, amber, and turquoise found in a mountain, and a treasure that has the mark of Islam is like luqata. [1] His saying: 'and no on pearls... etc.'; pearls (al-lu'lu') with damma on both lams, between them and after them a waw and hamza, it is created from spring rain when it falls into an oyster shell, and it is said: the oyster is an animal in which pearls are created. Amber (al-'anbar) on the weight of ja'far, it grows in the sea like grass on land, and it is said: it is a tree that breaks and the waves cast it to the shore, and it is said: it is a sea animal's dung, and it is said: it is the foam of the sea. Turquoise (al-fayruzaj) is the Arabized form of firozeh. The conclusion is that there is no khums on everything extracted from the sea, even if it were gold as a treasure at the bottom of the sea, because the origin of khums is in ghanima (spoils), which are what belonged to the disbelievers and then became the Muslims' by force and domination, and the bottom of the sea has not been dominated by anyone, so what is taken from it is not in the ruling of ghanima. Similarly, there is no khuns on stones like turquoise, ruby, emerald, etc., due to the hadith: 'No zakat on stones' narrated by Ibn 'Adi. (2) His saying: 'found in a mountain' is a description for all that was mentioned, and this is a qualification for what is found in the treasuries of the disbelievers taken by force, for khuns is obligatory on it by agreement, as in al-Nihaya. And according to Abu Yusuf, khums is also due on what is found in the sea. [3] His saying: 'mark of Islam' (simat al-Islam) with kasra on the sin and fatha on the mim meaning a sign, such as writing the word of shahada or another known engraving of the Muslims by which it is known that it is property placed and buried by Muslims. [4] His saying: 'like luqata' (ka-al-luqata); it is with damma what is picked up and taken from a place whose owner is unknown, and its ruling is that it is announced at the doors of mosques and markets until it is thought that it will not be claimed, then he spends it on himself if he is poor, otherwise to another poor person, and you will see the details of that in the Book of Luqata, God willing.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. The matn states that there is no khums (one-fifth tax) on pearls, amber, and turquoise found in a mountain, and a treasure with a mark of Islam is treated like luqata (lost property). The commentator expands: The terms are defined — pearls are produced in oysters from rain, amber is a sea plant or animal product, turquoise is a Persian loanword. The general principle: no khums on anything extracted from the sea, even gold, because khums is only on ghanima (spoils taken by force from disbelievers). Since no one has conquered the seabed, it is not ghanima. Similarly, stones like turquoise, ruby, emerald have no khums based on the hadith 'no zakat on stones' (Ibn 'Adi). The phrase 'found in a mountain' qualifies these items, contrasting them with treasures found in disbelievers' treasuries taken by force, where khums is obligatory by agreement. However, Abu Yusuf holds that khums is also due on items found in the sea — an intra-Hanafi difference. The 'mark of Islam' means any symbol like the shahada showing the item was buried by Muslims. Such items are treated like luqata: announced, and if unclaimed, the finder (if poor) may use it, or give to another poor person. This is a complete legal unit on the absence of khums for sea and mountain treasures, with definitions, proofs, and an intra-madhhab nuance.

Key Terms
الركاز (al-rikaz): In this passage, rikaz refers to buried treasure or minerals. The chapter is about rikaz, but the ruling differentiates various types.
الخمس (al-khums): One-fifth tax on spoils of war and certain treasures (rikaz).
سمة الإسلام (simat al-Islam): A mark or sign indicating that the treasure was buried by Muslims, e.g., the shahada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) No khums is due because they are from the sea, not spoils of war.
C) Khums is due according to Abu Yusuf, and that is the fatwa.
D) They are treated like luqata and must be announced.

Key Takeaway
No khums is due on items from sea or mountain unless taken from a conquered enemy treasury, and items with Islamic marks are treated as lost property (luqata).

Khums on Treasures with the Mark of Disbelief
Ruling on khums for treasures with disbeliever marks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a found treasure (rikaz) incurs khums according to the Hanafi school and explain the underlying analogy to ghanima.

Core Idea
Khums is wajib on any treasure with a mark of kufr, following the analogy to ghanima.

When a Muslim finds treasure that bears a clear mark of disbelief—such as an idol or a king's name—the Hanafi school rules that khums (one-fifth) is due. This lesson unpacks the definition of 'simat al-kufr', the rationale behind the obligation, and clarifies that not all treasures are subject to khums.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its subject
The act is finding a buried treasure (kanz or rikaz). Determine if it bears a mark of disbelief (simat al-kufr) such as an idol engraving or a disbeliever king's name.
Treasures with Islamic symbols are treated as luqata (lost property), not subject to khums.
2
State the hukm
If the treasure has simat al-kufr, khums is wajib (obligatory). The teacher explains that this ruling is derived by analogy (qiyas) to ghanima (spoils of war).
Khums is only due on the treasure itself, not on minerals found in land; minerals are considered part of the land.
3
Understand the proof (qiyas)
The treasure is analogized to ghanima because it was placed by disbelievers and found by Muslims. Just as khums is obligatory on war spoils, it is also due on such treasure, since the treasure is not part of the land's soil.
The qiyas is based on the shared illa (effective cause): wealth left by disbelievers that Muslims gain control over.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما فيه سمة الكفرِ خُمس ، وباقيه للواجد إن لم تُمْلَك أرضُهُ، وإلا فللمختط له وركاز صحراء دار الحرب كله لمستأمن وَجَدَه
[1] قوله : سمة الكفر ؛ كنقش صنم أو اسم ملك من ملوكهم أو غير ذلك مما يعرفُ به أنه وضعه كافر. (۲) قوله : خُمس ؛ سواء كان في أرضه أو أرض غيره أو أرض مباحة ؛ لأنَّ الكنز ليس من أجزاء الدار فأمكن إيجاب الخمس فيه بخلاف المعدن.
[٣] قوله : وإلا ؛ أي وإن كانت الأرض التي وجد فيها مملوكة لأحد فهو للذي اختلط له، وهو الذي ملكه الإمام هذه البقعة يوم فتح تلك البلدة، فإنَّ الإمام إذا فتح بلدة يجعل لكل واحد من الغانمين ناحية، ويجعلها له، ويجعل لها علامة، ويختط عليها خطاً ليعلم أنه قد اختارها، ومنه سميت خطط البصرة الكوفة ، وهو جمع. بالكسر، وهذا عندهما. وعند أبي يوسف : في هذه الصورة أيضاً الباقي بعد الخمس للواجد. كذا في ، وذكر في «السراج»: إن الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف ، وذكر في «المعراج»: إنَّ محل الخلافِ ما إذا لم يدعه مالك الأرض، فإن ادعى فالقولُ له اتفاقاً. (٤) قوله : فللمختط له ؛ أي إن كان حيّاً ، ولوارثِهِ إن وجد، فإن لم يعرفوا يوضع في بيت المال. كذا في «الفتح» [ 0 ] قوله : وركاز ؛ أعم من أن يكون كنزاً أو معدناً.
[٦]قوله : لمستأمن ؛ أي من دخل دارهم بأمان، وكذا لو دخل دارهم بدون أمان فوجده بخلاف ما إذا وجده في دارِ مملوكة لهم، فإنّه يردّه إلى مالكها إن كان مستأمنا.
And what has the mark of disbelief: khums, and the rest is for the finder if his land is not owned, otherwise it is for the one who was allotted (al-mukhtatt) that land. And rikaz in the desert of dar al-harb is entirely for the musta'min who found it. [1] His saying: 'mark of disbelief' (simat al-kufr) like the engraving of an idol or the name of one of their kings or other things by which it is known that a disbeliever placed it. (2) His saying: 'khums'; whether it is in his land or someone else's land or ownerless land, because the treasure is not part of the land, so it is possible to impose khums on it, unlike minerals. [3] His saying: 'otherwise' (illa); meaning if the land in which it was found is owned by someone, then it is for the one who was allotted (mukhtatt) that land, i.e., the one to whom the Imam gave that plot on the day of the conquest of that town. For when the Imam conquers a town, he assigns to each of the warriors a district, makes it his, places a marker, and draws a line (yukhtattu) to show that he has chosen it. From this come the 'khitat' (plans) of Basra and Kufa. This is according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf, in this scenario also the remainder after khums is for the finder. It is mentioned in al-Siraj that the fatwa is on the saying of Abu Yusuf, and in al-Mi'raj that the locus of disagreement is when the landowner does not claim it; if he claims, the saying is his (the landowner's) by agreement. (4) His saying: 'for the one allotted' (li-l-mukhtatt lahu); meaning if he is alive, and to his heir if found; if they are not known, it is placed in the public treasury. As in al-Fath. [5] His saying: 'rikaz' is more general, whether treasure or mineral. [6] His saying: 'for the musta'min' meaning one who entered their land with aman (safe conduct). Similarly, if he entered without aman and found it, unlike if he found it in owned land of theirs, then he returns it to its owner if he is musta'min.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the commentary on Al-Hidayah regarding treasures identified as having a 'mark of disbelief' (simat al-kufr). The matn states: such a treasure attracts khums (one-fifth), and the remaining four-fifths go to the finder if the land where it was found is not owned by anyone (i.e., ownerless). If the land is owned (e.g., from the initial conquest distribution), the rest goes to the original grantee of that land (al-mukhtatt lahu). However, an exception is made for rikaz found in the desert of dar al-harb (enemy territory) by a musta'min (person with safe conduct): the entire rikaz goes to him. The commentator explains: 'mark of disbelief' includes idols, names of kings, etc. The khums is due regardless of land ownership because the treasure is not part of the land itself, unlike minerals which are considered part of the land. The term 'illa' (otherwise) triggers the rule: if the land is owned, the treasure minus khums goes to the one who originally received that plot from the Imam at the time of conquest (the mukhtatt). This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf, however, holds that even in owned land, the balance after khums goes to the finder — and this is the relied-upon fatwa according to al-Siraj. The disagreement only applies if the landowner does not claim the treasure; if he does, his word is accepted by consensus. The mukhtatt, if alive, takes it; if dead, his heir; if unknown, it goes to the treasury. The term 'rikaz' here is broader than treasure, including minerals. For a musta'min in dar al-harb desert, the whole rikaz is his, whether he entered with aman or not, but if found in owned property of the enemy, it must be returned to the owner.

Key Terms
سمة الكفر (simat al-kufr): A mark or sign indicating the treasure was buried by disbelievers, such as an idol or king's name.
الخمس (al-khums): One-fifth share, obligatory on certain gains including war spoils and treasures with marks of disbelief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum requirement for a treasure to be subject to khums according to the Hanafi school?
A) It must be buried deep in the ground.
B) It must be found in ownerless land.
C) It must have a mark of disbelief (simat al-kufr).
D) It must be worth more than 200 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
Khums is wajib on any treasure bearing a clear mark of disbelief, regardless of land ownership, by analogy to ghanima.

Distribution of Treasure Remainder: Finder, Mukhtatt, and Musta'min
Distribution rules for remainder after khums based on land ownership and finder's status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine who is entitled to the remainder of a khums-eligible treasure based on land ownership and the legal status of the finder, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute and relied-upon fatwa.

Core Idea
After khums, the remainder goes to the finder in ownerless land, but to the land grantee in conquered land; however, the fatwa awards it to the finder even in owned land.

Once khums is paid on a treasure with a mark of disbelief, the remaining four-fifths must be distributed. This distribution hinges critically on whether the land is owned or ownerless, and if owned, to whom it was originally granted. The passage also covers a special rule for treasures found in dar al-harb by a musta'min.

Guided Path
1
Classify the land where the treasure was found
Determine if the land is ownerless (mubah), owned by the finder, owned by someone else, or part of dar al-harb. This classification dictates the next steps.
Ownerless land includes deserts, mountains, etc. Owned land includes conquered lands divided by the Imam.
2
Apply the basic rule for ownerless land
If the land is ownerless, the remainder after khums goes to the finder. This is the default ruling.
No dispute here.
3
Apply the rule for owned land: the two schools
If the land is owned (e.g., a plot granted to a warrior during conquest), the original ruling of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is that the remainder goes to the original grantee (al-mukhtatt). However, Abu Yusuf later held that the finder gets it, and this is the fatwa.
The mukhtatt is the person allocated that plot by the Imam; if he dies, his heir; if unknown, treasury.
4
Apply the exception for dar al-harb
If a musta'min (person with safe conduct) finds a treasure in the desert of dar al-harb, he gets the entire treasure, not just the remainder after khums. This includes both treasure and minerals.
If the musta'min finds it in owned land of dar al-harb, he must return it to the owner.
5
Note the consensus clause
If the landowner himself claims the treasure, his word is accepted by agreement, and the finder/mukhtatt does not get it.
This consensus applies only when the landowner makes a claim.

Key Terms
المختط له (al-mukhtatt lahu): The person to whom the Imam granted a specific plot of land during the conquest, marked by a line (khatt).
المستأمن (al-musta'min): A person from dar al-harb who enters Muslim lands with a safe conduct (aman), or vice versa.
بيت المال (bayt al-mal): The public treasury of the Muslim state.

In owned land, the fatwa gives the remainder after khums to the finder, overriding the original ruling for the mukhtatt, unless the landowner claims it.

Ruling on Treasure with Mark of Kufr
Explains the khums and ownership of treasure with pagan symbols.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on khums for treasure with a mark of kufr and identify who receives the remainder in different land-ownership scenarios, including the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Treasure with a disbeliever's mark: khums wajib; remainder to finder by default, but landowner's claim overrides.

This passage from Al-Wiqayah explains a specific category of treasure: that which bears a visible sign of having been deposited by a disbeliever (simat al-kufr). The ruling differs from ordinary buried treasure, as khums (one-fifth) is wajib, and the ownership of the remaining four-fifths depends on the status of the land. A nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute further determines the recipient, which the commentator clarifies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the trigger
Recognise that the act is finding treasure (kanz) with a mark indicating it was placed by a disbeliever. This triggers a different ruling than ordinary treasure.
Examples of marks: idol engraving, name of a non-Muslim king.
2
State the primary ruling
Khums (one-fifth) is wajib on such treasure, regardless of where it is found (own land, another's land, or ownerless land). The remainder is for the finder if the land is not owned.
Contrast with a mine: no khums on a mine because it is part of the land.
3
Identify the condition when land is owned
If the treasure is found in owned land (someone's property), the remainder after khums goes to the original grantee (mukhtatt) according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This is because the land is his property.
Grantee: the person to whom the Imam allocated the land at conquest.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that the remainder always goes to the finder, provided the landowner does not claim it. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Yusuf's view, as per al-Sarraj.
The locus of disagreement: only when the landowner does not claim the treasure; if he claims, all agree it is his.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Take a concrete case: a coin with a cross is found in a public park (ownerless land). Khums is wajib; the finder keeps the remainder. If found in a friend's garden and the friend does not claim it, the finder still keeps the remainder according to the mufta bihi.
If the friend claims it, it goes to the friend by agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما فيه سمةِ الكفرِ خُمسٌ، وباقيه للواجد إن لم تُمْلَك أرضُهُ، وإلا فللمختط له. قوله: سمة الكفر؛ كنقش صنم أو اسم ملك من ملوكهم أو غير ذلك مما يعرفُ به أنه وضعه كافر. قوله: خُمس؛ سواء كان في أرضه أو أرض غيره أو أرض مباحة؛ لأنَّ الكنز ليس من أجزاء الدار فأمكن إيجاب الخمس فيه بخلاف المعدن. قوله: وإلا؛ أي وإن كانت الأرض التي وجد فيها مملوكة لأحد فهو للذي اختَطَّ له، وهو الذي ملكه الإمام هذه البقعة يوم فتح تلك البلدة، فإنَّ الإمام إذا فتح بلدة يجعل لكل واحد من الغانمين ناحية، ويجعلها له، ويجعل لها علامة، ويختط عليها خطاً ليعلم أنه قد اختارها، ومنه سميت خطط البصرة والكوفة، وهو جمع. بالكسر، وهذا عندهما. وعند أبي يوسف: في هذه الصورة أيضاً الباقي بعد الخمس للواجد. كذا في، وذكر في «السراج»: إن الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف، وذكر في «المعراج»: إنَّ محل الخلافِ ما إذا لم يدعه مالك الأرض، فإن ادعى فالقولُ له اتفاقاً. قوله: فللمختط له؛ أي إن كان حيّاً، ولوارثِهِ إن وجد، فإن لم يعرفوا يوضع في بيت المال.
And that which bears the mark of disbelief: one-fifth, and the rest is for the finder if its land is not owned, otherwise it is for the one who was allocated the land. [Explanation:] His saying: 'mark of disbelief' — such as the engraving of an idol or the name of a king from their kings or other than that by which it is known that a disbeliever placed it. His saying: 'one-fifth' — whether it is in his land or the land of another or ownerless land; because the treasure is not part of the land, so it is possible to impose khums on it, contrary to a mine. His saying: 'otherwise' — i.e., if the land in which it was found is owned by someone, then it is for the one who was allocated that land, and he is the one whom the Imam made owner of this plot on the day of the conquest of that town. Indeed, when the Imam conquers a town, he assigns to each of the fighters a district, makes it his, places a mark on it, and draws a line on it to indicate that he has chosen it, and from this the plans of Basra and Kufa are named — it is a plural with kasrah. This is according to them both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf: in this scenario also the remainder after khums is for the finder. Thus it is mentioned, and it is mentioned in 'al-Siraj': the fatwa is according to the view of Abu Yusuf. And it is mentioned in 'al-Mi'raj': the locus of disagreement is when the owner of the land does not claim it; if he claims it, then the statement is his by agreement. His saying: 'for the one who was allocated the land' — i.e., if he is alive, and to his heir if found, and if they are not known, it is placed in the public treasury.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Wiqayah, here parsed by the commentator. It addresses treasure (kanz) that bears a clear sign of having been deposited by a disbeliever — such as an idol carving or the name of a non-Muslim king. The ruling is that one-fifth (khums) must be given from such treasure, and the remainder goes to the finder if the land where it was found is not privately owned (i.e., it is ownerless or the finder's own land). However, if the land is owned by someone else, the remainder after khums goes to the person who originally received that land as a grant (ikhtitāt) from the Imam at the time of the Islamic conquest. The commentator clarifies that the khums is obligatory regardless of where the treasure is found (own land, another's land, or ownerless land) because the treasure is not part of the land, unlike a mine. The commentator also notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the remainder goes to the original grantee (mukhtatt), while Abu Yusuf holds that the remainder goes to the finder even in owned land, provided the landowner does not claim it. The relied-upon position for fatwa (as per al-Sarraj) is Abu Yusuf's view. If the landowner does claim it, then by agreement the treasure belongs to him. If the grantee or his heir is unknown, the remainder is kept in the public treasury (bayt al-mal).

Key Terms
سمة الكفر (simat al-kufr): A mark or sign indicating the treasure was deposited by a disbeliever, such as an idol engraving or a king's name.
المختط له (al-mukhtatt lahu): The person to whom the Imam grants a specific plot of land in a conquered territory, marked by lines (khatt).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi), if treasure bearing a mark of kufr is found in land owned by another person and the owner does not claim it, who gets the remainder after khums?
A) The finder
B) The grantee (mukhtatt)
C) The public treasury (bayt al-mal)
D) The Imam

Key Takeaway
Treasure with a clear mark of kufr incurs khums; the remainder goes to the finder by the default fatwa, provided the landowner does not claim it.

Rikaz Found by a Musta'min in Dar al-Harb
Ruling for a musta'min finding treasure in enemy territory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rikaz found by a musta'min in Dar al-Harb and identify the conditions that determine whether khums applies.

Core Idea
Rikaz in the desert of Dar al-Harb belongs entirely to the musta'min finder, without khums.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: a Muslim merchant enters enemy territory with a safe-conduct (aman) and discovers buried treasure or minerals in the desert. The ruling distinguishes between desert and owned property, and whether the finder is a musta'min or a harbi. The commentary also clarifies an internal debate about the correct reading of the matn regarding khums for goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the finding scenario
Determine the location of the find (desert vs. owned house) and the status of the finder (musta'min vs. harbi).
The ruling changes based on these two variables.
2
Apply the primary rule
For desert rikaz found by a musta'min, the finder keeps all. For rikaz found in an owned house, return to owner.
The desert is not owned, so taking is not treachery.
3
Consider the finder's status without aman
If the finder is not a musta'min (i.e., entered without aman), the entire rikaz is his regardless of location.
This applies to a harbi who enters without permission.
4
Analyze the khums debate
Some early readings suggested khums for goods found in ownerless land, but later scholars rejected this because khums only applies to booty gained through conquest.
The musta'min is not a conqueror, so no khums.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position: no khums; the musta'min keeps all rikaz found in the desert of Dar al-Harb.
This is supported by al-Hidayah, al-Durr, and later fatwa works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وركاز صحراء دار الحرب كله لمستأمن وَجَدَه. قوله: وركاز؛ أعم من أن يكون كنزاً أو معدناً. قوله: لمستأمن؛ أي من دخل دارهم بأمان، وكذا لو دخل دارهم بدون أمان فوجده بخلاف ما إذا وجده في دار مملوكة لهم، فإنّه يردّه إلى مالكها إن كان مستأمناً، وإن وجده في دار منها رُدَّ إلى مالكها، وإن وُجِدَ ركاز متاعهم في أرض منها لم تُمْلَك خُمس وباقيه له. أي إذا دخل تاجرنا دار الحرب بأمان، فوجد في صحرائها ركازاً، فكله له، وإن وجده في دار منها رُدَّ إلى مالكها. وإن وُجِدَ ركاز متاعهم في أرض منها لم تُمْلَك خُمس وباقيه له. وإن لم يكن مستأمناً، فالكل له؛ وذلك لأنَّ صحراءهم ليست مملوكة لأحد، فلا يعد أخذه غدراً ولا كذلك الدارُ المملوكة. قوله: خمس؛ قال الشارح الهروي: فيه بحث؛ فإنَّ وجوب الخمس بعد أن يثبت الانتقال من أيدي الكفرة إلى أيدي المسلمين بطريق القهر والغلبة حقيقة أو حكماً. كما في «النهاية»، و«الكافي»، وغيره. وركاز دار الحرب متاعاً كان أو نقداً كله للواجد المستأمن إن وجد في الصحراء، وغاية التوجيه أن يقال: هذه المسألة من تتمّة قوله: وما فيه سمة الكفر خمس»، وهذا القول وإن كان أعم من النقدين والمتاع، لكن ذكر هذه المسألة دفعاً لتوهّم أنّ هذا القول مختص بالنقدين كما في الزكاة؛ فإنّها لا تجب في متاع لغير التجارة، فتقرير للمسألة على هذا: إن وجد في دار الإسلام ركاز متاعهم في أرض مباحةٍ خُمس. انتهى. وفي «الدر» بعد ذكر ما في المتن: هذا غير صحيح، لما صرح به شراح «الهداية» وغيرهم: أنّ الخمس إنّما يجب فيما يكون في معنى الغنيمة، وهو في ما يكون في يد دار الحرب، ووقع في أيدي المسلمين بإيجاف الخيل، والمذكور في «الوقاية» ليس كذلك؛ لأن المستأمن كالمتلصص، والأرض من دار الحرب لم تقع في أيدي المسلمين. فالصواب أن يقطع لفظ: «وجد» عمّا قبله ويقرأ على البناء للمفعول، ويترك لفظ: «منها»، وتضاف الأرض إلى المسلمين. انتهى. وفي «الشرنبلالية»: «وجد» مبني للمفعول ونائب فاعله المحذوف: أي ذو منعة لا المستأمن، والتقييد بقوله: «لم تُمْلَك»، يعلم منه المملوكة بالطريق الأولى.
And the rikaz of the desert of Dar al-Harb is entirely for the musta'min who found it. His saying: 'and rikaz' — more general than being a treasure or a mine. His saying: 'for a musta'min' — i.e., one who entered their land with aman, and similarly if he entered their land without aman and found it, contrary to if he found it in a house owned by them, then he returns it to its owner if he is a musta'min. And if he found it in a house of theirs, it is returned to its owner. And if the rikaz of their goods is found in a land of theirs that is not owned, one-fifth and the rest is for him — i.e., if our merchant entered Dar al-Harb with aman and found rikaz in its desert, it is all for him; and if he found it in a house of theirs, it is returned to its owner. And if the rikaz of their goods is found in a land of theirs that is not owned, one-fifth and the rest is for him. And if he is not a musta'min (i.e., entered without aman), then it is all for him; because their desert is not owned by anyone, so taking it is not considered treachery, unlike the owned house. His saying: 'one-fifth' — al-Sharih al-Harawi said: There is discussion in it; indeed, the obligation of khums is after it is established that the transfer from the hands of disbelievers to the hands of Muslims occurs by way of overpowering and domination, actually or legally. As in al-Nihayah, al-Kafi, etc. And the rikaz of Dar al-Harb, whether goods or cash, is entirely for the musta'min finder if found in the desert. The ultimate explanation is to say: This issue is a continuation of his saying: 'And that which bears the mark of disbelief: one-fifth'; and this statement, although it is general for both cash and goods, the mention of this issue is to prevent the misconception that this statement is specific to cash as in zakat; indeed, zakat is not obligatory on goods not for trade. So the reformulation of the issue on this basis: If he found in Dar al-Islam the rikaz of their goods in ownerless land, one-fifth. End. And in al-Durr after mentioning what is in the matn: This is not correct, because what the commentators of al-Hidayah and others have clarified: that khums is only obligatory on what is in the meaning of booty, and that is what was in the hands of Dar al-Harb and fell into the hands of Muslims by forcibly urging horses (i.e., conquest). What is mentioned in al-Wiqayah is not like that, because the musta'min is like a thief, and the land of Dar al-Harb did not fall into the hands of Muslims. So the correct [reading] is to separate the word 'found' from what precedes it and read it in the passive voice, and leave the word 'from it', and add the land to the Muslims. End. And in al-Shurnubaliyya: 'found' is passive, and its agent omitted, i.e., a person of power, not the musta'min, and the restriction by saying 'not owned' implies the owned by primary consideration.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling for rikaz (treasure or minerals) found in the desert of Dar al-Harb by a musta'min (a person who enters with a safe passage). The matn states that such rikaz is entirely for the musta'min who found it. The commentator clarifies that 'rikaz' includes both buried treasure and minerals. If the musta'min finds it in an owned house, he must return it to the owner to avoid treachery (ghadr). However, if he enters without aman (as a harbi), he gets everything regardless. The commentator also discusses a variant interpretation: if the rikaz is goods (not cash) found in ownerless land in Dar al-Harb, some readings impose khums (one-fifth). This leads to a debate: the correct position per al-Hidayah commentators is that khums only applies to booty gained through conquest (ijaf al-khayl), not to what a musta'min finds (as he is like a sneak). Therefore, the matn should be read differently: 'found' in passive, referring to a Muslim who conquers, not a musta'min. The relied-upon view is that khums is not obligatory here; the finder gets all. The passage demonstrates the careful textual criticism of the Hanafi scholars to preserve correct rulings.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta'min): A person from Dar al-Harb who enters Dar al-Islam (or a Muslim who enters Dar al-Harb) with a safe-conduct (aman).
ركاز (rikaz): Buried treasure or mineral deposits found in the ground. Includes both kanz and ma'din.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a musta'min who finds rikaz in an owned house in Dar al-Harb?
A) He keeps it all because it is Dar al-Harb.
B) He must give khums and keep the rest.
C) He must return it to the owner of the house.
D) He must give it to the Imam.

Key Takeaway
Rikaz found in the desert of Dar al-Harb by a musta'min belongs entirely to the finder, with no khums, because it is not booty from conquest.

Rikaz for a Musta'min in Dar al-Harb: Is Khums Required?
Discussion of rikaz rulings for a musta'min in Dar al-Harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rikaz found by a musta'min in unconquered Dar al-Harb and explain why the mufta bihi view rejects khums.

Core Idea
Rikaz from unconquered Dar al-Harb belongs entirely to the musta'min; khums only applies to conquered land.

Finding buried treasure in enemy territory raises questions of ownership and obligation. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on rikaz found by a musta'min (a protected traveller) in Dar al-Harb, clarifying a significant intra-madhhab dispute over the payment of khums.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal category and ruling of a musta'min finding rikaz in the desert of unconquered Dar al-Harb.
The act is mubah, and ownership is established for the finder.
2
Distinguish between desert and house
Note the difference: in the desert, the rikaz is all his; in a house, it must be returned to the owner.
Desert is ownerless; a house is privately owned.
3
Analyze the dispute over khums
Examine the conflicting views: some texts appear to require khums, but later commentators argue it is only due on conquered land.
The key issue is whether the land has been taken by force (qahr wa ghalaba).
4
Identify the mufta bihi position
Conclude that the relied-upon view is no khums, based on the reasoning of al-Harawi, al-Durr, and others.
This aligns with the principle that khums is akin to booty, requiring conquest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة باب الركاز
وإن وجده في دار منها رُدَّ إلى مالكها، وإن وُجِدَ ركاز متاعِهم في أرض منها لم تُمْلَكُ خُمس وباقيه له ... أي إذا دخل تاجرنا دار الحرب بأمان، فوجد في صحرائها ركازاً، فكله له، (وإن وجده في دار منها رُدَّ إلى مالكها). وإن وُجِدَ ركاز متاعهم في أرض منها لم تُمْلكُ خُمس وباقيه له). وإن لم يكن مستأمناً، فالكل له؛ وذلك لأنَّ صحراء هم مملوكة لأحد، فلا يعد أخذه غدراً ولا كذلك الدّارُ المملوكة. كذا في «غاية البيان»، وغيره.
[١] قوله: خمس؛ قال الشارح الهروي: فيه بحث؛ فإنّ وجوب الخمس بعد أن يثبت الانتقال من أيدي الكفرة إلى أيدي المسلمين بطريق القهر والغلبة حقيقة أو حكماً. كما في «النهاية»، و«الكافي»، وغيره.
وركاز دار الحرب متاعاً كان أو نقداً كله للواجد المستأمن إن وجد في الصحراء، وغاية التوجيه أن يقال: هذه المسألة من تتمّة قوله: وما فيه سمة الكفر خمس»، وهذا القول وإن كان أعم من النقدين والمتاع، لكن ذكر هذه المسألة دفعاً لتوهّم أنّ هذا القول مختص بالنقدين كما في الزكاة؛ فإنّها لا تجب في متاع لغير التجارة، فتقرير للمسألة على هذا: إن وجد في دار الإسلام ركاز متاعهم في أرض مباحةٍ خُمس. انتهى.
وفي «الدر» بعد ذكر ما في المتن: هذا غير صحيح، لما صرح به شراح «الهداية» وغيرهم: أنّ الخمس إنّما يجب فيما يكون في معنى الغنيمة، وهو في ما يكون في يد دار الحرب، ووقع في أيدي المسلمين بإيجاف الخيل، والمذكور في «الوقاية» ليس كذلك؛ لأن المستأمن كالمتلصص، والأرض من دار الحرب لم تقع في أيدي المسلمين. فالصواب أن يقطع لفظ: «وجد» عمّا قبله ويقرأ على البناء للمفعول، ويترك لفظ: «منها»، وتضاف الأرض إلى المسلمين. انتهى. وفي «الشرنبلالية»: «وجد» مبني للمفعول ونائب فاعله المحذوف: أي ذو منعة لا المستأمن، والتقييد بقوله: «لم تملك»، يعلم منه المملوكة بالطريق الأولى.
(۱) وكذا إن لم يدخلها بأمان، وإنما كان له لسبق يده على مال مباح، ولم يجب الخمس؛ لأنه أخذه متلصصا غير مجاهر. ينظر: درر الحكام (۱: ١٨٥).
(۲) حذراً عن الغدر والخيانة، ولم يرده وأخرجه إلى دارنا ملكه ملكاً خبيثاً. ينظر: «الدر المنتقى» (١: ٢١٤).
(۳) «الشرنبلالية» (١: ١٨٦).
The Book of Zakat, Chapter of Rikaz. If he finds it in a house from among them, it is returned to its owner. And if the rikaz of their goods is found in a land from among them that was not conquered, one-fifth (is due) and the rest is for him... That is, if our merchant enters Dar al-Harb with aman and finds rikaz in its desert, it is all for him. (And if he finds it in a house from among them, it is returned to its owner). And if the rikaz of their goods is found in a land from among them that was not conquered, one-fifth and the rest is for him. And if he is not a musta'min, then all is for him; because their desert is not owned by anyone, so taking it is not considered treachery, unlike the owned house. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan and others. [1] His saying: one-fifth; al-Harawi commentator said: There is discussion in it; for the obligation of one-fifth is after the transfer from the hands of the disbelievers to the hands of Muslims by way of overpowering and domination, actually or legally. As in al-Nihaya and al-Kafi and others. And the rikaz of Dar al-Harb, whether goods or cash, is all for the musta'min finder if found in the desert. The ultimate direction is to say: This issue is a completion of his saying: 'And what has the mark of disbelief, one-fifth.' And this statement, although general for both coins and goods, but mentioning this issue is to repel the misunderstanding that this statement is specific to coins as in zakat, for zakat is not obligatory on goods not for trade. So the statement of the issue is thus: If he finds in Dar al-Islam rikaz of their goods in an ownerless land, one-fifth. End. And in al-Durr after mentioning what is in the text: This is incorrect, as clarified by the commentators of al-Hidayah and others: that one-fifth is only obligatory on what is in the meaning of booty, which is what is in the hands of Dar al-Harb and falls into the hands of Muslims by urging horses. And what is mentioned in al-Wiqayah is not like that; because the musta'min is like a robber, and the land of Dar al-Harb has not fallen into the hands of Muslims. So the correct view is to separate the word 'found' from what precedes it and read it in the passive voice, and drop the word 'from among them', and add the land to the Muslims. End. And in al-Shurunbulaliyya: 'Found' is passive, and its agent is omitted: meaning a person of strength, not the musta'min, and the restriction by his saying 'not conquered' indicates the conquered land by primary inference. (1) Similarly if he did not enter with aman, and it is his due to prior possession of permissible wealth, and one-fifth is not obligatory; because he took it as a robber not openly. See: Durar al-Hukkam (1:185). (2) To avoid treachery and betrayal, and he did not return it and took it out to our land, he owns it as a vile ownership. See: al-Durr al-Muntaqa (1:214). (3) al-Shurunbulaliyya (1:186).
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on rikaz (treasure trove) found by a musta'min (a person granted aman/safe conduct) in Dar al-Harb. It begins by stating the basic ruling: if a musta'min finds rikaz in the desert of Dar al-Harb, it is all his; if he finds it in a house, he must return it to the owner. If he is not a musta'min (i.e., a combatant), then all is his regardless of location. The reasoning is that the desert is not owned, so taking it is not treachery, whereas a house is owned. The passage then engages in a critical refinement of the statement that khums (one-fifth) is due on such rikaz. The commentator (al-Harawi) notes that khums is only obligatory when wealth transfers from disbelievers to Muslims by conquest (qahr wa ghalaba). Since the land of Dar al-Harb has not been conquered, no khums is due. The author of al-Durr further clarifies that the correct understanding is to read the word 'found' as passive ('is found') referring to a powerful finder (dhu man'a) not the musta'min, and to drop 'from among them', thus applying the khums ruling only to conquered land. The passage concludes with a reference from al-Shurunbulaliyya supporting this reading. Thus, for a musta'min, the rikaz in unconquered land of Dar al-Harb is entirely his, without khums, because it is akin to a robber's gain, not booty.

Key Terms
ركاز (rikaz): Treasure trove or buried wealth, specifically wealth of disbelievers found in land.
مستأمن (musta'min): A person from Dar al-Harb who enters Muslim lands with aman (safe conduct), or a Muslim who enters Dar al-Harb with aman.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Land under non-Muslim rule where the laws of Islam are not applied.
خمس (khums): One-fifth, the share due on rikaz and booty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in this passage, what is the ruling on rikaz found by a musta'min in the desert of unconquered Dar al-Harb?
A) He must pay khums and keep the rest.
B) He must return it to the owner.
C) He keeps all of it, no khums due.
D) He must give it to the Muslim ruler.

Key Takeaway
For a musta'min in unconquered Dar al-Harb, rikaz is his entirely without khums, as khums only applies to conquered land.
