Zakat on Honey and Mountain Fruits: Ushr Obligation and Conditions
Ruling statement with conditions and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ushr (zakat) for honey and mountain fruits, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding nisab, and apply the condition of himāya (Imam's protection).

Core Idea
Honey and mountain fruits from non-kharaj land are subject to ushr even in small amounts, overriding qiyas.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh commentary opens the chapter on zakat of produce (zakat al-kharij). It establishes that honey and fruits from mountains are wajib for ushr, based on hadith evidence. The author clarifies key conditions: the land must be non-kharaj, and mountain fruits require the Imam's protection (himāya). There is also an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the nisab for honey.

Guided Path
1
Identify items subject to ushr
From the matn, note that honey, mountain fruits, and all produce from non-kharaj land are subject to ushr.
The phrase 'wa ma kharaja min al-ard' is general.
2
Understand the no-nisab rule for honey
The ruling is that ushr is taken from honey even if little, based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) taking ushr from honey. This overrides qiyas.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud, etc.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf reportedly held that ushr on honey is due only if its value reaches ten wasq. Qiyas would suggest no ushr at all, but the hadith is preferred.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.
4
Recognize the condition of himāya for mountain fruits
For mountain fruits, ushr is conditional on the Imam protecting the area from enemies and robbers. Without protection, the fruit is mubah and no ushr is due.
This is like game; collection is by protection.
5
Connect irrigation method to ushr rate
If irrigated by sayh (flowing water) or rain, the full ushr (10%) is due. Artificial irrigation reduces it to half ushr (5%).
This is a separate ruling, but the passage mentions sayh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة الخارج
في عَسَلِ أرض عشرية أو جبل، وثمره، وما خَرَجَ من الأرض، وإن لم يبلغ خمسة أوسق، ولم يبق سنة، وسقاه سَيْح، أو مطر عُشر
[١]قوله: في عسل؛ في إطلاقه إشارة إلى أنّه يؤخذ منه العشر، وإن قل، وفي رواية عنه، وهو قول أبي يوسف: إنه لا يؤخذ منه إلا إذا بلغت قيمة عشرة أوسق، والقياس: أن لا يؤخذ منه العشر مطلقاً، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف له؛ لأنه متولد من الحيوان لا من الأرض، فصار كالإبريسم إلا أنه تركنا ذلك لما ثبت في «سنن أبي داود والنسائي» و «جامع الترمذي» و «معجم الطبراني» وغيره: «أنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أخذ منه العشر وأمر به». [٢]قوله: عشرية أو جبل؛ الأخصر أن يقول: أرض غير خراجية؛ فإنّ المانع من وجوب العشر كون الأرض خراجية؛ لأنه لا يجتمع العشر والخراج فيشمل العشرية، وما ليست عشرية ولا خراجية كالجبل والمفاوز. [٣]قوله: وثمره؛ عطف على عسل، وضميره راجع إلى الجبل وما يليه أيضاً، عطف على عسل، ثم وجوب العشر في العسل وثمر الجبل مشروط بما إذا حماه الإمام؛ أي من أهل الحرب والبغاة وقطاع الطريق لا عن كلّ أحد، فإن ثمر الجبال مباح لا يمنعُ، فإنّ الجباية بالحماية، فإن لم يحمه، فلا، فإنّه كالصيد. كذا في «الدر المختار»، وحواشيه. [٤]قوله: سيح؛ بفتح السين المهملة، يقال: ساح الماء سيحاً: إذا جرى على وجه الأرض، والمراد به ماء الأنهار والأودية.
(1) أي ثمر الجبال. ينظر: شرح ابن ملك (ق٥٧ /ب). (۲) فعن أبي سيارة المتقي، قال: قلت: يا رسول الله إن لي نحلاً، قال: أد العشر، يا رسول الله احمها لي فحماها لي» في «سنن ابن ماجة (١: ٥٨٤)، و «مصنف ابن أبي شيبة (۲: ۳۷۳)، و «مسند أحمد (٤: ٢٦٣)، وغيرها. (۳) «رد المحتار على الدر المختار (۲: ۲۳٥-۲۳٦).
Chapter of Zakat of Produce. On honey from 'ushr land or a mountain, and its fruit, and what comes out of the earth, even if it does not reach five wasq, and does not remain for a year, and is irrigated by flowing water or rain: one-tenth. [1] His saying: on honey; in its generality is an indication that one-tenth is taken from it, even if little. And in one narration from him, which is the saying of Abu Yusuf: that it is not taken from it unless its value reaches ten wasq. And the analogy (qiyas) is that one-tenth is not taken from it at all, and that is a narration from Abu Yusuf from him; because it is produced from animals, not from the earth, so it is like silk. But we abandoned that due to what is established in the Sunan of Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Jami' al-Tirmidhi, Mu'jam al-Tabarani and others: 'That the Prophet (peace be upon him) took one-tenth from it and commanded it.' [2] His saying: 'ushr land or a mountain; the shortest way is to say: non-kharaj land; for the preventing factor for the obligation of ushr is that the land is kharaj land, because ushr and kharaj do not combine. So it includes 'ushr land, and what is neither 'ushr nor kharaj like the mountain and deserts. [3] His saying: and its fruit; is conjuncted to honey, and its pronoun refers to the mountain and what follows it, also conjuncted to honey. Then the obligation of ushr on honey and fruit of the mountain is conditional on the Imam protecting it; i.e., from the people of war, rebels, and highway robbers, not from everyone. For the fruit of mountains is permissible (mubah) and is not prevented. Indeed, collection is by protection. If he does not protect it, then no (ushr is due), for it is like game. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its glosses. [4] His saying: flowing water (sayh); with the fath of the sin, it is said: water flows (sāha) if it runs on the surface of the earth, and by it is meant water of rivers and valleys. (1) That is, fruit of the mountains. See: Sharh Ibn Malik (fol. 57b). (2) From Abu Sayyarah al-Muttaqi, he said: I said: O Messenger of Allah, I have bees. He said: Pay the ushr. O Messenger of Allah, protect them for me. So he protected them for me. In Sunan Ibn Majah (1:584), Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah (2:373), Musnad Ahmad (4:263), and others. (3) Radd al-Muhtar ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar (2:235-236).
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that opens the chapter on zakat of produce (zakat al-kharij) in a Hanafi fiqh commentary. It defines the items subject to 'ushr (one-tenth zakat): honey from 'ushr land or mountains, fruits of mountains, and all produce from the earth, without requiring a nisab of five wasq or a year's holding. The commentary then expands on each element. First, honey: the general ruling is that ushr is due even on small amounts, based on hadith evidence (the Prophet took ushr from honey). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf reportedly held that ushr on honey requires its value to reach ten wasq, and qiyas would suggest no ushr at all since honey is from animals, but the hadith overrides qiyas via istihsan. Second, the land type: 'ushr land or mountain is used, but the commentator simplifies to 'non-kharaj land' because kharaj land cannot have both ushr and kharaj. Thus, mountain and desert, being neither 'ushr nor kharaj, are included. Third, fruits of mountains: the pronoun in 'thamarahu' (its fruit) refers to the mountain. The obligation of ushr on mountain fruits is conditional upon the Imam's protection (himāya) of those areas from enemies and robbers; without protection, it remains mubah (free) like game, and no ushr is due. Fourth, 'sayh' (flowing water) is defined as water that flows on the surface, such as river and valley water, which determines the rate of ushr (one-tenth for natural irrigation).

Key Terms
عشر ('ushr): One-tenth (10%) zakat on agricultural produce and honey from non-kharaj land.
أرض عشرية (ard 'ushriyya): Land that is subject to 'ushr (one-tenth zakat), typically owned by Muslims or conquered peacefully.
حماية (himāya): Protection by the Imam of an area (e.g., mountain fruit) from usurpers, making it subject to 'ushr.
سيح (sayh): Flowing water on the surface, such as rivers and valleys.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the condition for the obligation of ushr on fruits of a mountain?
A) They must reach five wasq.
B) The Imam must protect the area from enemies and robbers.
C) The fruit must be from a valley.
D) The mountain must be within 'ushr land.

Key Takeaway
Ushr is wajib on honey and mountain fruits from non-kharaj land without nisab, and for mountain fruits, this depends on the Imam's protection.

Zakat on Honey: The Obligation of 'Ushr Despite Analogical Objection
States the ruling on 'ushr for honey and mountain fruits with conditions and proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'ushr for honey, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute, and explain why the Prophetic hadith overrides analogical reasoning.

Core Idea
The Prophet's taking of 'ushr from honey overrides the analogy that honey is animal produce.

This passage from the chapter on Zakat of Produce clarifies that honey from 'ushri land or a mountain is subject to 'ushr (one-tenth) regardless of quantity. The Hanafi school follows a specific hadith that overrides analogical reasoning (qiyas) which would otherwise exempt honey because it comes from an animal (the bee). The passage also highlights an intra-madhhab difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding a minimum threshold, and it sets a condition for mountain fruits: the Imam's protection from enemies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon (honey from 'ushri land or mountain) and the hukm level ('ushr is obligatory even if little, without year storage, regardless of irrigation).
The matn states 'عشر' unconditionally.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud, etc.: the Prophet took 'ushr from honey and ordered it. This is a zanni al-thubut (ahad) but qati' al-dalala (clear meaning of obligation).
The exact text: 'أنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أخذ منه العشر وأمر به'
3
Understand the qiyas objection
Analogy (qiyas) would exempt honey because it is produced from a living animal, not the earth, like silk and other animal products. The Hanafi school abandons this qiyas due to the specific sunnah.
The commentator says: 'القياس: أن لا يؤخذ منه العشر مطلقاً' but 'تركنا ذلك لما ثبت...'
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that 'ushr is due only if the value reaches ten awsuq. A narration from Abu Hanifa also supports this. However, the well-known position (Abu Hanifa) is that even a little is subject to 'ushr.
The text: 'وفي رواية عنه، وهو قول أبي يوسف: إنه لا يؤخذ منه إلا إذا بلغت قيمة عشرة أوسق'
5
Identify the condition for mountain fruits
For mountain fruits (and honey from the mountain), 'ushr is conditional upon the Imam's protection (himaya) from enemies, rebels, and highway robbers. Without protection, it is like hunting and no 'ushr is due.
The passage: 'ثم وجوب العشر في العسل وثمر الجبل مشروط بما إذا حماه الإمام'

Source Text

باب زكاة الخارج
في عسل أرض عشرية أو جبل، وثمره، وما خرج من الأرض، وإن لم يبلغ خمسة أوسق، ولم يبق سنة، وسقاه سيح أو مطر عشر
[1] قوله: في عسل؛ في إطلاقه إشارة إلى أنه يؤخذ منه العشر، وإن قل، وفي رواية عنه، وهو قول أبي يوسف: إنه لا يؤخذ منه إلا إذا بلغت قيمة عشرة أوسق، والقياس: أن لا يؤخذ منه العشر مطلقاً، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف له؛ لأنه متولد من الحيوان لا من الأرض، فصار كالإبريسم إلا أنه تركنا ذلك لما ثبت في «سنن أبي داود والنسائي و«جامع الترمذي» و«معجم الطبراني» وغيره: «أنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أخذ منه العشر وأمر به».

Chapter of Zakat of produce. On honey of 'ushri land or a mountain, and its fruit, and what comes out of the earth, even if it does not reach five awsuq, and does not remain for a year, and is watered by flowing water or rain: one-tenth. [1] His saying: 'honey' - in its unrestrictedness is an indication that one-tenth is taken from it even if little. And in a narration from him (Abu Hanifa), and it is the saying of Abu Yusuf: it is not taken from it unless its value reaches ten awsuq. And analogically, one-tenth should not be taken from it at all, and that is a narration from Abu Yusuf from him (Abu Hanifa), because it is produced from a living animal, not from the earth, so it becomes like silk, except that we abandoned that due to what is established in Sunan Abi Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Jami' al-Tirmidhi, Mu'jam al-Tabarani, etc.: 'The Prophet ﷺ took one-tenth from it and ordered it.' [2] His saying: ''ushri or a mountain' - the shortest is to say: non-kharaji land, for the preventer of the obligation of 'ushr is the land being kharaji, because 'ushr and kharaj do not combine; so it includes 'ushri land and what is neither 'ushri nor kharaji like the mountain and deserts. [3] His saying: 'and its fruit' - coordinated with honey, and its pronoun refers to the mountain and what follows it as well, coordinated with honey. Then the obligation of 'ushr on honey and fruit of the mountain is conditional upon the Imam having protected it, i.e., from people of war, rebels, and highway robbers, not from every person. For the fruit of mountains is permissible, not prevented; indeed, collection is by protection. If he does not protect it, then no, for it is like hunting. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its glosses.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Zakat of produce (Zakat al-Kharij) states the ruling regarding 'ushr (one-tenth) on honey from 'ushri land or a mountain. The matn declares that 'ushr is obligatory on honey regardless of quantity (even if it does not reach the nisab of five awsuq), regardless of time (even if it is not stored for a year), and regardless of irrigation method (flowing water or rain). The commentator explains that the unrestricted wording indicates the obligation even for a small amount. He then mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that honey must reach the value of ten awsuq for 'ushr to be due, and analogically (qiyas) one might argue no 'ushr at all because honey comes from an animal (bees), like silk, but the Hanafi school abandons this qiyas due to the specific sunnah (the Prophet took 'ushr from honey and ordered it). The passage also clarifies that the condition for 'ushr on mountain fruits is that the Imam must have protected them (from enemies and rebels); otherwise they are like hunting—no zakat is due. This combines ruling with textual proof and rational reasoning, showing the Hanafi methodology of prioritizing sunnah over qiyas.

Key Terms
عشر ('ushr): One-tenth (10%) levy on agricultural produce and honey, synonymous with zakat on produce.
أرض عشرية (ard 'ushriyya): Land on which 'ushr is levied, typically conquered peacefully and assigned to Muslims.
حماية (himaya): Protection by the Imam of mountain produce from enemies, making it subject to 'ushr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The fruit must reach five awsuq.
B) The Imam must protect it from enemies.
C) It must be stored for a year.
D) It must be irrigated manually.

Key Takeaway
Honey from 'ushri land is always subject to 'ushr due to the Prophetic sunnah, even if little, and mountain fruit requires Imam's protection.

Dispute on Nisab and Vegetables in Zakat
Discusses the nisab for agricultural produce and the exemption of vegetables.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the nisab for agricultural produce and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with its practical implications.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, no nisab for produce; for Sahibayn and Shafi'i, five awsuq threshold. Vegetables always exempt.

This passage delves into one of the key inter-madhhab disputes in zakat al-harth (agricultural produce): whether a minimum threshold (nisab) of five awsuq is required. It contrasts the position of Imam Abu Hanifa with that of his two disciples and Imam al-Shafi'i, and also confirms the exemption of vegetables. The commentary provides the textual proofs and acknowledges the strength of the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine the precise point of contention: the requirement of a nisab for agricultural produce and the zakatability of vegetables.
2
State the Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa, no nisab is required; 'ushr or half-'ushr is due on all produce. Vegetables are exempt.
This is the predominant view in the Hanafi school.
3
State the opposing position
Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i hold that no zakat is due on less than five awsuq. They also agree that vegetables are exempt.
Their evidence is the authentic hadith 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awsuq.'
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa relies on the general hadith 'In what is watered by the sky... is the tenth.' The commentator notes that the opponents' evidence is strong both rationally and textually.
Despite this, the matn follows Abu Hanifa's position.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: a farmer with 3 awsuq pays no zakat according to Sahibayn and Shafi'i, but pays according to Abu Hanifa.
Both sides agree on vegetable exemption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتب الزكاة باب الخارج [1]: عشر: مبتدأ، وقوله: في عسل أرض خبره، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له، وأما عند عندهما وعند الشَّافِعِي ليس فيما دون خمسة أوسق صدقة. والوسق ستّونَ صاعاً، والصَّاعُ ثمانية أرطال عند عندهما [كذا] وأيضاً ليس عندهم
[1] قوله: وأما عندهما... الخ، سندهم في ذلك حديث: «ليس فيما دون خمسة أوسق صدقة»، أخرجه البخاري ومسلم وغيرهما.
وله ظاهر حديث: «فيما سقت السماء والعيون أو كان عشرياً العشر، وما سقى بالنضح نصف العشر»، أخرجه البخاري؛ فإنّه بعموم لفظه دال على أنّ في كلِّ قليل وكثير صدقة، وبه استدلّ في وجوب الصدقة في الخضراوات، وزيادة تحقيق مذهبه في القدير، وغيره، وغير خاف على الفطن المتجر قوّة قولهما في الموضعين عقلا ونقلا.
[2] قوله: والوَسق؛ بفتح الواو والسين المهملة.
[3] قوله: ليس ... الخ؛ لحديث: «ليس في الخضراوات صدقة»، أخرجه الدارقطني والبزار وغيرهما بأسانيد متعدّدة أكثرها ضعيفة، كما بسطه الزَّيْلَعِي. وعند التِّرْمِذِي إِنّ معاذاً كتب إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يسأله عن الخضراوات، وهي البقول، فقال: «ليس فيها شيء». وعند الحاكم عنه: إنّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «فيما سقت السماء والسيل العشر، وفيما سقى بالنضح نصف العشر، وإنّما يكون في التمر والحنطة والحبوب فأما القثاء والبطيخ والرمان والقصب معفو عنها».
The book of Zakat, chapter of produce. [1]: 'tenth' is the subject, and his saying: 'in honey of land' is its predicate. This is according to Abu Hanifa. As for according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and according to al-Shafi'i: there is no sadaqah on less than five awsuq. And the wasq is sixty sa', and the sa' is eight ratls according to the two. And also not according to them. [1] His saying: 'As for according to the two...' etc. Their evidence in that is the hadith: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awsuq', narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, and others. And for him (Abu Hanifa) is the apparent meaning of the hadith: 'In what is watered by the sky and springs, or is 'ushri, is the tenth; and what is watered by irrigation is half a tenth', narrated by Bukhari; for its general wording indicates that on every little and much is sadaqah. And by it he argued for the obligation of sadaqah on vegetables. And further verification of his madhhab is in al-Qadir and others. And it is not hidden from the intelligent one the strength of their saying (the two) in both places rationally and by transmission. [2] His saying: 'al-wasq' - with fatha on the waw and sin. [3] His saying: 'not...' etc. Because of the hadith: 'There is no sadaqah on vegetables', narrated by al-Daraqutni and al-Bazzar and others with multiple chains, most of which are weak, as al-Zayla'i elaborated. And according to al-Tirmidhi: that Mu'adh wrote to the Messenger of Allah, asking him about vegetables, which are greens, and he said: 'There is nothing in them.' And according to al-Hakim from him: that the Messenger of Allah said: 'In what is watered by the sky and the stream is the tenth, and in what is watered by irrigation is half a tenth. But it is only on dates, wheat, and grains. As for cucumbers, melons, pomegranates, and sugarcane, they are exempt.'
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on zakat of agricultural produce, focusing on the nisab (minimum threshold) and the types of produce subject to zakat. The matn states that according to Abu Hanifa, the earlier ruling (that 'ushr is due on honey regardless of amount) stands. However, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i hold that no sadaqah (zakat) is due on less than five awsuq. The commentator explains the evidence for each side: the two and Shafi'i rely on the authentic hadith 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awsuq' (narrated by Bukhari and Muslim). Abu Hanifa relies on the general hadith 'In what is watered by the sky and springs...' (also in Bukhari) which implies zakat on all amounts. The commentator notes that Abu Hanifa's evidence is supported by its general wording, but acknowledges the strength of the opponents' position both rationally and textually (عقلا ونقلا). The passage then defines wasq (60 sa') and sa' (8 ratls). Finally, it addresses vegetables: there is no zakat on them, citing various hadiths (though some chains are weak) that explicitly exempt cucumbers, melons, pomegranates, and sugarcane. Thus, zakat on produce is only on staple grains and fruits that can be stored and measured.

Key Terms
وسق (wasq): A measure of volume equal to 60 sa' (approximately 180 kg dates/grain).
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume equal to 8 ratls (approximately 3 kg).
خضراوات (khadrawat): Vegetables, greens, including cucumbers, melons, pomegranates, sugarcane.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Nisab of five awsuq is required.
C) Nisab of ten awsuq is required.
D) Only for honey, not grains.

Key Takeaway
For Abu Hanifa, zakat on agricultural produce has no nisab; the nisab of five awsuq is the view of Sahibayn and Shafi'i. Vegetables are exempt from zakat.

The Nisab for Zakat on Produce: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Dispute regarding the minimum threshold (nisab) for zakat on agricultural produce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the nisab for zakat on agricultural produce, distinguish the proofs of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa says any quantity requires zakat; Sahibayn and Shafi'i require five wasq as nisab.

This passage from Sharh al-Wiqaya presents an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the nisab for zakat on agricultural produce. The base text discusses zakat on honey, but the dispute extends to all produce. Abu Hanifa holds that the general hadith about 'ushr applies to any amount, while his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Sahibayn), together with al-Shafi'i, require a minimum of five wasq based on a specific hadith. Understanding this dispute helps you appreciate how the Hanafi school reconciles general and specific texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and subject
Locate the word 'ushr (tithe) and its predicate 'in honey of land'. The base text is ruling on honey, but the dispute applies to all produce.
The honey example is specific, but the principle is general.
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Abu Hanifa holds that zakat is due on all agricultural produce, regardless of quantity. He relies on the general wording of the hadith about 'ushr.
3
State the opposing position (Sahibayn and Shafi'i)
Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i require a nisab of five wasq. Their proof is the hadith: 'There is no charity on less than five wasq.'
The Sahibayn here are within the Hanafi school, making this an intra-madhhab dispute.
4
Analyze the proofs
Compare the two hadiths: the general 'ushr hadith (عموم) vs. the specific nisab hadith. Abu Hanifa gives priority to the general; the Sahibayn and Shafi'i give priority to the specific.
The commentator notes قوّة قولهما (strength of their statement) indicating preference for the Sahibayn's view.
5
Identify the practical difference
Under Abu Hanifa, a farmer with a small harvest pays zakat; under the Sahibayn/Shafi'i, no zakat until the yield reaches five wasq (approx 217 kg).
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عشر : مبتدأ، وقوله : في عسل أرض خبره ، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له، وأما عند الشَّافِعِي ليس فيما دون خمسة أوسق صدقة. والوسق ستّونَ صاعاً، والصَّاعُ ثمانية أرطال عندهما. وأيضاً ليس... [١]قوله : وأما عندهما ... الخ، سندهم في ذلك حديث : «ليس فيما دون خمسة أوسق صدقة» ، أخرجه البخاري ومسلم وغيرهما. وله ظاهر حديث : «فيما سقت السماء والعيون أو كان عشرياً العشر، وما سقى بالنضح نصف العشر»، أخرجه البخاري ؛ فإنّه بعموم لفظه دال على أنّ في كلِّ قليل وكثير صدقة، وبه استدلّ في وجوب الصدقة في الخضراوات، وزيادة تحقيق مذهبه في القدير ، وغيره، وغير خاف على الفطن المتجر قوّة قولهما في الموضعين عقلا ونقلا . [٢] قوله : والوَسق ؛ بفتح الواو والسين المهملة.
Tenth: is the subject, and his statement: 'in honey of land' is its predicate, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. As for al-Shafi'i, there is no charity on less than five wasq. The wasq is sixty sa's, and the sa' is eight ratls according to them. And also not... [1] He said: 'As for according to them... etc.', their proof in that is the hadith: 'There is no charity on less than five wasq', narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim and others. And for him is the apparent hadith: 'On what is irrigated by rain and springs or is 'ushri, the tithe, and on what is irrigated by a bucket, half a tithe', narrated by al-Bukhari; for by its general wording it indicates that on every little and much there is charity, and by it one deduces the obligation of charity on vegetables, and additional verification of his madhhab in al-Qadir and others. And it is not hidden from the intelligent careful person the strength of their statement in both respects, rationally and narratively. [2] He said: 'Al-wasq': with a fatha on the waw and the important seen.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and also a disagreement with al-Shafi'i regarding the nisab (minimum threshold) for zakat on agricultural produce. The base text (matn) presents a parsing: the word 'ushr (tithe) is the subject, and 'fi 'asali ardi' (in honey of land) is the predicate, meaning the ruling concerns honey from land. According to Abu Hanifa, zakat is due on all such produce regardless of quantity. In contrast, al-Shafi'i holds that no zakat is due on less than five wasq. The commentator explains that the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) also hold the nisab condition, relying on the hadith 'There is no charity on less than five wasq.' Abu Hanifa relies on the general hadith about 'ushr and half 'ushr, which does not specify a minimum. The commentator notes that the companions' view is stronger both rationally and in transmission, implying it is the preferred position. The terms wasq (60 sa's) and sa' (8 ratls) are defined according to the companions. The mention of 'khudrawat' (vegetables) in the argument shows that Abu Hanifa used this general hadith to argue for zakat on vegetables as well.

Key Terms
الوَسق (al-wasq): A measure equal to 60 sa's, used as the nisab threshold for agricultural produce.
الصاع (al-sa'): A volume measure, here defined as 8 ratls according to the companions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Less than five wasq
B) Less than ten wasq
C) Less than one wasq
D) Less than two wasq

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on the nisab for zakat on produce, with the mufta bihi being the Sahibayn's view requiring five wasq.

Zakat on Vegetables and Perishable Crops: The Sahibayn Exemption
Exemption of vegetables from zakat with intra-Hanafi disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling on zakat for vegetables and perishable crops, IDENTIFY the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and APPLY the exceptions for firewood and sugarcane.

Core Idea
Vegetables and perishable crops are exempt from zakat; only staple grains and lasting fruits require it.

Zakat on agricultural produce is obligatory, but not all crops are subject to it. The Hanafi school, relying on hadith evidence, holds that vegetables and items that spoil within a year are exempt. However, there is an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa includes all produce, while the Sahibayn limit zakat to staple grains and fruits. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the ruling and its exceptions, clarifying the nuanced application for firewood, sugarcane, and irrigation methods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The text states that no zakat is due on vegetables (al-khudrawat) and items that do not last a year. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn).
Vegetables include fruits like apples and pears, and legumes like leeks and celery.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith 'There is no charity on vegetables' is cited, along with the explicit listing of exempt items: cucumbers, watermelons, pomegranates, and sugarcane. Note that the chains are weak but accepted by the Sahibayn.
The hadith from Mu'adh (al-Tirmidhi) says: 'There is nothing in them.'
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa held that zakat is due on all produce, including vegetables. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) exempt vegetables. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) follows the Sahibayn.
The Shafi'i school agrees with the Sahibayn on this exemption.
4
Understand the exceptions
Items like firewood, Persian sugarcane, and hay are exempt unless specifically cultivated for profit. Sugar cane (qasab al-sukkar) is subject to zakat according to Abu Hanifa. Produce irrigated by a large bucket (gharb) may have different rulings.
The text clarifies that intent (qasd al-istighlal) triggers zakat for otherwise exempt items.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
Modern farmers growing vegetables like spinach or tomatoes do not pay zakat on those crops. However, if they grow sugarcane, zakat is due (per Abu Hanifa). Similarly, if a farmer intentionally plants firewood trees for profit, zakat applies.
This ruling prevents undue burden on perishable produce and aligns with the hadith.

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling that no zakat is due on vegetables (khudrawat) and on items that do not last a year, according to the relied-upon position of the Sahibayn. The proof is a set of hadiths: 'There is no charity on vegetables' (though its chains are weak), and the hadith from Mu'adh listing only dates, wheat, and grains as subject to zakat, explicitly excusing cucumbers, watermelons, pomegranates, and sugarcane. However, later exceptions are mentioned: things like firewood (حطب) which are not normally cultivated for land exploitation are exempt, unless one intentionally cultivates them for profit, in which case the tithe applies. Persian sugarcane (used for pens) is exempt, but sugar cane (قصب السكر) is subject to tithe according to Abu Hanifa. The commentary also clarifies that 'vegetables' includes fruits and legumes, and that items that spoil within a year are exempt. The term 'gharb' refers to a large bucket used for irrigation, and the ruling for produce irrigated by such methods is mentioned.

Key Terms
الخضراوات (al-khudrawat): Vegetables and fruits that are perishable, including legumes and fruits like apples and pears.
الحطب (al-hatab): Firewood and non-cultivated plant matter not normally intended for land exploitation.
القصب (al-qasab): Persian sugarcane (used for pens and building) and sugar cane (qasab al-sukkar).
الغرب (al-gharb): A large bucket used for irrigation, implying a method that incurs effort.

Zakat on Vegetables and Non-Storable Crops
Ruling on sadaqah for vegetables and exemption for perishables

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat (sadaqah) for vegetables and identify which items are exempt due to perishability or lack of intended land exploitation.

Core Idea
Vegetables require zakat paid directly to the poor; perishables that spoil within a year are exempt.

The matn clearly states that sadaqah (zakat) is due on vegetables, but not on items that do not last a year. Imam Abu Hanifa further specifies that this zakat is an obligation on the owner to pay directly to the poor—the ruler does not collect it. The commentary then expands on exceptions: items like firewood, reeds, and grass that are not typically cultivated for land exploitation are exempt, but if someone intentionally cultivates them for profit, the tithe ('ushr) applies. This lesson unpacks the conditions and exceptions surrounding zakat on vegetables.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Find the core statement: 'On vegetables, there is sadaqah; and there is no sadaqah on what does not remain for a year.' This establishes both the general obligation and the key exemption.
The ruling is for sadaqah (zakat) on all vegetables, including fruits and herbs.
2
Understand the payment mechanism
According to Abu Hanifa, the sadaqah is paid by the owner directly to the poor, not collected by the ruler. This distinguishes it from other zakat types.
This is from the source 'Al-Asrar'.
3
Analyze the exemption for perishables
Items that do not last a year (i.e., spoil before a year) are exempt from sadaqah. The condition is temporal: if the produce cannot be stored for a full year, no zakat is due.
The commentary clarifies 'do not remain' means they spoil and decay.
4
Examine the exception for non-exploitation items
Items like firewood, reeds, grass, and palm fronds are exempt because they are not typically intended for land exploitation. However, if someone cultivates them with the intention of profit (e.g., turning a garden into a reed field), then 'ushr becomes obligatory.
The phrase 'except for things like firewood' introduces this exception.
5
Distinguish between types of reeds and sugar cane
Persian reeds (used for pens and construction) are exempt, but sugar cane is subject to 'ushr according to Abu Hanifa. This shows that the same category (reeds) can have different rulings based on usage.
The commentary explicitly mentions this distinction from Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

On vegetables, there is sadaqah; and there is no sadaqah on what does not remain for a year. Know that according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, sadaqah is obligatory on vegetables, which the owner pays to the poor, not that the ruler takes it. This is in 'Al-Asrar' by Qadi Imam Abu Zayd al-Dabusi. (Except for things like firewood) such as qasab (reeds) and hashish (dry grass). His statement: 'on vegetables' is with fatha on kha' and 'ajam, plural of khadra', meaning fruits like apples, pears, etc., and herbs like leeks, celery, etc., according to 'Al-Binaya' (1). His statement: 'and not on what does not remain' means things that do not last to a year but spoil and decay. His statement: 'Al-Asrar' with fatha on hamza, name of a book compiled by Qadi Abu Zayd al-Dabusi, and he is with fatha on dal, attributed to Dabusa, name of a village. His statement: 'except for things like firewood' means what is not usually intended for land exploitation, and its growth is not sought in gardens typically, like firewood, straw which is herbage, and palm fronds: i.e., leaves of palm trees from which baskets and fans are made, and marshmallow, saltwort, cotton trees, etc. However, if one intends exploitation with something from these, as when one makes gardens a reed-field or tree-filled or a grass-growing place, the tithe is obligatory. This is in 'Al-Hidayah' (2). His statement: 'like qasab' means Persian reeds from which pens are made and used in buildings; as for sugar cane, it has the tithe according to him. This is in 'Al-Hidayah' (3) and 'Al-Binaya' (4).

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the ruling on zakat for vegetables and perishable crops. The matn states that sadaqah (zakat) is due on vegetables, but not on items that do not last a year (i.e., they spoil before a year). The commentator clarifies that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, this sadaqah is obligatory on the owner to pay directly to the poor; the ruler (sultan) does not collect it. The exception 'except for things like firewood' refers to items not typically cultivated for land exploitation, such as reeds, grass, palm fronds, etc. However, if someone intentionally cultivates these for profit (e.g., turning a garden into a reed field), then 'ushr becomes obligatory. The commentator also notes that Persian reeds (for pens) are exempt, but sugar cane does incur 'ushr according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
خضراوات (khadrawāt): Vegetables, including fruits and herbs, as per this text: fruits like apples and pears, and herbs like leeks and celery.
حطب (ḥaṭab): Firewood; in this context, items not intended for land exploitation, such as reeds, grass, palm fronds, etc.
عشر ('ushr): Tithe, one-tenth of agricultural produce, obligatory on certain lands.

Key Takeaway

Zakat on Irrigated Crops and Banu Taghlib
Ruling on half-tithe for well/waterwheel irrigation and double tithe for Christian Arabs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi zakat rate for crops irrigated by well or waterwheel and apply the rule of non-deduction of expenses, and distinguish the rate for Banu Taghlib Christians.

Core Idea
Half 'ushr for irrigated crops; expenses not deducted; Taghlibis pay khums (double).

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies two distinct rulings: the zakat rate for crops that require manual irrigation, and the special rate for Christian Arabs of Banu Taghlib. The author explains that the half-'ushr (5%) is due because of the hardship and cost of watering, and no cultivation expenses are deducted from the gross produce. For Banu Taghlib, who hold 'ushri land, they pay khums (20%)—double the Muslim rate—by treaty. We will walk through the reasoning and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled: zakat on agricultural produce watered by a well bucket (gharb) or waterwheel (daliyah). The ruling is half 'ushr (nisf 'ushr).
Half 'ushr = 5% of total produce.
2
Understand the rationale for half 'ushr
Note the reason: hardship and cost (mashaqqa wa kulfa) in drawing water. The Lawgiver lightened the obligation accordingly. This is confirmed by Shafi'i scholars who also apply half 'ushr when water is purchased.
Hanafi principles do not reject this view.
3
Apply the rule on expenses
Recognize that expenses of cultivation (mu'an) such as wages are not deducted from the produce before calculating zakat. The half 'ushr is imposed on the gross yield. Ibn al-Humam argues that if expenses were deducted, the rate would always be 'ushr on the net, but the law varies the rate based on irrigation method, proving expenses are not deductible.
Variation in rate is due to irrigation difficulty, not net profit.
4
Identify the special case of Banu Taghlib
Banu Taghlib are Christian Arabs who, by treaty, pay double the Muslim zakat on 'ushri land: khums (20%) instead of 'ushr (10%). This is a historical precedent for differentiated jizya/zakat arrangements.
The rate is khums (one-fifth), double the 'ushr.
5
Summarize the practical differences
For a Muslim farmer: if crop is rain-fed or naturally irrigated → full 'ushr (10%); if watered by well/waterwheel → half 'ushr (5%). For a Taghlibi on 'ushri land: always khums (20%) regardless of irrigation. No expenses are deducted from any of these rates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفيما سُقِيَ بغَرب أو دالية نصفُ عُشْرِ بلا رفعِ مُؤَنِ الزّرع وخُمْسَ تَغْلَبِيِّ له أرض عشرية. قوله : نصف عشر ؛ لوجودِ المشقة والكلفة في السقي من الآبار، فخفف الشارع في الصدقة فيه؛ ولهذا ذكرت الشافعية أنه لو سقى بماء اشتراه يجب نصف العشر، وقواعدنا لا تأباه كذا نقله الباقاني في شرح ملتقى الأبحـر عن شيخه البهنسي. قوله : بلا رفع ...الخ ؛ قال ابن الهمام : «يعني لا يقالُ بعدم وجوب العشر في قدر الخارج الذي بمقابلة المؤنة، بل يجب العشر في الكل؛ لأنه حكم بتفاوت الواجب لتفاوت المؤنة، ولو رُفِعَتْ المؤنة كان الواجب واحداً، وهو العشر دائماً في الباقي؛ لأنه لم ينزل إلى نصفه إلا للمؤنة، والباقي بعد رفع المؤنة لا مؤنة فيه، فكان الواجب دائماً العشر، لكنَّ الواجب قد تفاوت شرعاً، فعلمنا أنه لم يعتبر شرعاً عدم عشر بعض الخارج». قوله : وخُمس تغلبي ؛ أي يؤخذ من التغلبي ضعف ما يُؤخذ من المسلم فيؤخذ الخمس، وهو ضعف العشر؛ لأنّ بني تغلب قوم من نصارى العرب، أنكروا
And for what is watered by a large bucket or a waterwheel, half a tithe, without deducting the expenses of cultivation; and a fifth for a Taghlibi who has 'ushri land. His statement: 'half a tithe' because of the hardship and cost in watering from wells, so the Lawgiver lightened the sadaqah in it; hence the Shafi'is mentioned that if he waters with purchased water, half a tithe is obligatory, and our principles do not reject it. This is narrated by al-Baqani in his commentary on Multaqa al-Abhar from his shaykh al-Bahansi. His statement: 'without deducting...etc.'; Ibn al-Humam said: 'It means one does not say that the tithe is not obligatory on the amount of produce corresponding to the expense; rather, the tithe is obligatory on the whole, because the variation in the obligatory amount is due to variation in expense; and if the expense were deducted, the obligatory amount would be uniform, always the tithe on the remainder, because it was reduced to half only due to expense, and the remainder after deducting expense has no expense in it, so the obligatory would always be the tithe; but the obligatory has varied by law, so we know that the law did not consider not tithing part of the produce.' His statement: 'and a fifth for a Taghlibi' means that from the Taghlibi is taken double what is taken from a Muslim, so a fifth is taken, which is double the tithe; because Banu Taghlib are a people of Christian Arabs, they refused...
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage discusses the zakat rates for crops based on irrigation method. If crops are watered by a well (gharb) or a waterwheel (daliyah), the zakat is half 'ushr (5%) due to the hardship and cost. Importantly, this half-'ushr is calculated on the total produce without deducting expenses such as wages for harvesters. The commentator, Ibn al-Humam, explains that the reduction to half is precisely because of the hardship; if expenses were deducted first, the rate would always be 'ushr on the net, but the law varies the rate based on irrigation method, so the expense is not deducted. The passage also addresses the case of Banu Taghlib, Christian Arabs who, by treaty, pay double the Muslim rate: instead of 'ushr, they pay khums (one-fifth) on 'ushri land.

Key Terms
غرب (gharb): A large bucket used for drawing water from a well; refers to well irrigation.
دالية (dāliyah): A waterwheel used for irrigation; like a noria.
نصف عشر (nisf 'ushr): Half tithe, 5% of produce, due when irrigation involves hardship or cost.
مؤن (mu'an): Expenses of cultivation, such as wages, which are not deducted from the produce before calculating zakat.
تغلبي (taghlabī): A member of the Banu Taghlib, a Christian Arab tribe subject to double zakat (khums) on 'ushri land.
خمس (khums): One-fifth, here the rate for Banu Taghlib on agricultural produce, equivalent to double the 'ushr.

Zakat on Irrigated Land: Half a Tenth and Non-Deduction of Expenses
Explaining the zakat rate for irrigated land and non-deduction of expenses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi zakat rate for irrigated land and explain why cultivation expenses are not deducted before calculating zakat.

Core Idea
Irrigated land pays half a tenth on the gross yield, not after deducting expenses.

Zakat on agricultural produce depends on the method of irrigation. This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah clarifies that for land irrigated by artificial means (dāliyah), the rate is half a tenth, and importantly, cultivation expenses such as harvesting wages are not deducted from the produce before zakat is calculated. The reasoning is based on istihsan due to the hardship and cost of irrigation. We will explore the ruling, its proof, and how Hanafi principles differ from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is zakat on agricultural produce from land irrigated by a waterwheel (dāliyah). The ruling: half a tenth (5%) of the total yield is wajib. No deduction of cultivation expenses.
The rate is half of the full tenth due to additional cost.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is istihsan based on the presence of hardship and cost (al-mashaqqah wa al-kulfah) in artificial irrigation. The Legislator lightened the charity accordingly.
The dalil is rational, not directly from nass.
3
Note the cross-madhhab reference
The commentator notes that even the Shafi'is agree that if water is purchased, half a tenth is due, which does not conflict with Hanafi principles.
However, for naturally irrigated land, Shafi'is give full tenth while Hanafis give half tenth for any artificial irrigation.
4
Analyse Ibn al-Humam's rationale
Ibn al-Humam argues that if expenses were deducted, the remaining produce would always be subject to the full tenth, contradicting the legal variation. The reduction to half is specifically due to expenses, so they cannot be deducted.
This reinforces that zakat is on the gross yield.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon ruling is half a tenth on the total produce without deduction of expenses. This is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah and supported by later authorities like Ibn al-Humam.
This is the operative fatwa for Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة باب الخارج
أو دالية نصفُ عُشْرِ بلا رفعِ مُؤَنِ الزّرع وخُمْسَ تَغْلَبِيِّ له أرض عشرية أو دالية نصف عُشْر بلا رفع مُؤَنِ الزرع: أي تجب الوظيفة: وهي عُشْرُ الكل أو نصفه، لا أنه يرفعُ مُؤنَ الزَّرع - كأجر الحصاد، ونحوه- ثم يُعطي وظيفته - وهي عشر الباقي أو نصفه .
قوله: نصف عشر؛ لوجودِ المشقة والكلفة في السقي من الآبار، فخفف الشارع في الصدقة فيه؛ ولهذا ذكرت الشافعية أنه لو سقى بماء اشتراه يجب نصف العشر، وقواعدنا لا تأباه كذا نقله الباقاني في شرح ملتقى الأبحر عن شيخه البهنسي .
قوله: بلا رفع ...الخ؛ قال ابن الهمام: «يعني لا يقالُ بعدم وجوب العشر في قدر الخارج الذي بمقابلة المؤنة، بل يجب العشر في الكل؛ لأنه حكم بتفاوت الواجب لتفاوت المؤنة، ولو رُفِعَتْ المؤنة كان الواجب واحداً، وهو العشر دائماً في الباقي؛ لأنه لم ينزل إلى نصفه إلا للمؤنة، والباقي بعد رفع المؤنة لا مؤنة فيه، فكان الواجب دائماً العشر، لكنَّ الواجب قد تفاوت شرعاً، فعلمنا أنه لم يعتبر شرعاً عدم عشر بعض الخارج».
Book of Zakat, Chapter on External (produce). Or a waterwheel (irrigated) [pays] half a tenth, without deducting the expenses of cultivation, and one-fifth from a Taghlabi who has 'ushri land. Or a waterwheel: half a tenth without deducting the expenses of cultivation: meaning the duty is imposed, which is a tenth of the whole or half of it, not that one deducts the expenses of cultivation—like wages of harvesting etc.—then gives the duty—which is a tenth of the remainder or half of it. His saying: half a tenth due to the presence of hardship and cost in irrigation from wells, so the Legislator lightened the charity therein; hence the Shafi'is mentioned that if one irrigated with purchased water, half a tenth is obligatory, and our principles do not reject it, as al-Baqani transmitted from his teacher al-Bahansi in his commentary on Multaqa al-Abhar. His saying: without deducting etc.; Ibn al-Humam said: 'It means that it is not said that the tenth is not obligatory on the amount of output corresponding to the expense, rather the tenth is obligatory on the whole; because the obligation was made to vary according to the variation of expense, and if the expense were deducted, the obligation would be one, which is always a tenth on the remainder; because it was reduced to half only because of the expense, and the remainder after deducting the expense has no expense, so the obligation would always be a tenth, but the obligation has varied legally, so we know that legally the non-tenth of some output was not considered.'
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Al-Wiqayah regarding zakat on agricultural produce. It clarifies the ruling for land irrigated by artificial means (dāliyah, a waterwheel): the zakat is half a tenth (1/20) of the total produce, not a full tenth. Importantly, this half-tenth is calculated on the gross yield without deducting any cultivation expenses such as harvesting wages. The commentator explains that the reduced rate is due to the additional hardship and cost of irrigation. He supports this by noting that even the Shafi'i school, which normally differs, agrees that if water is purchased, half a tenth becomes obligatory—a point that the Hanafi principles do not contradict, as transmitted by al-Baqani. Ibn al-Humam then provides a deeper rationale: if expenses were deducted, the remaining produce would always be subject to the full tenth, because the reduction to half was only due to the presence of expenses. Since the obligation varies legally (half-tenth with expenses vs. full tenth without), it proves that the law does not consider the non-tenth on any portion of the output; rather, the entire yield is subject to the flat rate as determined by the source of irrigation.

Key Terms
دالية (dāliyah): A waterwheel or any artificial irrigation device; the text uses it to denote land irrigated by such means.
مؤَن الزرع (mu'an al-zar'): Expenses of cultivation, such as wages of harvesters and other costs directly related to growing the crop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For artificially irrigated land, zakat is half a tenth on the total produce without deducting any cultivation expenses.

Double Zakat on Banu Taghlib: Continuity After Conversion
Intra-Hanafi dispute on continuity of double zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the double zakat for Banu Taghlib's 'ushri land and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding its continuity after conversion or sale.

Core Idea
The double zakat on Banu Taghlib's land is a fixed obligation tied to the land, not to the owner's religion.

This passage addresses a unique rule from the pact of Caliph 'Umar with the Christian Arab tribe Banu Taghlib: they pay double the Muslim zakat rate (one-fifth instead of one-tenth) on their 'ushri land. The key question is whether this double rate remains if the owner converts to Islam or if the land is sold to a Muslim or dhimmi. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement, and the relied-upon position shapes how this rule is applied in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the special pact
Understand why Banu Taghlib pay double: they refused jizya, so 'Umar fixed double zakat instead. This establishes the origin of the rate.
2
State the scope of the rule
The passage says the rule applies to all Taghlabi (adult male, child, female) and continues regardless of conversion or sale. Note this claim.
3
Locate the dispute
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the double rate remains even after conversion. Abu Yusuf says it drops to a single tenth because the cause (kufr) is gone.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyse the reasoning
Abu Hanifa/Muhammad: the doubling is a characteristic (wazifa) of the land itself. Abu Yusuf: the cause is the owner's disbelief; when that ends, the doubling ends.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If a Taghlabi converts, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad still take one-fifth; Abu Yusuf takes one-tenth. The mufta bihi is the majority view (double remains).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

رجله، وطفله، وأنثاه سواء، وإن أسلم، أو شراها مسلم أو ذمي) ، اعلم أنَّ العُشْرَ يؤخذ من أراضي أطفالنا، فيؤخذ ضعفُ ذلك من أراضي أطفالهم، ولا يسقط عنهم العشر المضاعفُ بالإسلام عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، وكذا عند محمد رحمه الله، وأما عند أبي يوسف رحمه الله فيؤخذ عشر واحد.
قوله: فيؤخذ عشر واحد؛ لا عشران؛ لذهاب علة التضعيف وهو الكفر.
And one-fifth from a Taghlabi who has 'ushri land: meaning from the Taghlabi is taken double what is taken from a Muslim, so one-fifth is taken, and it is double the tenth; because Banu Taghlib are a people of Christian Arabs, they refused to have the jizya (poll tax) taken from them, so 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) made a pact with them to take double what is taken from a Muslim, as has been mentioned. Its adult male, child, and female are equal, and if he becomes Muslim, or a Muslim or dhimmi buys it. Know that the tenth is taken from the lands of our children, so double that is taken from the lands of their children, and the double tenth does not drop from them by Islam according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), and likewise according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him). As for Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), a single tenth is taken. His saying: so a single tenth is taken; not two-tenths; because the cause of doubling—namely disbelief—is gone.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's phrase 'and one-fifth from a Taghlabi who has 'ushri land.' It explains that Banu Taghlib, being Christian Arabs, have a special arrangement: they pay double the Muslim zakat rate (i.e., one-fifth or 20%) on their 'ushri land. This originated from a pact made by Caliph 'Umar when they refused to pay jizya. The rule applies uniformly to all members of the tribe—male adults, children, females—and continues even if the owner converts to Islam or sells the land to a Muslim or a dhimmi. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the double rate persists regardless of conversion or change of ownership, because the doubling is a fixed characteristic of that land (a 'function' attached to the land). Abu Yusuf argues that once the owner converts, the cause (kufr) disappears, and only a single tenth is due. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is as per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, i.e., the double rate remains.

Key Terms
تغلبي (Taghlabī): A member of the Banu Taghlib tribe, Christian Arabs who had a special pact with 'Umar to pay double the Muslim zakat instead of jizya.
خمس (khums): One-fifth, which is double the standard tenth (ushr) payed by Muslims on 'ushri land.
علة التضعيف (illat al-tad'if): The cause of doubling—the disbelief (kufr) of the Taghlabi owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The double zakat on Banu Taghlib's 'ushri land is a land-linked obligation that persists regardless of the owner's conversion or sale to a Muslim or dhimmi, per the majority Hanafi view.

The Reversibility of 'Ushri Land Between Muslim and Dhimmi Ownership
Explaining the change of land type when transferred between Muslim and dhimmi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on when 'ushri land becomes subject to kharaj and when it reverts to 'ushr, and apply it to scenarios of sale, pre-emption, and invalid contracts.

Core Idea
Land loses its 'ushri status when owned by a dhimmi but regains it if reacquired by a Muslim.

In Hanafi fiqh, the type of land tax ('ushr or kharaj) is tied to the religious status of the owner. This lesson explains a key rule: when a dhimmi purchases 'ushri land from a Muslim, the land becomes subject to kharaj. However, if a Muslim later reacquires that land through pre-emption (shuf'a) or because the sale was invalid, the land returns to its original 'ushri status. Understanding this reversibility is crucial for correctly applying the tax obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original land type
Recognize that the land in question is 'ushri, i.e., land conquered peacefully or owned by a Muslim subject to 'ushr (tithe).
'Ushri land is distinct from kharaji land, which is conquered by force.
2
Determine the effect of dhimmi ownership
When a dhimmi acquires 'ushri land, the land becomes kharaji, meaning kharaj (land tax) is imposed instead of 'ushr.
The rationale: 'ushr is an act of worship not required of non-Muslims.
3
Identify the conditions for reversion to 'ushri
If a Muslim reacquires the land via pre-emption (shuf'a) or due to an invalid sale (fasid bay'), the land reverts to 'ushri status.
The text emphasizes both scenarios.
4
Understand the legal reasoning
The reversion occurs because the owner's faith changes, and 'ushr is attached to the Muslim owner, not the land itself.
This is a consistent Hanafi principle: obligations that are acts of worship depend on the person.
5
Apply to practical scenarios
Practice with examples: sale to dhimmi, Muslim taking by shuf'a, return due to invalid contract.
The land's classification changes with each transfer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأُخِذَ الخَراجُ من ذمي اشترى عشرية مسلم، وعُشْرَ مسلمٌ أخذها منه بشفعة، أو ردت عليه لفساد البيع: أي إن أخذها من ذمي شفعة، أو اشترى الذمي المسلم العشرية، ثُمَّ رُدَّت على المسلم لفساد البيع، عادت عشرية كما كانت.
قوله: شفعة: بالضم: مأخوذ من الشفع: بمعنى الضم: وهو عبارة شرعاً: عن تملك الأرض بما قام على المشتري بالشركة أو الجوار. فإذا كانت أرض للذمي فباعها الذمي وكان لمسلم فيها حق شفعة، فأخذها من المشتري صارت عشرية.
قوله: عادت عشرية؛ الظاهر أنه جزاء لقوله: إن أخذها، ولا يخفى أن العود إلى الحالة الأولى إنّما هو الأولى، ولو اكتفى على قوله: صارت عشرية كان أخصر وأظهر.
And kharaj is taken from a dhimmi who buys a Muslim's 'ushri land, and a Muslim who takes it from him by pre-emption, or it is returned to him due to invalidity of the sale: i.e., if a Muslim takes it from a dhimmi by pre-emption, or a dhimmi buys the Muslim's 'ushri land then it is returned to the Muslim due to invalid sale, it returns to being 'ushri as it was. His saying: pre-emption (shuf'a) is derived from shaf' meaning joining; it is a legal term for ownership of land by what the buyer paid, due to partnership or adjacency. So if a dhimmi owned land and sold it, and a Muslim had a right of pre-emption in it, he takes it from the buyer and it becomes 'ushri. His saying: returns to 'ushri; apparently it is the result of his saying 'if he takes it', and it is clear that returning to the original state is primary, and if he sufficed with saying 'it becomes 'ushri' it would be more concise and clearer.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage explains the effect of transfer of 'ushri land between Muslims and dhimmis. The rule: if a dhimmi purchases 'ushri land from a Muslim, kharaj is levied on that land (it becomes kharaji) because the 'ushr is a form of worship not required of a non-Muslim. Conversely, if a Muslim acquires such land from a dhimmi—either by exercising the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) or because the original sale to the dhimmi was invalid and the land is returned—the land reverts to its original 'ushri status. The commentator notes that the phrase 'it returns to 'ushri' is a bit redundant; simply saying 'it becomes 'ushri' would be sufficient, but the intended meaning is clear: the land regains its original classification.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'a): Pre-emption: the right of a partner or neighbor to purchase land sold to a third party at the same price.
خراج (kharāj): Land tax imposed on non-Muslim owners of 'ushri land; equivalent to land revenue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Kharaj
C) Jizya
D) No tax

Key Takeaway
When 'ushri land is transferred to a dhimmi, kharaj becomes due; when it returns to a Muslim, the land reverts to 'ushri status, because 'ushr is an act of worship required only of Muslims.

Double Ushr on Banu Taghlib Lands and Kharaj on Transfer of Ushri Land to a Dhimmi
Ruling on double 'ushr for Banu Taghlib and kharaj from dhimmi buying 'ushri land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on double 'ushr for Banu Taghlib, evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and apply the rule for kharaj when a dhimmi acquires 'ushri land.

Core Idea
The double 'ushr on Banu Taghlib lands is perpetual and attached to the land, not the owner's faith.

This lesson examines a specific land-tax ruling from the Hanafi school concerning the Christian Arab tribe Banu Taghlib. The passage also clarifies what happens when ownership of 'ushri land changes between Muslims and dhimmis. You will learn the basis of the double 'ushr and the intra-Hanafi disagreement, as well as the principle that 'ushr being an act of worship cannot be taken from a non-Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main issues
Recognize that the passage covers: (1) the double 'ushr on Banu Taghlib lands and the effect of conversion to Islam, and (2) the imposition of kharaj when a dhimmi buys 'ushri land and the return to 'ushr when a Muslim reacquires it.
These are separate but related rulings on land taxation.
2
Analyze the double 'ushr ruling
Note that the same rule applies to male, female, and minor Taghlibi landowners. The double 'ushr does not drop if the owner becomes Muslim according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
Abu Yusuf's opposing view is that only a single 'ushr is taken after Islam because the cause (kufr) is gone.
3
Understand the reasoning for persistence
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that the doubling became a function of the land itself (ṣārat waẓīfa tilka al-arḍ), so it does not change with a change of owner.
This is a key legal principle: the tax is attached to the land, not the owner's religious status.
4
Apply the rule for dhimmi purchase
When a dhimmi buys 'ushri land from a Muslim, kharaj is taken from the dhimmi because 'ushr is an act of worship and cannot be required of a non-Muslim.
Conversely, if a Muslim acquires 'ushri land from a dhimmi via pre-emption (shuf'a) or a defective sale (fasād al-bay'), the land reverts to being 'ushri and 'ushr is taken.
5
Connect the underlying principle
The overall principle is that the tax regime follows the land's original classification ('ushri vs. kharaji) and the owner's faith only matters to the extent that 'ushr is worship-based.
This explains why a dhimmi cannot be charged 'ushr and must pay kharaj instead.

His male, his child, and his female are equal, and if he becomes Muslim, or a Muslim or dhimmi buys it, and the kharaj is taken from a dhimmi who bought a Muslim's 'ushri land, and the 'ushr of a Muslim who took it from him by pre-emption, or it was returned to him due to defective sale. His male, his child, and his female are equal, and if he becomes Muslim, or a Muslim or dhimmi buys it, know that the 'ushr is taken from the lands of our children, so double that is taken from the lands of their children, and the doubled 'ushr does not drop from them by Islam according to Abu Hanifa, and similarly according to Muhammad, but according to Abu Yusuf, a single 'ushr is taken. And the kharaj is taken from a dhimmi who bought a Muslim's 'ushri land, and the 'ushr of a Muslim who took it from him by pre-emption, or it was returned to him due to defective sale: that is, if he took it from a dhimmi by pre-emption, or the dhimmi bought the Muslim's 'ushri land, then it was returned to the Muslim due to defective sale, it reverts to 'ushri as it was from him in the presence of the Companions on the condition that jizya be taken from them, and 'Umar made peace with them. [2] His statement: 'becomes Muslim'; meaning if the Taghlibi owner of the 'ushri land becomes Muslim, or a Muslim or dhimmi buys it from him, the double remains upon it according to him, because the doubling became a function of that land, so it does not change with change of owner, and there is disagreement with Abu Yusuf. [3] His statement: 'a single 'ushr is taken'; not two 'ushrs, because the cause of doubling, which is disbelief, is gone. [4] His statement: 'and the kharaj is taken'; because the 'ushr contains the meaning of worship, so it is not taken from the disbeliever, and only kharaj is obligatory upon them. [0] His statement: 'pre-emption' (shuf'a); with damm, derived from shaf' meaning joining, and in legal terminology it is the ownership of land for what the buyer paid, due to partnership or adjacency. So if a dhimmi owns land and sells it, and a Muslim has a right of pre-emption in it, and he takes it from the buyer, it becomes 'ushri. [6] His statement: 'it reverts to 'ushri'; apparently it is the result of his statement 'if he took it', and it is not hidden that return to the first state is primary, and if he sufficed with his statement 'it becomes 'ushri' it would be shorter and clearer.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the taxes ( 'ushr and kharaj ) on lands belonging to Banu Taghlib (a Christian Arab tribe) and the effect of change of ownership. The matn states that the same rule applies to male, female, and minor owners, and that even if the Taghlibi owner becomes Muslim or a Muslim or dhimmi buys the land, the double 'ushr remains obligatory. However, Abu Yusuf differs: he says that when the owner becomes Muslim, only a single 'ushr is taken because the cause of doubling (kufr) is removed. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the double 'ushr is attached to the land itself, not the owner's religion, so it persists. Next, the text rules that if a dhimmi buys 'ushri land from a Muslim, kharaj is taken from the dhimmi, because 'ushr is an act of worship and cannot be required of a non-Muslim. Conversely, if a Muslim acquires 'ushri land from a dhimmi via pre-emption or a defective sale, the land reverts to being 'ushri and kharaj is not taken. The commentary explains the legal reasoning and provides the technical definition of shuf'a (pre-emption). This ruling is based on the precedent of Caliph 'Umar's pact with Banu Taghlib.

Key Terms
العشر (al-'ushr): The tithe or one-tenth tax on agricultural produce from 'ushri lands.
الخراج (al-kharaj): A land tax imposed on non-Muslims (dhimmis) for land they cultivate, in lieu of 'ushr.
التضعيف (al-tad'if): Doubling of the 'ushr to two-tenths (i.e., 20%) on the lands of Banu Taghlib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The 'ushr drops entirely because he is now Muslim.
B) The 'ushr is reduced to a single 'ushr (one-tenth).
C) The double 'ushr (two-tenths) remains obligatory on the land.
D) The land becomes kharaji and kharaj is taken instead.

Key Takeaway
The double 'ushr on Banu Taghlib lands is a perpetual land tax, not affected by the owner's faith, and kharaj replaces 'ushr when a dhimmi owns 'ushri land.

Classification of 'Ushri and Kharaji Lands
Listing of six 'ushri and eight kharaji land types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify the six types of 'ushri lands and eight types of kharaji lands according to the Hanafi school, and explain the basis for their classification.

Core Idea
Land tax status in Hanafi fiqh is determined by acquisition method and irrigation source.

Determining whether a land is subject to 'ushr (tithe) or kharaj (land tax) is crucial for calculating zakat and Islamic taxation. This lesson presents the authoritative Hanafi taxonomy from al-Binaya, listing six types of 'ushri lands and eight types of kharaji lands. Understanding this classification will help you correctly identify the legal ruling for a given land based on its history and water source.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two categories
Recognize that lands are divided into 'ushri (subject to 'ushr) and kharaji (subject to kharaj). The classification depends on factors like how the land was acquired, the status of its owners, and the water source used for irrigation.
'Ushr is typically 1/10 or 1/20 of the produce; kharaj is a fixed amount.
2
Memorize the six 'ushri types
Go through the list: (1) Arab lands (Hijaz, Yemen), (2) lands whose inhabitants embraced Islam voluntarily, (3) lands conquered by force and distributed to warriors, (4) revived lands irrigated with 'ushri water, (5) former kharaji lands now irrigated with 'ushri water, (6) a house converted into an orchard irrigated with 'ushri water. Note the common thread: either the land is originally Arab, became Muslim-owned through peaceful means, or is irrigated with 'ushri water.
3
Memorize the eight kharaji types
Study the eight types: (1) lands conquered by force left with kharaj (e.g., Sawad Iraq), (2) land revived by a dhimmi with permission, (3) house turned orchard even if irrigated with 'ushri water (status stays kharaji), (4) land where non-Muslims requested kharaj, (5) land irrigated with kharaj water, (6) land bought by a Muslim from a non-Muslim, (7) 'ushri land now irrigated with kharaj water, (8) Muslim's house turned orchard irrigated with kharaj water. Note that kharaj status can persist or be acquired through irrigation.
Type 6 is debated: buying from a dhimmi may transfer kharaj liability.
4
Note the definition of 'bustan'
The text defines 'bustan' as land enclosed by a wall with scattered trees. This definition matters because converting a house into a bustan can affect the tax classification, depending on the water source.

[٢]قوله: بستاناً؛ هو أرض يحوط عليها حائط، وفيها أشجار متفرقة. كذا في «معراج الدراية».
Book of Zakat / Chapter of External (Tax) and on a House Made into an Orchard (And on a House Made into an Orchard) Six: [1] His statement: And on a house... etc.; al-'Ayni said in al-Binaya: Know that the 'ushri lands: First: The land of the Arabs like Hijaz and Yemen. Second: Land whose people embraced Islam willingly on that [basis]. Third: Land conquered by force and divided among the warriors. Fourth: Land revived and irrigated with 'ushr water. Fifth: The kharaji land whose kharaj water ceased, so it was irrigated with 'ushri water. Sixth: He made his house an orchard and irrigated it with 'ushr water. And the kharaji lands are eight: First: That which was conquered by force and left in their hands with the kharaj levied on them, as 'Umar did with the lands of Sawad Iraq and Egypt. Second: Land revived by a dhimmi infidel with the imam's permission or a fighter to whom the imam granted a portion according to al-Tuhfa. Third: He made his house an orchard even if he irrigates it with 'ushr water. Fourth: Some infidels asked the imam to impose kharaj on their lands without [fighting?]. Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage is a listing from al-Binaya by al-'Ayni, quoted in the commentary, enumerating the types of 'ushri and kharaji lands. It serves as a foundational taxonomy for determining which lands are subject to 'ushr (tithe) and which to kharaj (land tax). The six 'ushri lands include: (1) original Arab lands like Hijaz and Yemen, (2) lands whose inhabitants accepted Islam voluntarily with the understanding that 'ushr applies, (3) lands conquered by force and distributed to the Muslim army, (4) dead lands revived and irrigated with rainwater or river water that is 'ushri, (5) kharaji lands that lost their kharaj water source and are now irrigated with 'ushri water, (6) a house converted into an orchard and irrigated with 'ushri water. The eight kharaji lands include: (1) lands conquered by force and left in the hands of the original owners with kharaj, following 'Umar's practice in Iraq and Egypt, (2) land revived by a dhimmi with permission, (3) a house turned into an orchard even if irrigated with 'ushri water (because the original status was kharaji?), (4) lands where the non-Muslims requested kharaj imposition, (5) land that was irrigated with kharaj water, (6) land bought by a Muslim from a non-Muslim (the ruling is debated), (7) 'ushri land that loses its water source and is irrigated with kharaj water, (8) a Muslim's house made into an orchard and irrigated with kharaj water. The author also defines 'bustan' (orchard) as land enclosed by a wall with scattered trees.

Key Terms
الأرض العشرية (al-ard al-'ushriyya): Land on which 'ushr (one-tenth or half-tenth) is payable on its produce.
الأرض الخراجية (al-ard al-kharajiyya): Land on which kharaj (a fixed land tax) is imposed, typically on conquered lands left in non-Muslim hands.
البستان (al-bustan): A garden or orchard enclosed by a wall with scattered trees.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a kharaji land according to the text?
A) The land of the Arabs (Hijaz and Yemen).
B) Land revived and irrigated with 'ushri water.
C) Land bought by a Muslim from a non-Muslim.
D) Land conquered by force and distributed to warriors.

Key Takeaway
The tax status of land in Hanafi fiqh is based on its acquisition history and current water source, not solely on the owner's religion.

Classification of 'Ushri and Kharaji Lands and Ruling on a House Turned into a Garden
Definition and ruling on land taxation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six types of 'ushri lands and eight types of kharaji lands, and apply the rule that a Muslim's garden irrigated with kharaj water becomes subject to kharaj due to the water's transfer of obligation.

Core Idea
Land tax status follows the water source: using kharaj water invites kharaj even for a Muslim's garden.

This lesson covers a crucial topic in Hanafi land taxation: the classification of lands into 'ushri (subject to tithe) and kharaji (subject to land tax) based on their origin, water source, and ownership. The passage also addresses a specific case: when a Muslim converts his house into a garden and irrigates it with kharaj water, does kharaj become due? The answer, grounded in the principle that water's tax status transfers to the land, resolves a seeming contradiction with the rule that kharaj is not originally imposed on Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main topics
The passage has two parts: first, a classification of 'ushri and kharaji lands (six and eight types respectively) from al-Binaya; second, a ruling on a house turned into a garden, with an objection and response.
The classification sets the stage by defining when land is 'ushri or kharaji.
2
Analyze the definition of bistan
The commentator defines 'bistan' (garden) as enclosed land with scattered trees. This definition matters because the ruling on taxation depends on the land being a garden, not just having trees.
The definition helps avoid confusion with mere tree planting.
3
Extract the ruling for a Muslim's garden
For a Muslim who makes his house a garden and irrigates it with kharaj water, kharaj becomes wajib. For a dhimmi, kharaj is due regardless of water type.
The key condition for a Muslim is irrigation with kharaj water.
4
Understand the objection and its answer
The objection: kharaj cannot be imposed on a Muslim initially. The answer: here, kharaj arises from the water's transfer of obligation, not direct imposition; the Muslim consents by using kharaj water.
Al-Zayla'i and Ibn al-Humam explained the transfer mechanism.
5
Apply the water principle to other scenarios
The passage also generalizes: for revived dead land, water source determines tax status. This principle allows consistent classification.
Consider how this applies to a Muslim buying kharaji land or a dhimmi using 'ushr water.

Book of Zakat / Chapter of Produce / And concerning a house that is made into a garden
