(٤) إذا تمهد هذا فنقول : اللام الداخلة على الصدقات والفقراء وغيره في آية المصارف لا يمكن حملها على العهد ، وهو ظاهر لعدم المعهوديّة ، ولا يمكن حملها على الاستغراق، فإنه يستلزم حرجاً بيناً ، وتكليفاً بما ليس في وسع أحد، فلا بد أن يراد بها الجنس، فإذن يكون معناه : جنس الصدقة الجنس الفقير وجنس المسكين، وقس عليه، فلا جمعية هاهنا ، حتى يقال إنه لا يصرفه إلى أقل من ثلاثة ؛ لئلا يفوت مؤدّي الجمعية.
[١] قوله : المعهود ؛ أي الخارجي ؛ فإنّه المقدّم على الاستغراق والجنس، وأما العهد الذهني فيكمن في كل موضع، وحكمه حكم الجنس، كما حققه التفتازاني في «التلويح»). (٢) قوله : كما في قوله : فإن النبي لو كان قد حرم عليه التزوج بعد نسائه التسع اللاتي كن معه، فمعناه : لا يحل لك يا محمد جنس النساء من بعد، وليس معناه أنه لا يحلّ لك كلّ من نساء الدنيا، فإنّه ليس في وسع أحد فلا يفيد المنع منه، ولا عهد هاهنا . فظاهر [٣]قوله : لأنه ... الخ ؛ دليل لعدم إرادة الاستغراق، وأمـا عـدم إرادة العـهـدِ فظاهر [٤]قوله : جميع الصدقات ؛ أي كل واحد واحد منهما، لكل واحد من الفقير وغيره، فإنّ الاستغراق يراد به الكلّ الإفرادى لا الكلّ المجموعي، وإن كان في الجمع كما فصله التفتازاني في «المطوّل». [1] Ibn al-Sabil: he is one who has wealth but it is not with him. [2] (1) And the giver of Zakat may distribute it to all of them or to some of them: a precaution against the saying of al-Shafi'i, because according to him it is necessary to distribute to all categories, so he gives from each category three; because the minimum of a plural is three. And we say: when 'lam' enters upon a plural, he said in 'al-Nahr': 'The dispute is verbal due to agreement that all categories except the worker are given on condition of poverty, so the stranded traveler is given by agreement.' End. Yes, the benefit of the dispute appears in wills and endowments and the like, when the testator says: in the path of Allah. [3] His saying: 'not with him'; meaning whether he is away from his homeland or in his homeland, and he has debts that he cannot collect. Thus in 'al-Nahr'. His saying: 'And for the giver'; meaning it is permissible for the giver of Zakat to distribute Zakat to all the mentioned categories, or to some of them, even one from any category, as was narrated from 'Umar that he used to take the obligatory portion in charity and put it in one category, and from Ibn 'Abbas: in whichever category you distribute it, it suffices you. Al-Tabari narrated both in his 'Tafsir'. [3] His saying: 'When 'lam' enters... etc.' Explanation: The original use of 'lam' is for external specification; if not, then for generality; if not, then for genus, whether it enters upon a singular or a plural. And when 'lam' is taken as for genus in the plural, the meaning of plurality is nullified, and the genus itself is intended. This has been established in the books of Usul in a way that leaves no room for addition. (4) When this is established, we say: The 'lam' that enters upon 'al-sadaqat' (charities) and 'al-fuqara' (the poor) and others in the verse of disbursements cannot be taken as for specification; this is apparent due to the absence of a specified referent. And it cannot be taken as for generality, because that would entail manifest hardship and an obligation beyond anyone's capacity. So it must be taken as for genus. Therefore its meaning is: the genus of charity for the genus of the poor and the genus of the needy, and so on. So there is no plurality here such that it would be said that he may not give to fewer than three, lest the significance of plurality be lost. [1] His saying: 'the specified'; meaning external; for it is given precedence over generality and genus. As for mental specification, it occurs in every place, and its ruling is that of genus, as al-Taftazani established in 'al-Talwih'. (2) His saying: 'as in His saying': for the Prophet if it had been forbidden for him to marry after his nine wives who were with him, its meaning is: O Muhammad, it is not permissible for you the genus of women hereafter, and its meaning is not that it is not permissible for you all women of the world, for that is beyond anyone's capacity and thus does not effect a prohibition, and there is no specification here. So it is apparent. [3] His saying: 'because... etc.': evidence for not intending generality. As for not intending specification, it is apparent. [4] His saying: 'all charities'; meaning each individual one, for each poor person and others, for generality intends individual totality, not collective totality, even if in the plural, as al-Taftazani detailed in 'al-Mutawwal'. [0] His saying: 'And this is not... etc.': an objection was raised against it that it is possible because the ruler of each town could decide.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the distribution of Zakat. The Hanafi school holds that the giver of Zakat may distribute it to all eight categories (asnaf) mentioned in Surah al-Tawbah 9:60, or to some of them, even a single category. The Shafi'i school, on the other hand, requires distribution to all categories, giving at least three individuals from each, because the plural form (e.g., 'al-fuqara') implies a minimum of three. The Hanafi response is based on a linguistic analysis of the definite article 'lam' (ال) in the verse. They argue that 'lam' when attached to a plural noun is not for generality (istiqraq) but for genus (jins). This analysis prevents the interpretation that 'al-fuqara' means all poor people individually, which would be an impossible obligation. Instead, it means the genus of the poor. Therefore, giving Zakat to one category is sufficient. The passage also cites support from the practices of Umar and Ibn Abbas. The benefit of this dispute appears in wills and endowments where wording like 'in the path of Allah' may be used. The text also clarifies that Ibn al-Sabil includes one who has wealth but is away from it, even in his homeland, if he cannot access it.

Key Terms
ابن السبيل (Ibn al-Sabil): The wayfarer; one who has wealth but it is not with him, whether away from home or at home but unable to access his wealth (e.g., due to debts or imprisonment).
اللام (al-lam): The definite article (ال) used for definition. In Usul al-Fiqh, it can indicate: external specification (al-‘ahd al-khariji), generality (al-istiqraq), or genus (al-jins).
الجمعية (al-jum'iyyah): The meaning of plurality or collective sense of a plural noun. The argument is that when 'lam' indicates genus, this collectivity is nullified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because there is an external specified context (al-‘ahd al-khariji).
B) Because it would lead to hardship (haraj) and an impossible requirement.
C) Because the word 'al-fuqara' is singular in meaning.
D) Because the Prophet said so in a hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits giving Zakat to a single category because the definite article in the verse indicates genus; the Shafi'i requirement to distribute to all categories is based on a different linguistic interpretation.

The Hanafi Interpretation of the Laam in the Zakat Verse: Genus, Not Entitlement
Explaining Hanafi interpretation of 'li' in zakat verse as genus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi interpretation of the laam in Quran 9:60 and analyze the Shafi'i counter-argument, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
The laam in the zakat verse indicates genus, not entitlement — zakat is for the category, not every individual or all categories.

This lesson explores a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the meaning of the laam (ل) in the zakat verse (Quran 9:60). The Hanafis argue that the laam indicates genus (jins), meaning zakat is for the category of recipients, not that every individual must receive. The Shafi'is interpret it as indicating entitlement and division, requiring distribution to all eight categories if possible. This interpretive difference has a direct impact on how zakat is disbursed in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi claim: the laam in 'li al-fuqara' indicates genus (jins), not the known (ahd) or all-inclusive (istighraq). The verse specifies the type of recipients, not that every poor person must receive.
The Hanafi position relies on impossibility of istighraq and the original meaning of laam.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
State that Imam al-Shafi'i views the laam as indicating entitlement (istihqaq) and division, similar to 'mal li-Zayd'. This would require zakat to be distributed among all categories and to multiple individuals.
The Shafi'i dalil includes analogies to bequests and ownership.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof against istighraq
Examine the Hanafi argument that istighraq (all-inclusive) would require every zakat payment to reach every poor person, which is impossible and leads to hardship. Therefore, the laam must be for genus.
The text uses the example of 'Women are not lawful for you after this' (Quran 33:52) to illustrate laam as genus.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal to the Shafi'i argument
Review the Hanafi responses: (1) The unknown cannot be entitled; (2) Laam originally indicates specification, not ownership; (3) Some categories use 'fi' (e.g., fi al-riqab) showing the verse is about expenditure, not entitlement; (4) Even if istighraq is conceded, juxtaposition of collectives implies division of individuals among individuals.
The rebuttal uses usul principles like muqabala al-jam' bi al-jam'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafis allow giving zakat to any one eligible individual from any category (e.g., all zakat to one poor person). Shafi'is require distributing to all eight categories if they exist, with at least three persons per category if possible.
This difference stems from the interpretive starting point.

ولا يمكن حملها على المعهود ، ولا على الاستغراق، يراد بها الجنس، وتبطل الجمعية ) ، كما في قوله تعالى : في لَا يَحِلُّ لَكَ النِّسَاءُ مِنْ بَعْدُ .

And we say: The unknown is not suitable to be entitled, and also the original of laam is for specification, not for ownership and entitlement, and also transferring ownership to the unknown is invalid, and also there is no laam in His statement: 'and for the necks' and His statement: 'and for the path of Allah', and in summary the verse is for clarifying the avenue of expenditure, not for clarifying entitlement. Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the interpretation of the laam in the verse on zakat recipients (Quran 9:60). The Hanafi position is that the laam indicates genus (jins), not the known (ahd) or all-inclusive (istighraq). The commentary begins by arguing that carrying the laam on al-ahd or al-istighraq is impossible because it would imply that all zakat in the world must be distributed to every poor person, which is beyond human capacity and leads to hardship. Therefore, the laam must be interpreted as genus: 'the genus of alms for the genus of the poor, the genus of the needy,' etc. This interpretation also invalidates the requirement to give to a minimum of three individuals per category.

The commentator then addresses objections: If we concede that the laam indicates istighraq (all-inclusive), the Hanafi still wins because the juxtaposition of collectives (alms and recipients) necessitates a division of individuals among individuals—each individual alms goes to an individual recipient, not all to all. This is a usul principle also applied in the discussion of wudu.

The Shafi'i claim is then presented: The laam indicates entitlement (istihqaq) and division, like 'the wealth is for Zayd' or a bequest to categories. The Hanafi response is multifaceted: (1) the unknown (the poor collectively) cannot be an entitled party; (2) the original meaning of laam is specification (ikhtisas), not ownership; (3) transferring ownership to an unknown entity is invalid; (4) some zakat categories (e.g., 'fi al-riqab', 'fi sabilillah') use 'fi' not 'li', showing the verse is about expenditure avenues, not entitlement.

In summary, the passage establishes the Hanafi method of interpreting the zakat verse: the laam indicates genus, making zakat payable to any individual from any category, without requiring distribution to all or a specific number. The text also references other Hanafi sources for deeper study.

Key Terms
اللام (al-lam): The Arabic particle lām used in the zakat verse; interpreted by Hanafis as indicating genus (jins).
الاستغراق (al-istighrāq): Implicating all individuals of a category; interpreting lām as 'all-inclusive' would mean zakat must reach every poor person.
الجنس (al-jins): The genus or category; the lām indicates the type, not each individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi interpretation of the laam in the zakat verse, what does the laam indicate?
A) That zakat must be distributed to all eight categories equally
B) That zakat is for the genus (jins) of the recipients, not every individual
C) That zakat must be given to at least three persons from each category
D) That zakat is a ownership transfer to each poor person individually

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi interpretation of the laam as genus (jins) allows zakat to be given to any eligible individual from any category, without requiring distribution to all categories or a minimum number.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Hanafi Interpretation of Lam in Zakat Verse and Refutation of Shafi‘i
Hanafi refutation of Shafi‘i on lam in zakat verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi interpretation of the lam in the zakat verse and refute the Shafi‘i claim that it indicates mandatory division.

Core Idea
The lam in the zakat verse specifies the category, not ownership — mandatory division is not required.

This passage presents a classical linguistic and rational dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools over the interpretation of the lam in Surah At-Tawbah 9:60. At stake is whether zakat must be divided among multiple categories or can be given to a single recipient group. The Hanafi school defends its permissive view with a detailed analysis of the Quranic wording and logical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi‘i claim and evidence
State that Imam al-Shafi‘i argues the lam indicates ownership and mandatory division, analogizing to ownership statements like 'al-mal li Zayd' and to a bequest (one-third to categories).
2
Analyze the Hanafi counter-arguments on the lam
Note that the Hanafis point out: lam originally indicates specification (ikhtisas) not ownership; the recipients are unknown so cannot own; some categories (fi al-riqab, fi sabil Allah) lack lam altogether.
This is the core linguistic dispute.
3
Examine the infinite regress (tasalsul) argument
If division is intended, each part of zakat must also be divided, leading to an endless regression. This proves division cannot be the intended meaning.
This refutes the Shafi‘i reading from a rational perspective.
4
Distinguish the Quranic verse from human bequests
In a bequest, the lam is used with the intention of division, so it must be followed. In the Quranic verse, the lam is for specifying categories, not division.
The bequest analogy does not apply.
5
Conclude with the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the Hanafi view, giving all zakat to one category is permissible; under the Shafi‘i view, it must be divided among all eight categories if they exist.
This is the practical difference in rulings.

So it becomes like his statement: 'Charity is for the poor and needy... etc.' It is not intended that charity is divided among them; because if it is divided among the categories, then what reaches the poor would undoubtedly be called charity collectively, due to the concern of delivering it to every single type of disbursement. In summary, the verse is for explaining the category of disbursement, not for explaining entitlement. If you want more detail on this discussion, refer to 'al-Binaya' and other commentaries of 'al-Hidayah'. And by this is repelled what was objected: that if it is said: 'the water of the pitcher is divided between two', it is not understood except that each has a portion of it, not that every part is divided. The refutation: that it is not understood only because the intended meaning of water is the total quantity; if a rule is applied to the type of water in the pitcher, that would necessitate it definitely. [1] His statement: 'contrary to... etc.'; a response to what al-Shafi‘i cited as evidence, and its gist: that when one says: 'one-third of my wealth is for the poor and needy', the lam there is not for explaining the category of disbursement, but for explaining division; so it is not permissible to give to one category only, because that contradicts the intention of the endower or testator, unlike the verse of categories; for the lam in it cannot be for division. [2] His statement: 'not division'; meaning division is not intended, and it is possible its meaning is: not an explanation of division, then it is in the genitive case. So it is understood that the intended meaning is the explanation of the categories, not division.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Shafi‘i school interprets the lam in 'lil-fuqara' as indicating ownership and mandatory division among the eight categories of zakat recipients. The Hanafi school responds with several arguments: (1) The lam originally indicates specification (ikhtisas), not ownership. (2) Giving ownership to an unknown group is invalid. (3) The categories 'fi al-riqab' and 'fi sabil Allah' lack lam, proving it is not for ownership. (4) If the lam indicated division, it would lead to infinite regress (tasalsul): if each recipient must receive a share, then each share must be further divided. The Hanafi view is that the verse only states the categories where zakat may be spent, without requiring division among them or that every category receives a share. The example of a bequest (one-third to the poor) is distinguished because the lam there is from the testator’s intention of division, whereas the Quranic lam is from Allah for specifying categories.

Key Terms
اللام (al-lam): The letter lam used as a preposition in the Quranic verse, interpreted by Hanafis as indicating the category (li bayan al-masrif) not ownership.
المصرف (al-masrif): The categories or channels where zakat is to be disbursed, as specified in the Quran.
القسمة (al-qismah): Division or distribution among multiple recipients, which Hanafis argue is not required by the verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what does the lam in 'lil-fuqara' in the zakat verse indicate?
A) Ownership and division
B) Category of disbursement
C) Mandatory distribution
D) Priority of the poor

Key Takeaway
The lam in the zakat verse specifies the categories of disbursement, not mandatory division, according to the Hanafi school.

Zakat Requires Ownership Transfer
Ruling with proof on zakat's tamlik condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement of tamlik in zakat and identify expenditures that violate this condition.

Core Idea
Zakat must be given as ownership to a living person; spending on mosques or the dead is invalid.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies a key principle: zakat is not a general charity fund but a specific transfer of ownership. Understanding this distinction prevents misapplication of zakat funds on communal projects or funeral expenses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What acts are being prohibited? Spending zakat on building mosques, bridges, digging rivers, and on funeral expenses (shroud, burial, debt of deceased). The ruling is that these are impermissible (haram).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the principle of tamlik derived from the Quranic verses on zakat (Surah al-Tawbah:60) and the Sunnah, which imply giving ownership to the recipient.
The passage explicitly states 'li-‘adam al-tamlik' (due to lack of ownership).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic categories (fuqara, masakin, etc.) necessitate transferring ownership, not mere permission to use. The word 'tamlik' is the operative concept.
The Hanafi school distinguishes between tamlik and ibahah (permission).
4
Note the ikhtilaf and thamarah
Some schools (e.g., some Maliki positions) allow spending on public works if considered maslaha, but Hanafis uphold tamlik. The practical difference: a mosque built with zakat is invalid; the zakat must be re-distributed.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is strict adherence to tamlik.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٣]قوله : لا إلى بناء مسجد ... الخ ؛ أي لا يجوز صرف الزكاةِ إلى ما ليس فيه تمليك لأحد كبناء المساجد وبناء الرباطات والقناطر، وكري الأنهار ونحو ذلك، وكذا إلى تكفين ميت وتجهيزه وتدفينه ؛ لعدم التمليك فيه، فإن الميت لا يملك، وكذا إلى قضاء دين الميت، وأما قضاء دين الحي فيجوز إن كان بأمره. [٤]قوله : يعتق ؛ أي يعتقه الذي اشتراه بزكاة ماله أو يعتق عليه، بأن اشترى بمال الزكاة ذا رحم محرم منه. [0]قوله : تمليكاً ؛ فلا يكفي فيه إلا طعام إباحة. (1) أي لا يشتري بها رقبة تعتق ؛ لانعدام التمليك فيها. ينظر : «درر الحکام»(۱ : ۱۸۹). (۲) انتهى من (النقاية»(ص٥٢).
[3] His statement: 'not to building a mosque ... etc.'; meaning it is not permissible to spend zakat on that which does not involve giving ownership (tamlik) to anyone, such as building mosques, building ribats (hospices), bridges, digging rivers and the like, and likewise to shrouding a deceased, preparing him and burying him, due to the lack of ownership in it, for the deceased owns nothing. Also similarly to paying off the debt of the deceased. As for paying off the debt of a living person, it is permissible if it is with his command. [4] His statement: 'he frees'; meaning he frees the one whom he bought with the zakat of his wealth, or he is freed upon him, in that he bought with zakat wealth a person who is a mahram relative of his. [0] His statement: 'as ownership'; so mere permission (ibahah) food is not sufficient. (1) That is, he does not buy with it a slave who is freed, due to the absence of ownership in it. Refer to 'Durar al-Hukkam' (1:189). (2) End from 'al-Nuqayah' (p. 52).
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It establishes that zakat must be given as a transfer of ownership (tamlik) to a living person. Therefore, spending zakat on building mosques, bridges, or other public works, or on shrouding and burying the dead, or on paying the debt of a deceased person is not permissible because no living individual receives ownership. However, paying the debt of a living person is permissible if the debtor authorizes it. Similarly, buying a slave with zakat money to set him free is not valid because the ownership is not transferred to the slave himself; rather, the buyer owns the slave. The only exception mentioned is food given as ibahah (permission) which is not sufficient for zakat. The key principle is that zakat is a form of tamlik, not ibahah.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): The act of giving ownership, a necessary condition for the validity of zakat distribution.
إباحة (ibahah): Permission to use without ownership, which is insufficient for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it prohibited to spend zakat on building a mosque?
A) Because it is not a charitable act
B) Because building mosques is not a category in the verse
C) Because zakat requires giving ownership to a person
D) Because it is disliked

Key Takeaway
Zakat must be given as ownership to a living person; expenditures that do not transfer ownership are invalid.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Zakat Must Be Given in Ownership: Prohibited Expenditures
Listing prohibited expenditures for zakat due to lack of tamlik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why zakat cannot be spent on building mosques or providing shrouds, and apply the tamlik requirement to identify prohibited expenditures.

Core Idea
Zakat requires transferring ownership (tamlik) to a recipient; communal and death-related expenses lack this.

This passage from the Hanafi text clarifies that zakat is not a general fund for public works or funeral costs. The key condition is that zakat must be given as ownership (tamlik) to a specific recipient. Thus, building mosques, digging canals, or shrouding the dead are invalid uses. The text also responds to Imam al-Shafi'i's analogy regarding the word 'li' (for) in the zakat verse and in a will.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling on spending zakat on mosques, shrouds, etc.? It is prohibited because it lacks tamlik.
2
Understand the condition of tamlik
Why is tamlik required? Because zakat must be owned by the recipient; the poor must take possession.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i objection
What analogy did Shafi'i use? The word 'li' in a will indicates division, so same in zakat verse.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
How does the text refute it? The lam in zakat verse indicates expenditure category, not division, unlike a will.

لا إلى بناء مسجد، وكفن ميت، وقضاء دينه، وثمن ما يُعْتَقُ فيجب أن يكون مقسوماً أيضاً، فيلزم التسلسل بخلاف ما إذا قال : ثلث مالي للفقراء والمساكين، فعُلِمَ أن المراد بيان المصارف لا القسمة.
(لا إلى بناء مسجد ، وكفن ميت، وقضاء دينه، وثمن ما يُعتق)؛ لأنه البعض تمليك لا بُدَّ أن يملك أحد المستحقين، فلهذا قال في المختصر: فيصرفُ إلى الكل أو أصاب منها الفقير يصدق عليه أنه صدقة فيلزم أن يكون ذلك القدر أيضاً مقسوماً ما على الأصناف، وهكذا إلى غير النهاية.
وبهذا اندفع ما أورد أنه إذا قيل : ماء الكوز منقسم بين اثنين لا يفهم منه إلا أن يكون لكل منهما نصيباً منه، لا أن يقسم كل جزء منه. وجه الدفع : أنه إنما لا يفهم منه؛ لكون المراد بالماء مجموعة دلو حكم به على جنس ماء الكوز لزم ذلك يقيناً.
[١] قوله : بخلاف ... الخ؛ جواب عمّا استشهد به الشافعي، وحاصله : أنَّ قول القائل: ثلث مالي للفقراء والمساكين، ليست اللام فيه لبيان المصرف، بل لبيان القسمة، فلا يصح أن يعطى صنفاً واحداً؛ لكونه مخالفاً لما قصده الواقف أو الموصي بخلاف آية المصارف؛ فإنّ اللام فيها لا يمكن أن تكون للقسمة.
[٢] قوله : لا القسمة؛ أي ليست المراد القسمة ويحتمل أن يكون معناه : لا بيان القسمة، فهو حينئذ مجرور.
[٣] قوله : لا إلى بناء مسجد ... الخ؛ أي لا يجوز صرف الزكاةِ إلى ما ليس فيه تمليك لأحد كبناء المساجد وبناء الرباطات والقناطر، وكري الأنهار ونحو ذلك، وكذا إلى تكفين ميت وتجهيزه وتدفينه؛ لعدم التمليك فيه، فإن الميت لا يملك، وكذا إلى قضاء دين الميت، وأما قضاء دين الحي فيجوز إن كان بأمره.
[٤] قوله : يعتق؛ أي يعتقه الذي اشتراه بزكاة ماله أو يعتق عليه، بأن اشترى بمال الزكاة ذا رحم محرم منه.
[٠] قوله : تمليكاً؛ فلا يكفي فيه إلا طعام إباحة.
(١) أي لا يشتري بها رقبة تعتق؛ لانعدام التمليك فيها. ينظر : درر الحكام (١: ١٨٩).
(۲) انتهى من النقاية (ص٥٢).

ولا إلى من بينهما ولاد، أو زوجية، ومملوكه، وعبد أُعْتِق بعضه، وغَنِي، ومملوكه وطفله وبني هاشم، وهم آل علي وآل عباس، وجعفر، وعقيل، والحارث بن عبد المطلب
[١] قوله : ولا إلى من ... الخ؛ لأنّ منافع الأملاك بينهم متصلة، فلا يتحقق التمليك على الكمال.
[٢] قوله : وعبد؛ ذلك لأنّ معتق البعض بمنزلة المكاتب عنده.
(۳) قوله : وطفله؛ لأن ولد الغني إذا كان صغيراً يُعدُّ غنياً بغنى أبيه، والمنافع متصلة بينهما، والأصل في هذا الباب حديث : «لا تحلّ الصدقة لغني)، أخرجه أبو داود والنسائي وابن ماجة وغيرهم.
ويثبت به حرمته على من ملك ملك الغني، كمملوكه غير المكاتب، فإن صرفه في فك رقبته بالنص القرآني، وكذا في من يكون تحت ولايته، بخلاف ابن الغني البالغ إذا كان فقيراً أو امرأته الفقيرة، فإنّه يجوز دفعه إليهما؛ لأنهما لا يعدان غنيّين لغناه.

(١) وفائدة التخصيص بهؤلاء أنه يجوز الدفع إلى من عداهم من بني هاشم كذرية أبي لهب؛ لأنهم لم يناصروا النبي .. ينظر : الجوهرة النيرة (١: ١٣٢).
(۲) في سنن الترمذي (۳): (٤٢)، و سنن أبي داود (١: ٥١٤)، و سنن النسائي الكبرى (٢: ٥٤)، و المجتبى (۵) (۹۹)، وسنن ابن ماجة (١): (٥٨٩)، و صحيح ابن حبان (۸: ۱۸۷)، و صحيح ابن خزيمة (٤: ٦٩)، وغيرها.
Book of Zakat / Chapter of Expenditures. Not to building a mosque, shroud of a deceased, repaying his debt, price of what is freed. So it must also be divided, otherwise circularity would occur, contrary to if one says: one-third of my wealth is for the poor and needy. So it is known that the intent is to explain the expenditures, not division. (Not to building a mosque, shroud of a deceased, repaying his debt, price of what is freed) because it is a part of ownership; one of the entitled must own it. Hence he said in al-Mukhtasar: 'It is spent on all or (if) one poor person receives from it, it is considered charity, and that portion must also be divided among the categories, and so on ad infinitum.' And with this is repelled the objection that when it is said 'the water of the pitcher is divided between two', it is only understood that each has a share of it, not that each part of it is divided. The rebuttal: it is only not understood because the intended meaning of water is the collective of a bucketful ruled upon as a genus of pitcher-water, so that would necessarily follow. [1] His saying: 'Contrary to... etc.' is a response to what al-Shafi'i adduced. Summary: the statement 'one-third of my wealth is for the poor and needy' - the lam therein is not for specifying expenditure but for specifying division, so it is not valid to give to only one category because it contradicts the intent of the waqf or testator, contrary to the verse of expenditures, for the lam therein cannot be for division. [2] His saying: 'not division' means division is not intended, and it may mean 'not explanation of division', so it is then in genitive. [3] His saying: 'Not to building a mosque... etc.' means it is not permissible to spend zakat on anything that does not involve ownership for someone, like building mosques, ribats (hostels), bridges, digging canals and the like, and likewise shrouding a deceased, preparing and burying him, because there is no ownership in that, for the deceased does not own. Likewise repaying the debt of a deceased. As for repaying the debt of a living person, it is permissible if by his command. [4] His saying: 'is freed' means he frees him by buying him with his zakat wealth, or he is obligated to free him if he buys with zakat wealth a mahram relative of his. [0] His saying: 'ownership' - so only food of mubah (permissible) suffices for it. (1) Meaning he should not buy with it a slave to free because ownership is lacking. See: Durar al-Hukkam (1:189). (2) End from al-Niqayah (p.52). And not to those between whom there is parentage or marriage, and his slave, and a slave partly freed, and a wealthy person, and his slave and his child, and Banu Hashim, and they are the family of Ali and family of Abbas, Ja'far, Aqil, and al-Harith ibn Abd al-Muttalib. [1] His saying: 'And not to those... etc.' because the benefits of properties between them are connected, so complete ownership is not realized. [2] His saying: 'And a slave' because the partial manumitter is like a mukatab (contract slave) according to him. (3) His saying: 'and his child' because the child of a wealthy person, if a minor, is considered wealthy by the wealth of his father, and benefits are connected between them. The basis of this chapter is the hadith: 'Charity is not permissible for a wealthy person,' narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and others. And by it is established the prohibition of giving to anyone who possesses the wealth of the wealthy, like his non-mukatab slave, for spending it on his manumission is by the Quranic text, and likewise to those under his guardianship. Contrary to the mature son of a wealthy person if he is poor, or his poor wife, for it is permissible to give to them because they are not considered wealthy by his wealth. [4] His saying: 'And they are the family of Ali... etc.' Know that al-Abbas and al-Harith are two paternal uncles of the Prophet, the former embraced Islam and was counted among the great Companions, not the latter. Ja'far and Aqil are brothers of Ali ibn Abi Talib, the Prophet's uncle. He is Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Abd al-Muttalib ibn Hashim ibn Abd Manaf. So all of them trace lineage to Hashim, and he had four (sons). (1) The benefit of specifying these is that it is permissible to give to others among Banu Hashim, like the descendants of Abu Lahab, because they did not support the Prophet. See: al-Jawhara al-Nayyira (1:132). (2) In Sunan al-Tirmidhi (3:42), Sunan Abi Dawud (1:514), Sunan al-Nasa'i al-Kubra (2:54), al-Mujtaba (5:99), Sunan Ibn Majah (1:589), Sahih Ibn Hibban (8:187), Sahih Ibn Khuzayma (4:69), etc.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage from Bab al-Masarif (Chapter on Expenditures) of Kitab al-Zakat lists categories to whom zakat cannot be given. The text explains that zakat is an act of tamlik (giving ownership), so it must be given to a specific recipient who takes ownership. Therefore, it cannot be spent on communal projects like building mosques, bridges, or canals, nor on shrouding the deceased or repaying their debts, as these do not involve transferring ownership to an individual. The passage also discusses a refutation of Imam al-Shafi'i's analogy with a will (one-third for the poor and needy), showing that the lam in that context indicates division, not specification of categories, unlike the verse of zakat expenditures.

Then the text lists eight types of prohibited recipients: (1) one's own ascendants (parents, grandparents), (2) descendants (children, grandchildren), (3) spouse (husband or wife), (4) one's own slave, (5) a partially freed slave (since he still has a master), (6) a wealthy person (ghani), (7) a slave of a wealthy person, (8) a minor child of a wealthy person, and (9) Banu Hashim (the Prophet's clan). The reason is that benefits are connected between these individuals and the giver, so complete ownership is not achieved. The hadith 'No charity is permissible for a wealthy person' is cited as the basis. However, exceptions are noted: a mature poor son of a wealthy person and a poor wife may receive zakat. Banu Hashim are specified as the families of Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, Aqil, and al-Harith. Others from Banu Hashim, like descendants of Abu Lahab, can receive zakat because they did not support the Prophet.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership to a specific recipient; zakat must involve ownership.
مصارف (masarif): Expenditure categories for zakat; in this context, the eight categories mentioned in the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it prohibited to use zakat to build a mosque?
A) Mosques are not for the poor.
B) Building a mosque does not involve tamlik (ownership transfer).
C) Mosques can only be funded by sadaqah.
D) The mosque would be owned by Allah, not a person.

Key Takeaway
Zakat must be given in ownership (tamlik) to a poor recipient; any expenditure that does not transfer ownership, such as building mosques or burying the dead, is invalid.

Prohibited Recipients of Zakat: Wealthy, Relatives, and Banu Hashim
Listing prohibited recipients and the hadith basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight categories prohibited from receiving zakat and explain the rationale of connected benefits, including the exception for mature poor relatives and the intra-Hanafi difference on the partially freed slave.

Core Idea
Zakat cannot be given to those who have wealth or whose benefits are connected to the giver, such as parents, children, spouse, slaves, and Banu Hashim.

The passage continues to specify individuals who cannot receive zakat. The key principle is that zakat must be complete ownership, which is not realized when the recipient's benefits are connected to the giver or when the recipient is already wealthy. This lesson covers the eight categories: ascendants, descendants, spouse, own slave, partially freed slave, wealthy person, wealthy person's slave and minor child, and Banu Hashim. Exceptions and the intra-Hanafi difference from Imam Muhammad are also discussed.

Guided Path
1
List the categories
Identify the eight prohibited types from the text.
2
Understand the rationale
Explain why each is prohibited: connected benefits (usul, furu', zawj) or wealth (ghani, slave of ghani, child of ghani) or honor (Banu Hashim).
3
Note exceptions
Adult poor child of wealthy, poor wife of wealthy, and descendants of Abu Lahab.
4
Identify intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Muhammad's view on the partially freed slave.
5
Evaluate the hadith proof
The hadith 'La tahillu al-sadaqatu li ghani' as the basis.

كتاب الزكاة / باب المصارف
لا إلى بناء مسجد، وكفن ميت، وقضاء دينه، وثمن ما يُعْتَقُ فيجب أن يكون مقسوماً أيضاً، فيلزم التسلسل بخلاف ما إذا قال : ثلث مالي للفقراء والمساكين، فعُلِمَ أن المراد بيان المصارف لا القسمة.
(لا إلى بناء مسجد ، وكفن ميت، وقضاء دينه، وثمن ما يُعتق)؛ لأنه البعض تمليك لا بُدَّ أن يملك أحد المستحقين، فلهذا قال في المختصر: فيصرفُ إلى الكل أو أصاب منها الفقير يصدق عليه أنه صدقة فيلزم أن يكون ذلك القدر أيضاً مقسوماً ما على الأصناف، وهكذا إلى غير النهاية.
وبهذا اندفع ما أورد أنه إذا قيل : ماء الكوز منقسم بين اثنين لا يفهم منه إلا أن يكون لكل منهما نصيباً منه، لا أن يقسم كل جزء منه. وجه الدفع : أنه إنما لا يفهم منه؛ لكون المراد بالماء مجموعة دلو حكم به على جنس ماء الكوز لزم ذلك يقيناً.
[١] قوله : بخلاف ... الخ؛ جواب عمّا استشهد به الشافعي، وحاصله : أنَّ قول القائل: ثلث مالي للفقراء والمساكين، ليست اللام فيه لبيان المصرف، بل لبيان القسمة، فلا يصح أن يعطى صنفاً واحداً؛ لكونه مخالفاً لما قصده الواقف أو الموصي بخلاف آية المصارف؛ فإنّ اللام فيها لا يمكن أن تكون للقسمة.
[٢] قوله : لا القسمة؛ أي ليست المراد القسمة ويحتمل أن يكون معناه : لا بيان القسمة، فهو حينئذ مجرور.
[٣] قوله : لا إلى بناء مسجد ... الخ؛ أي لا يجوز صرف الزكاةِ إلى ما ليس فيه تمليك لأحد كبناء المساجد وبناء الرباطات والقناطر، وكري الأنهار ونحو ذلك، وكذا إلى تكفين ميت وتجهيزه وتدفينه؛ لعدم التمليك فيه، فإن الميت لا يملك، وكذا إلى قضاء دين الميت، وأما قضاء دين الحي فيجوز إن كان بأمره.
[٤] قوله : يعتق؛ أي يعتقه الذي اشتراه بزكاة ماله أو يعتق عليه، بأن اشترى بمال الزكاة ذا رحم محرم منه.
[٠] قوله : تمليكاً؛ فلا يكفي فيه إلا طعام إباحة.
(١) أي لا يشتري بها رقبة تعتق؛ لانعدام التمليك فيها. ينظر : درر الحكام (١: ١٨٩).
(۲) انتهى من النقاية (ص٥٢).

ولا إلى من بينهما ولاد، أو زوجية، ومملوكه، وعبد أُعْتِق بعضه، وغَنِي، ومملوكه وطفله وبني هاشم، وهم آل علي وآل عباس، وجعفر، وعقيل، والحارث بن عبد المطلب
[١] قوله : ولا إلى من ... الخ؛ لأنّ منافع الأملاك بينهم متصلة، فلا يتحقق التمليك على الكمال.
[٢] قوله : وعبد؛ ذلك لأنّ معتق البعض بمنزلة المكاتب عنده.
(۳) قوله : وطفله؛ لأن ولد الغني إذا كان صغيراً يُعدُّ غنياً بغنى أبيه، والمنافع متصلة بينهما، والأصل في هذا الباب حديث : «لا تحلّ الصدقة لغني)، أخرجه أبو داود والنسائي وابن ماجة وغيرهم.
ويثبت به حرمته على من ملك ملك الغني، كمملوكه غير المكاتب، فإن صرفه في فك رقبته بالنص القرآني، وكذا في من يكون تحت ولايته، بخلاف ابن الغني البالغ إذا كان فقيراً أو امرأته الفقيرة، فإنّه يجوز دفعه إليهما؛ لأنهما لا يعدان غنيّين لغناه.
[٤] قوله : وهم آل علي ... الخ؛ اعلم أن العباس والحارث عمان للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، أسلم الأوّل، وعُدّ من أجلة الصحابة و لا الثاني. وجعفر وعقيل أخوان لعلي بن أبي طالب عم النبي، وهو محمد بن عبد الله ابن عبد المطلب بن هاشم بن عبد مناف، فكلهم ينتسبون إلى هاشم، وكان له أربعةُ
(١) وفائدة التخصيص بهؤلاء أنه يجوز الدفع إلى من عداهم من بني هاشم كذرية أبي لهب؛ لأنهم لم يناصروا النبي .. ينظر : الجوهرة النيرة (١: ١٣٢).
(۲) في سنن الترمذي (۳): (٤٢)، و سنن أبي داود (١: ٥١٤)، و سنن النسائي الكبرى (٢: ٥٤)، و المجتبى (۵) (۹۹)، وسنن ابن ماجة (١): (٥٨٩)، و صحيح ابن حبان (۸: ۱۸۷)، و صحيح ابن خزيمة (٤: ٦٩)، وغيرها.
Book of Zakat / Chapter of Expenditures. Not to building a mosque, shroud of a deceased, repaying his debt, price of what is freed. So it must also be divided, otherwise circularity would occur, contrary to if one says: one-third of my wealth is for the poor and needy. So it is known that the intent is to explain the expenditures, not division. (Not to building a mosque, shroud of a deceased, repaying his debt, price of what is freed) because it is a part of ownership; one of the entitled must own it. Hence he said in al-Mukhtasar: 'It is spent on all or (if) one poor person receives from it, it is considered charity, and that portion must also be divided among the categories, and so on ad infinitum.' And with this is repelled the objection that when it is said 'the water of the pitcher is divided between two', it is only understood that each has a share of it, not that each part of it is divided. The rebuttal: it is only not understood because the intended meaning of water is the collective of a bucketful ruled upon as a genus of pitcher-water, so that would necessarily follow. [1] His saying: 'Contrary to... etc.' is a response to what al-Shafi'i adduced. Summary: the statement 'one-third of my wealth is for the poor and needy' - the lam therein is not for specifying expenditure but for specifying division, so it is not valid to give to only one category because it contradicts the intent of the waqf or testator, contrary to the verse of expenditures, for the lam therein cannot be for division. [2] His saying: 'not division' means division is not intended, and it may mean 'not explanation of division', so it is then in genitive. [3] His saying: 'Not to building a mosque... etc.' means it is not permissible to spend zakat on anything that does not involve ownership for someone, like building mosques, ribats (hostels), bridges, digging canals and the like, and likewise shrouding a deceased, preparing and burying him, because there is no ownership in that, for the deceased does not own. Likewise repaying the debt of a deceased. As for repaying the debt of a living person, it is permissible if by his command. [4] His saying: 'is freed' means he frees him by buying him with his zakat wealth, or he is obligated to free him if he buys with zakat wealth a mahram relative of his. [0] His saying: 'ownership' - so only food of mubah (permissible) suffices for it. (1) Meaning he should not buy with it a slave to free because ownership is lacking. See: Durar al-Hukkam (1:189). (2) End from al-Niqayah (p.52). And not to those between whom there is parentage or marriage, and his slave, and a slave partly freed, and a wealthy person, and his slave and his child, and Banu Hashim, and they are the family of Ali and family of Abbas, Ja'far, Aqil, and al-Harith ibn Abd al-Muttalib. [1] His saying: 'And not to those... etc.' because the benefits of properties between them are connected, so complete ownership is not realized. [2] His saying: 'And a slave' because the partial manumitter is like a mukatab (contract slave) according to him. (3) His saying: 'and his child' because the child of a wealthy person, if a minor, is considered wealthy by the wealth of his father, and benefits are connected between them. The basis of this chapter is the hadith: 'Charity is not permissible for a wealthy person,' narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and others. And by it is established the prohibition of giving to anyone who possesses the wealth of the wealthy, like his non-mukatab slave, for spending it on his manumission is by the Quranic text, and likewise to those under his guardianship. Contrary to the mature son of a wealthy person if he is poor, or his poor wife, for it is permissible to give to them because they are not considered wealthy by his wealth. [4] His saying: 'And they are the family of Ali... etc.' Know that al-Abbas and al-Harith are two paternal uncles of the Prophet, the former embraced Islam and was counted among the great Companions, not the latter. Ja'far and Aqil are brothers of Ali ibn Abi Talib, the Prophet's uncle. He is Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Abd al-Muttalib ibn Hashim ibn Abd Manaf. So all of them trace lineage to Hashim, and he had four (sons). (1) The benefit of specifying these is that it is permissible to give to others among Banu Hashim, like the descendants of Abu Lahab, because they did not support the Prophet. See: al-Jawhara al-Nayyira (1:132). (2) In Sunan al-Tirmidhi (3:42), Sunan Abi Dawud (1:514), Sunan al-Nasa'i al-Kubra (2:54), al-Mujtaba (5:99), Sunan Ibn Majah (1:589), Sahih Ibn Hibban (8:187), Sahih Ibn Khuzayma (4:69), etc.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage from Bab al-Masarif (Chapter on Expenditures) of Kitab al-Zakat lists categories to whom zakat cannot be given. The text explains that zakat is an act of tamlik (giving ownership), so it must be given to a specific recipient who takes ownership. Therefore, it cannot be spent on communal projects like building mosques, bridges, or canals, nor on shrouding the deceased or repaying their debts, as these do not involve transferring ownership to an individual. The passage also discusses a refutation of Imam al-Shafi'i's analogy with a will (one-third for the poor and needy), showing that the lam in that context indicates division, not specification of categories, unlike the verse of zakat expenditures.

Then the text lists eight types of prohibited recipients: (1) one's own ascendants (parents, grandparents), (2) descendants (children, grandchildren), (3) spouse (husband or wife), (4) one's own slave, (5) a partially freed slave (since he still has a master), (6) a wealthy person (ghani), (7) a slave of a wealthy person, (8) a minor child of a wealthy person, and (9) Banu Hashim (the Prophet's clan). The reason is that benefits are connected between these individuals and the giver, so complete ownership is not achieved. The hadith 'No charity is permissible for a wealthy person' is cited as the basis. However, exceptions are noted: a mature poor son of a wealthy person and a poor wife may receive zakat. Banu Hashim are specified as the families of Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, Aqil, and al-Harith. Others from Banu Hashim, like descendants of Abu Lahab, can receive zakat because they did not support the Prophet.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership to a specific recipient; zakat must involve ownership.
غني (ghani): A wealthy person who is not eligible to receive zakat.
بني هاشم (Banu Hashim): The clan of the Prophet Muhammad; they are prohibited from receiving zakat due to honor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is permitted to receive zakat?
A) One's own father.
B) One's slave.
C) A wealthy person's poor adult son.
D) A partially freed slave.

Key Takeaway
Zakat cannot be given to those whose benefits are connected (ascendants, descendants, spouse, slaves) or who are wealthy, including Banu Hashim, with exceptions for certain poor relatives and non-supporting descendants of Abu Lahab.

Prohibited Recipients of Zakat in Hanafi Fiqh
Listing prohibited Zakat recipients with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories of persons prohibited from receiving Zakat in Hanafi fiqh and explain the legal basis (hadith) and the underlying reasoning for each prohibition.

Core Idea
Zakat cannot be given to those whom the giver is obligated to support or who are already wealthy by proxy.

In the previous lesson, we discussed the eight eligible categories for Zakat. The present passage completes the picture by listing those who are disqualified, even if they appear poor. These include direct relatives, spouses, one's own slaves, the wealthy and their dependents, and the Banu Hashim. The prohibition is rooted in Prophetic hadith and legal reasoning that prevents circular transfer or supporting those already provided for.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act of giving Zakat to certain individuals is ruled haram (impermissible). If given, the Zakat obligation is not fulfilled.
The ruling is for the giver; the recipient becomes unlawful possessor.
2
List the prohibited categories
Enumerate each group mentioned: ascendants and descendants (uli al-ard), spouses, one's own slaves, partially emancipated slaves, rich people, rich people's slaves (except mukatab), rich person's minor child, Banu Hashim, and their freed slaves.
Memorize the list: 9 distinct categories.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The text cites the hadith 'لا تحل الصدقة لغني' (Zakat is not permissible for the rich). The negation 'لا تحل' indicates prohibition. The term 'rich' (ghani) is interpreted broadly to include those whose wealth is imputed from a legal guardian (e.g., minor child of a rich father) or who are maintained by the giver.
Hanafi usul: a command/negation from the Prophet (ﷺ) indicates wujub/tahrim unless contextualized.
4
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider a partially emancipated slave as free, thus eligible to receive Zakat. Abu Hanifa treats him as a slave, so prohibited. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
This is an example of ikhtilaf within the school; the later tradition prefers the view of the Imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا إلى من بينهما ولاد أو زوجية: أي لا يعطي أصله وإن علا وفرعه وإن سفل ولا يعطي الزوج زوجته ولا الزوجة لزوجها. ومملوكه: أي مملوك المزكي. وعبد أعتق بعضه. وغني ومملوكه: أي مملوك الغني والمراد غير المكاتب إذ يجوز أن يؤدي إلى مكاتب الغني. وطفله: أي طفل الرجل الغني. وبني هاشم وهم آل علي وآل عباس وجعفر وعقيل والحارث بن عبد المطلب. ومواليهم.
And not to one between whom and him there is parenthood or marriage: meaning he does not give to his root even if high, nor his branch even if low, nor does the husband give to his wife nor the wife to her husband. And his slave: meaning the slave of the giver of Zakat. And a slave who is partially emancipated. And a rich person, and his slave: meaning the slave of the rich person, the intended meaning is other than the mukatab, for it is permissible to give to the mukatab of a rich person. And his child: meaning the child of a rich man. And the Banu Hashim, and they are: the family of Ali, and the family of Abbas, Ja'far, 'Uqayl, and al-Harith ibn 'Abd al-Muttalib. And their freed slaves.

Key Terms
ولاد (wilaad): Parenthood, meaning direct lineage (ascendants and descendants).
مكاتب (mukaatab): A slave who has a contract of emancipation, part of his price paid. He can own property and may receive Zakat.
بني هاشم (Banu Hashim): The descendants of Hashim, the Prophet's great-grandfather, including the families of Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, 'Uqayl, and al-Harith.
مملوكه (mamlūkuhu): His slave; the slave owned by the giver of Zakat.
غني (ghaniyy): Rich person; one who possesses wealth beyond need.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) A mukatab slave of a rich person
D) A rich person’s minor child

Key Takeaway
Zakat cannot be given to ascendants, descendants, spouses, one's own slaves, partially emancipated slaves, the rich, their non-mukatab slaves and minor children, Banu Hashim, and their freed slaves—even if they appear poor.

Zakat to Mawali and Dhimmis: Prohibition and Exceptions
Rulings on zakat to mawali and dhimmis with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on giving zakat to mawali of Banu Hashim and dhimmis, and explain the evidence and exceptions.

Core Idea
Zakat is restricted to Muslims; it cannot be given to the Prophet's family, their freed slaves, or dhimmis.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the boundaries of zakat distribution. While zakat is for the poor among Muslims, certain categories are excluded entirely. Moreover, other forms of charity are not bound by these restrictions. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correct disbursement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
List the three distinct rulings in the passage: (1) prohibition of zakat to mawali of Banu Hashim, (2) prohibition of zakat to dhimmis, (3) permissibility of other sadaqah to dhimmis.
2
Locate the proof for each
For the first, the hadith of Abu Rafi'; for the second, the hadith of Mu'adh; for the third, the general permissibility of sadaqah to non-Muslims.
3
Understand the exception for 'ushr
The tithe on land is in the same ruling as zakat and thus cannot be given to dhimmis.
4
Analyze the extension to musta'min
The passage notes that a musta'min (non-Muslim with temporary protection) cannot receive any obligatory charity.
5
Apply the principle to descendants of 'Abd al-Muttalib
Zakat can be given to the children of most of his sons except those of 'Abbas, Harith, and Abu Talib, who are considered Hashimites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة/ باب المصارف
ومواليهم ، ولا إلى ذمي، وجازَ غيرُها إليه
[1]قوله : ومواليهم ; لما ورد أن النبي نهى مولاه أبا رافع عن أكل الصدقة، وقال: «مولى القوم من أنفسهم إنا لا تحلّ لنا الصدقة»، أخرجه أبو داود وغيره.
[2]قوله : لا إلى ذمي ; لحديث معاذ إن النبي [؟] الله قال له : «خذها من أغنيائهم وردها إلى فقرائهم» ، أخرجه الأئمة السنّة، وبه استدلّ على أنه من التمليك في الزكاة كما مر ، وعلى كراهته نقل الزكاة على ما سيجيء.
[3]قوله : غيرها ; يستثنى منه العشر ; فإنّه في حكم الزكاة، والمراد به أعم من صدقة التطوع والواجبة كصدقة الفطر وغيرها، والحربي المستأمن لا يجوز دفع الواجبات مطلقاً إليه. كذا في «البحر».
أبناء انقطع نسل الكلّ إلى عبد المطلب، فإنّه أعقب اثني عشرة، وتجوزُ صرف الزكاة إلى أولاد كلّ إذا كانوا مسلمين فقراء، إلا أولاد عباس وحارث وأبي طالب. كذا في «جامع الرموز»، وغيره.
Book of Zakat / Chapter of Expenditures. And their freed slaves, and not to a dhimmi, and other than it is permissible to him. [1] His saying: 'and their freed slaves' because it has been reported that the Prophet forbade his freed slave Abu Rafi' from eating charity, and said: 'The freed slave of a people is from them; indeed charity is not permissible for us.' Reported by Abu Dawud and others. [2] His saying: 'not to a dhimmi' due to the hadith of Mu'adh that the Prophet [?] said to him: 'Take it from their rich and return it to their poor.' Reported by the Imams of the Sunnah, and it is used as evidence that zakat involves ownership as previously mentioned, and for the dislike of transferring zakat as will come. [3] His saying: 'other than it' excludes the 'ushr (tithe) because it is in the ruling of zakat, and what is meant is general including voluntary charity and obligatory like sadaqat al-fitr and others, and the musta'min harbi (non-Muslim seeking protection) is absolutely not permissible to give obligatory [charity] to him. As in 'al-Bahr'. The children whose lineage ends to 'Abd al-Muttalib, for he had twelve children, and it is permissible to give zakat to each of his children if they are Muslims and poor, except the children of 'Abbas, Harith, and Abu Talib. As in 'Jami' al-Rumuz' and others.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage lays down three rulings: (1) Zakat cannot be given to the freed slaves (mawali) of those who are prohibited from receiving zakat themselves, specifically the mawali of the Prophet's family (Banu Hashim). The proof is the hadith where the Prophet forbade his freed slave Abu Rafi' from eating charity, saying 'Mawla al-qawm min anfusihim' meaning the freed slave shares the same rulings as his masters. Since charity is forbidden for the Prophet and his family, it is also forbidden for their freed slaves. (2) Zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi (a non-Muslim living under Muslim protection). The proof is the hadith of Mu'adh where the Prophet instructed him to take zakat from the rich Muslims and give it to their poor Muslims. This indicates that zakat is specifically for Muslims. (3) Other forms of charity (such as voluntary sadaqah or obligatory sadaqah like sadaqat al-fitr) may be given to dhimmis. An exception is made for 'ushr (tithe on land) which is similar to zakat in ruling. Also, a musta'min (non-Muslim with temporary protection) cannot receive any obligatory charity. The additional note clarifies that among the descendants of 'Abd al-Muttalib, zakat may be given to the children of most of his sons except the children of 'Abbas, Harith, and Abu Talib because they are considered Hashimites who are prohibited from receiving zakat.

Key Terms
مولي (mawla): Freed slave; specifically in this context, the freed slaves of the Prophet's family (Banu Hashim).
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen living under Muslim protection and paying jizyah.
العشر (al-'ushr): The tithe (10% on produce of irrigated land) which is in the ruling of zakat and cannot be given to dhimmis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can zakat be given to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen)?
A) Yes, it is permissible.
B) No, it is not permissible; only other sadaqah may be given.
C) It is permissible but disliked.
D) It is permissible only if the dhimmi is poor.

Key Takeaway
Zakat is exclusively for Muslim poor; it cannot be given to the Prophet's family, their freed slaves, or dhimmis; other sadaqah has wider scope.

Mistaken Zakat Payment: When Repetition Is Required and When Not
Ruling on mistaken zakat payment with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between cases where zakat must be repeated due to a mistaken recipient and where it remains valid, applying the Hanafi criterion of tamlik (ownership transfer).

Core Idea
Zakat paid to one's own slave fails because ownership is not transferred; other mistaken recipients do not invalidate if the payer acted in good faith.

When you give zakat to someone you believe is eligible but later discover otherwise, the ruling depends on the type of ineligibility. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position: if the recipient turns out to be your slave or mukatab, the zakat is invalid and must be repeated. But if they turn out to be rich, a disbeliever, your father, son, or a Hashimi, the zakat is valid and no repetition is needed. We will also examine Imam Abu Yusuf's dissent and the evidence that resolves the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of mistaken recipients
The author lists two groups: (1) slave/mukatab – repetition required; (2) rich/kaafir/father/son/Hashimi – repetition not required. Note the distinction.
The condition of eligibility (ghina, Islam, etc.) is separate from the condition of ownership transfer.
2
Understand the condition of tamlik for slave/mukatab
For the slave or mukatab, the payment fails because the giver cannot truly own the zakat and giving to one's own slave does not transfer ownership fully. This is a condition (shart) for valid zakat payment.
This is by consensus – all agree repetition is required here.
3
For other ineligible recipients, apply the principle of intention
The hadith of Yazid shows that when the Prophet said 'for you is what you intended,' intention based on a good-faith supposition suffices. The giver did what was in his capacity.
This is the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf argues that once the error becomes certain, the supposition is worthless, so repetition is always required. The response: the giver is not responsible for hidden facts.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: under Abu Yusuf, zakat would be invalid in all mistaken cases.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text takes Abu Hanifa's view as the relied-upon position, citing the hadith of Yazid. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Students should apply this in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دفع إلى من ظن أنه مصرف، فبان أنه عبده، أو مكاتبه يعيدها. وإن بان غناه، أو كفره، أو أنه أبوه، أو ابنه، أو هاشمي لم يعد خلافاً لأبي يوسف.

[4]قوله : إلى من ظنّ ... الخ ; فإن صرف إلى من ظنّه غير مصرف، أو شك ولم يتحر لم يجز، حتى يظهر أنه مصرف، فيجزئه. كذا في «النهر» [0]قوله : يعيدها ; أي تجب عليه إعادة الزكاة ; لأنّ ما أدّاه فقد فيه شرط الأداء، وهو تمليك غيره تمليكاً كاملاً. (1) أي تجب إعادة الزكاة; لأنه لم يخرج عن ملكه خروجاً صحيحاً، وهذا بالإجماع. ينظر : الاختيار (١ : ١٥٨).

[1]قوله : خلافاً لأبي يوسف له ; له : أنه قد ظهر خطؤه بيقين، ولا عبرة بالظنّ الذي تبين خطؤه. ، ولنا : أنه أتى بما في وسعه ، وهو تمليك المصرف على ظنّه، ويشهد له أن يزيد بن معن له دفع الصدقة إلى أبيه معن الله ، ثم ظهر له ذلك ، وقال : ما إياك أردت، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «يا يزيد، لك ما نويت ويا معن لك ما أخذت)، أخرجه البخاري.
He gave to whom he thought was a recipient, then it became clear that he was his slave, or his mukatab, he repeats it. And if it becomes clear that he is rich, or a disbeliever, or that he is his father, or his son, or a Hashimi, he does not repeat it, contrary to Abu Yusuf.

[4] His saying: 'to whom he thought... etc.' So if he gave to someone he thought was not a recipient, or he doubted and did not ascertain, it is not valid until it becomes apparent that he was a recipient, then it suffices. As in 'al-Nahr'. [0] His saying: 'he repeats it' meaning repetition of zakat is obligatory upon him, because what he paid lacked the condition of performance, which is complete ownership of another. (1) meaning repetition of zakat is obligatory, because it did not leave his ownership in a valid manner, and this is by consensus. See al-Ikhtiyar (1:158).

[1] His saying: 'contrary to Abu Yusuf' - his proof: that his error has become certain, and no consideration is given to a supposition that turned out to be wrong. And for us: he did what was in his capacity, which is transferring ownership to the recipient based on his supposition, and supporting him is that Yazid ibn Ma'n gave charity to his father Ma'n Allah, then it became apparent to him, and he said: 'I did not mean you,' so the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him said: 'O Yazid, for you is what you intended, and O Ma'n, for you is what you took.' Reported by al-Bukhari.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where a person gives zakat to someone he believes is an eligible recipient, but later discovers otherwise. The ruling distinguishes between two categories: (1) If the recipient turns out to be the giver's own slave (mamluk) or mukatab (slave under contract of manumission), the zakat is invalid and must be repeated. This is because the giver cannot own the zakat himself, and giving it to his own slave does not truly transfer ownership—it remains under his control, so the condition of tamlik (transfer of ownership) is not fulfilled. This is by consensus. (2) If the recipient turns out to be rich (independent of zakat), a disbeliever (dhimmi or harbi), the giver's father, son, or a Hashimi (descendant of Hashim), then according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, the zakat is valid and does not need to be repeated. The reasoning is that the giver did his due diligence based on his best supposition (zann), and he cannot be held responsible for hidden facts. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that once the error is certain, the supposition is nullified. The Hanafi majority relies on the hadith of Yazid ibn Ma'n, who gave charity to his father thinking he was eligible, and when the Prophet was informed, he confirmed the validity of the charity based on Yazid's intention. This hadith establishes that a good-faith mistake does not invalidate the act.

Key Terms
مكاتبه (mukatabuh): A slave who has made a contract with his master to earn his freedom by paying a sum of money.
هاشمي (Hashimi): A descendant of Hashim, the great-grandfather of the Prophet; prohibited from receiving zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person gives zakat to someone he believes is a poor Muslim, but later discovers that the recipient is his own father who is not in need, according to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling?
A) The zakat is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The zakat is valid and does not need repetition.
C) The zakat is valid only if the father was actually poor.
D) The zakat is invalid only if the giver knew the truth beforehand.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that zakat paid in good faith to an apparently eligible recipient is valid even if later proven ineligible, except when the recipient is the payer's own slave or mukatab, where ownership transfer fails.

Recommended and Disliked Practices in Zakat Distribution
Rulings on recommended amount and disliked practices in zakat distribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended amount to give in zakat and identify the situations in which it is disliked to give a large sum or transfer zakat, applying the Hanafi rulings.

Core Idea
Zakat distribution: give enough for a day's independence; avoid giving a full nisab to a single non-indebted poor; avoid transferring zakat after the year except to relatives.

This lesson explains three key rulings from a classical Hanafi text on how to distribute zakat wisely. It covers the recommended amount to give a poor person, the dislike of giving a large sum (the nisab) to one person without special need, and the dislike of transferring zakat to another city after the year has passed, with an important exception for relatives. Understanding these rules helps ensure that zakat is distributed in a balanced way, benefiting the poor without causing social or economic disruption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended amount
Find the statement that encourages giving an amount sufficient for one day's needs. Understand the wisdom of avoiding extreme poverty while not overendowing.
The passive voice 'hubiba' indicates a recommended (mustahabb) act.
2
Recognize the dislike of giving a large sum to one person
Note that giving 200 dirhams (the nisab) or more to a single poor person who is not in debt and has no dependents is disliked (makruh tanzih). The exception: if the recipient is in debt or has dependents to support, the dislike is removed.
The underlying reason is to avoid making the recipient overly wealthy at once and to encourage wider distribution.
3
Understand the ruling on transferring zakat to another city
Transferring zakat to another city after the year is disliked because the local poor have a prior claim. However, if paid in advance (before the year ends), there is no dislike. Also, giving to a relative in another city is exempt from this dislike.
The hadith about relatives reinforces the merit of maintaining kinship ties.
4
Apply the rulings to a practical scenario
Given a specific amount and set of poor individuals, decide how to distribute to avoid disliked actions while fulfilling the obligation.
Consider the status of each recipient: debt, dependents, location, relationship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحبب دفع ما يُغنيه عن السؤال ليوم، وكره دفع مئتي درهم إلى فقير غير مديون، ونقلها إلى بلد آخر إلا إلى قريبه

[2]قوله : وحبب ; بصيغة المجهول ; أي يُستحب أن يدفع من الزكاة لواحد من الفقراء مقداراً يكفيه ويغنيه عن السؤال ليوم واحد، وكُرة دفع مقدار النصاب أو أزيد منه لواحد، إلا إذا كان المدفوع إليه مديوناً أو كان ذا عيال، بحيث لو فرقه عليهم لا يبقى فضل. كذا في «الفتح»).
[3] قوله : إلى بلد آخر ; هذا إذا كان أخرجها بعد الحول ; لأنّ حق فقراء بلده تعلّق بها أما إذا عجلها قبله فلا يكره نقلها. كذا في «الخلاصة».
[4]قوله : قريبه ; أي من له قرابة بالمزكّي، فقد ورد : «أنه لا يقبلُ الله الصدقة من رجل وله قرابة محتاجون إلى صلته ويصرفها إلى غيرهم» أخرجه الطبراني مرفوعاً.
And it is recommended (passive voice) to give what makes him independent from asking for a day, and it is disliked to give two hundred dirhams to a poor person who is not in debt, and to transfer it to another city except to his relative.

[2] His saying: 'and it is recommended' in the passive voice: i.e., it is recommended to give from the zakat to one of the poor an amount that suffices him and makes him independent from asking for one day, and it is disliked to give the amount of nisab or more to one person, unless the recipient is in debt or has dependents such that if he distributed it among them nothing extra remains. As in 'al-Fath'.
[3] His saying: 'to another city' – this is if he paid it after the year has passed, because the right of the poor of his city is attached to it; but if he paid it before the year, then there is no dislike in transferring it. As in 'al-Khulasa'.
[4] His saying: 'his relative' i.e., one who has kinship with the giver, for it has been reported: 'Indeed Allah does not accept the charity of a man who has needy relatives to whom he should give but he gives to others.' Reported by al-Tabarani as marfu'.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage outlines three subsidiary rulings regarding the distribution of zakat. First, it is recommended (mustahabb) to give a poor person enough zakat to cover his needs for one day and make him independent from begging. However, it is disliked (makruh) to give a large amount like 200 dirhams (the nisab of zakat) or more to a single poor person who is not in debt, unless he has dependents to support or is in debt himself, such that distributing the large amount among them would leave no surplus. The reason is to avoid making the recipient too wealthy at once, which might change his behavior. Second, it is disliked to transfer zakat from one city to another after the zakat has become due (after the year), because the poor of the locality have a right over it. But if the zakat was paid before the year (i.e., in advance), there is no dislike in transferring it. Third, it is especially recommended to give zakat to relatives who are in need, to fulfill both the obligation of zakat and the duty of maintaining kinship ties. A hadith warns that Allah does not accept charity from one who neglects his needy relatives.

Key Terms
مئتي درهم (mi'atay dirham): Two hundred dirhams, which is the nisab for zakat, indicating a significant amount.
مديون (madyun): A person in debt; giving a larger amount to such a person is not disliked because he needs to clear his debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) When the giver is rich.

Key Takeaway
In distributing zakat, give enough for a day, avoid giving a full nisab to a single non-indebted poor, and avoid transferring zakat after the year except to relatives.

Zakat Not Repeated When Recipient's True Status Discovered
Ruling and proof for validity of Zakat given in good faith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Zakat given to an ineligible recipient and evaluate the evidence from the hadith of Yazid bin Ma'n.

Core Idea
Zakat given in good faith is valid even if the recipient is later found ineligible — intention suffices.

When you give Zakat, you are required to ensure the recipient is eligible (poor, Muslim, not a descendant of the Prophet, etc.). But what happens if you later discover your assessment was wrong? The Hanafi school, relying on a clear prophetic hadith, holds that the Zakat is valid and does not need to be repeated. This lesson unpacks that ruling, the proof, and the intra-school disagreement with Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving Zakat to someone believed to be eligible. The ruling is that the Zakat is valid (sahih) and does not need to be repeated (lam yu'ad).
The matn explicitly lists five scenarios of ineligibility that might become apparent later.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith of Yazid bin Ma'n, recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari. The Prophet (PBUH) told Yazid, 'For you is what you intended, and for Ma'n is what he took.'
This is a hadith ahad, but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala) regarding the validity of the act based on intention.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's statement explicitly validates both the giver's intention and the recipient's taking. This indicates that the Zakat is effective despite the mistaken identity, because the giver fulfilled his obligation by acting on his best conjecture.
The key operative term is 'ما نويت' (what you intended), which the Hanafis use to prioritize intention over outcome.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf disagreed, arguing that since the error is certain, the original conjecture is invalid, so the Zakat must be repeated.
His proof: certainty overrides conjecture when the error is discovered.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) side with the hadith, and the commentary (and later Hanafi fatwa) follows this view. The mufta bihi is that Zakat is not repeated.
The strength of the hadith and the principle of acting within one's capacity ('ma fi was'ihi') outweigh the purely logical argument of Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن بان غناه، أو كفره، أو أنه أبوه، أو ابنه، أو هاشمي لم يعد خلافاً لأبي يوسف. قوله: خلافاً لأبي يوسف. له: أنه قد ظهر خطؤه بيقين، ولا عبرة بالظن الذي تبين خطؤه. ولنا: أنه أتى بما في وسعه، وهو تمليك المصرف على ظنّه، ويشهد له أن يزيد بن معن له دفع الصدقة إلى أبيه معن [؟]، ثم ظهر له ذلك، وقال: ما إياك أردت، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «يا يزيد، لك ما نويت ويا معن لك ما أخذت»، أخرجه البخاري.
And if it becomes apparent that he (the recipient) is rich, or a disbeliever, or that he is his father, or his son, or a Hashimi, it is not repeated, contrary to Abu Yusuf. He said: opposite to Abu Yusuf. For him: that his error has become manifest with certainty, and there is no consideration for a conjecture whose error is apparent. And for us: that he did what was within his capacity, which is giving ownership to the recipient based on his conjecture, and as evidence for him is that Yazid bin Ma'n gave charity to his father Ma'n, then it became apparent to him, and he said: 'I did not intend you,' so the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'O Yazid, for you is what you intended, and O Ma'n, for you is what you took,' reported by al-Bukhari.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn of Al-Wiqayah, expanded in the sharh. The issue: if a person gives Zakat to someone he believes is eligible, but later discovers the recipient was actually rich, a disbeliever, a direct ascendant/descendant, or a Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet), does the Zakat need to be given again? The Hanafi position, based on the proof from the hadith of Yazid bin Ma'n, is that it does not need to be repeated. Abu Yusuf disagreed, arguing that since the error is certain, the presumption no longer holds. However, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that the giver did his duty by acting on his best judgment, and the hadith supports this: the Prophet told Yazid that his intention was credited and Ma'n could keep the charity. Thus, the Zakat is valid.

Key Terms
لم يعد (lam yu'ad): The Zakat does not need to be repeated or given again.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Zakat is invalid and must be given again.
B) The Zakat is valid and does not need to be repeated.
C) The Zakat is valid but you must inform the rich person.
D) The Zakat becomes a voluntary charity.

Key Takeaway
Zakat given to a person who appears eligible, even if later found ineligible, remains valid and does not need to be repeated, because the giver fulfilled his obligation based on his best judgment.

Recommended Amount and Disliked Giving in Zakat
Ruling on amount of Zakat given to an individual

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recommended amount (enough for one day) and the disliked amount (nisab or more) of Zakat given to a single poor person, and identify the exceptions.

Core Idea
Zakat aims to alleviate need, not create wealth — give enough for a day, not a full nisab to one person.

In distributing Zakat, the amount given to a single recipient matters. The Hanafi school provides guidance to balance generosity with the purpose of Zakat: to meet immediate needs without making the recipient dependent or overly wealthy. This lesson explains the recommended and disliked amounts, and when exceptions apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the passage carefully. Find the two distinct hukm levels: one recommended (حُبِّبَ) and one disliked (كُرِهَ). What specific amounts are associated with each?
The recommended amount is 'ما يُغنيه عن السؤال ليوم' (what suffices him from asking for a day). The disliked amount is 'مئتي درهم' (200 dirhams, the nisab) or more.
2
Understand the hukm levels
The passive form 'حُبِّبَ' indicates istihbab (recommendation), a level below sunnah but above mubah. 'كُرِهَ' indicates karahah tanzihiyyah (disliked but not prohibited). Why are these levels chosen?
The recommendation encourages giving enough for one day to remove immediate need. The dislike discourages giving a large lump sum that might make the recipient independent of Zakat in the future, violating the circulation of wealth.
3
Identify the exception
The disliked ruling has an exception: if the recipient is indebted (مديون) or has dependents (عيال) such that distributing the amount among them leaves no surplus, then giving the nisab is no longer disliked. Why?
Because the large amount is actually needed to cover multiple obligations, so it does not create unwanted independence.
4
Trace the commentary expansion
The commentary (قوله: وحبب...) expands on the matn by clarifying the passive voice and the exact meaning. It also adds the exception explicitly, confirming from al-Fath. How does this expansion help avoid misunderstanding?
The commentary ensures that the exception is clearly stated, preventing rigid application of the dislike.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a person who wants to give Zakat to a poor man who has a large family. According to the ruling, is giving a full nisab (200 dirhams) disliked?
No, because the recipient has dependents; the amount is needed and the dislike is removed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَحبب دفع ما يُغنيه عن السؤال ليوم، وكُره دفع مئتي درهم إلى فقير غير مديون. قوله: وحبب؛ بصيغة المجهول؛ أي يُستحب أن يدفع من الزكاة لواحد من الفقراء مقداراً يكفيه ويغنيه عن السؤال ليوم واحد، وكُره دفع مقدار النصاب أو أزيد منه لواحد، إلا إذا كان المدفوع إليه مديوناً أو كان ذا عيال، بحيث لو فرقه عليهم لا يبقى فضل. كذا في «الفتح».

Thus in al-Fath.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings regarding the amount of Zakat given to an individual. First, it is recommended (mustahabb) to give an amount that covers the recipient's needs for one day, saving them from begging. Second, it is disliked (makruh) to give a full nisab (200 dirhams) or more to a single poor person who is not indebted. The rationale is to avoid creating a situation where the recipient becomes wealthy from Zakat, which contradicts the purpose of redistributing wealth. However, an exception is made if the poor person has debts or many dependents, so that the large amount is actually needed to cover their obligations. The commentary clarifies that the dislike applies to giving a large lump sum; giving smaller amounts to multiple poor people is better.

Key Terms

مئتي درهم (mi'atay dirham): Two hundred dirhams, which is the nisab for Zakat on silver.

Key Takeaway
It is recommended to give Zakat enough for one day, and disliked to give a full nisab to a non-indebted poor person unless they have dependents.
