Transferring Zakat: Timing and Relatives
Ruling on moving Zakat funds to another locality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on transferring Zakat to another city and explain the exception for relatives, applying the correct timing condition.

Core Idea
After the year, Zakat belongs to local poor; before the year, transfer is free — but relatives always come first.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical question: can you send your Zakat to another city? The answer depends on timing and relationship. After the Zakat becomes obligatory, the rights of the local poor are attached, so transferring is disliked. But if you pay early, before the year ends, you may send it anywhere. And an exception: transferring to needy relatives is recommended, supported by a hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is transferring Zakat to another city after the haul (year). The default ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked).
This is because the rights of the local poor have attached to the Zakat.
2
Distinguish the timing
If Zakat is paid in advance before the haul, the local poor's rights have not yet attached, so transferring is not disliked; it is mubah.
3
Identify the exception for relatives
Transferring to a needy relative is not disliked; it is recommended (mustahabb) and removes the karahah.
The exception is for any relative of the giver.
4
Locate the dalil
The dalil is a marfu' hadith recorded by al-Tabarani: 'Indeed, God does not accept charity from a man who has needy relatives deserving of his support and he gives it to others.'
5
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly shows that charity to non-relatives when relatives are needy is not accepted, implying the preference for relatives. It is not evidence of prohibition but of recommendation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونقلها إلى بلد آخر إلا إلى قريبه. قوله: إلى بلد آخر؛ هذا إذا كان أخرجها بعد الحول؛ لأنّ حق فقراء بلده تعلّق بها أما إذا عجلها قبله فلا يكره نقلها. كذا في «الخلاصة». قوله: قريبه؛ أي من له قرابة بالمزكّي، فقد ورد: «أنه لا يقبلُ الله الصدقة من رجل وله قرابة محتاجون إلى صلته ويصرفها إلى غيرهم» أخرجه الطبراني مرفوعاً.
And transferring it to another city except to his relative. He said: to another city; this is when he has taken it out after the year, because the right of the poor of his city has attached to it. But if he gave it in advance before the year, then there is no dislike in transferring it. Thus in al-Khulasah. He said: his relative; meaning whoever has kinship with the giver of Zakat, for it has been reported: 'Indeed, God does not accept charity from a man who has needy relatives deserving of his support and he gives it to others,' reported by al-Tabarani as a marfu' hadith.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues regarding the transfer of Zakat. First, the general ruling: it is disliked (makruh) to transfer Zakat from one city to another after the year is complete, because the poor of the locality have a right to it. However, if the Zakat was paid in advance before the year's end, transfer is not disliked. Second, an exception is made for relatives: it is not disliked to transfer Zakat to one's relatives who are in need. The proof is a hadith warning against giving charity to others when one's own relatives are needy. This emphasizes the priority of family ties, as supporting relatives is an obligation (silat al-rahim) and charity starts with them.

Key Terms
الحول (al-hawl): The lunar year after which Zakat becomes obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Transferring Zakat after the year is disliked unless to a relative; before the year, transfer is permissible.

Zakat for the Student of Knowledge: Exception to the Wealth Barrier
Ruling on Zakat distribution preference and exception for students of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on giving Zakat to a wealthy student of knowledge and explain the reasoning based on analogy with the Zakat collector (amil).

Core Idea
Zakat can be given to a wealthy student of knowledge if he devotes himself to learning, akin to the amil.

The text from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya expands on a short phrase in the matn: 'or to one more needy than the people of his city.' It lists several categories where transferring Zakat is commendable, including the student of knowledge. A key point is the permissibility of giving Zakat to a student even if he possesses the nisab, provided his devotion to learning prevents him from earning. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its foundation in analogy and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling in the matn
The matn permits transferring Zakat to a recipient more needy than the people of the donor's city. This is the context for the exceptions that follow.
2
Recognize the listed exceptions
The sharh lists who qualifies: more righteous, more pious, more beneficial, a refugee from Dar al-Harb, and a student of knowledge (talib 'ilm).
These categories share a common trait: they serve the community or are in dire need.
3
Understand the student of knowledge exception
Ibn Abidin's research, cited in the text, holds that a student of knowledge devoted to learning and unable to earn may take Zakat even if he is rich. This is based on the hadith: 'It is permissible to give Zakat to a student of knowledge even if he has expenses for forty years.'
The student's service to religion is seen as analogous to the amil's service, who is also allowed Zakat despite wealth.
4
Trace the analogy (qiyas)
The reasoning is that just as the amil is paid for his work collecting Zakat, the student is engaged in preserving and transmitting knowledge, which benefits the ummah. Thus, his need for financial support justifies the exception.
The analogy is used to override the general rule that Zakat is only for the poor.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
A Zakat committee or individual can prioritize a full-time student of sacred knowledge over other recipients, even if the student has savings up to nisab, as long as his studies prevent him from earning a livelihood.
This ruling is from later Hanafi fatwas (mutakhkhirin) and is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).

Source Text

أو إلى أحوج من أهل بلده. قوله: أو إلى أحوج؛ أصلح أو أورع أو أنفع للمسلمين، أو من دار الحرب إلى دار الإسلام، أو إلى طالب علم. كذا في «البحر»، وغيره. (۱) ولأهمية الاهتمام بطالب العلم الشرعي أذكر بحث ابن عابدين في جواز صرف الزكاة له وإن كان غنياً، قال في منحة الخالق ٢ : ٢٦٠) : «في «منح الغفار» بعد ذكره عن «البدائع» من تعليل حل الدفع للعامل الغني، بأنه فرغ نفسه لهذا العمل فيحتاج إلى «الكفاية» إلخ قال : وبهذا التعليل يقوى ما نسب إلى بعض الفتاوى أن طالب العلم يجوز له أن يأخذ الزكاة، وإن كان غنياً إذا فرغ نفسه لإفادة العلم واستفادته لكونه عاجزا عن الكسب، والحاجة داعية إلى ما لا بد منه، وهكذا رأيته بخط موثوق وعزاه إلى الواقعات، والله تعالى أعلم اهـ. قلت : وقد رأيته أيضا في جامع الفتاوى معزيا إلى «المبسوط» ، ونصه : وفي «المبسوط» لا يجوز دفع الزكاة إلى من يملك نصابا إلا إلى طالب العلم والغازي والمنقطع لقوله عليه السلام ويجوز دفع الزكاة لطالب العلم ، وإن كان له نفقة أربعين سنة اهـ.
Or to one more needy than the people of his city. He said: or to the more needy; more righteous, or more pious, or more beneficial to Muslims, or from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam, or to a student of knowledge. Thus in al-Bahr and others. (1) And due to the importance of paying attention to the student of Islamic knowledge, I mention the research of Ibn Abidin on the permissibility of disbursing Zakat to him even if he is rich. He said in Minhat al-Khaliq 2:260: 'In Minh al-Ghaffar, after mentioning from al-Bada'i' the reasoning for the permissibility of payment to the rich worker (amil), that he has devoted himself to this work and needs sufficiency, etc., he said: By this reasoning, what is attributed to some fatwas is strengthened: that a student of knowledge is permitted to take Zakat, even if he is rich, when he has devoted himself to acquiring and imparting knowledge, being unable to earn, and necessity calls for what is indispensable. This is how I saw it in a reliable hand and it is attributed to al-Waqi'at, and God knows best. End.' I said: I also saw it in Jami' al-Fatawa attributed to al-Mabsut, and its text: 'In al-Mabsut, it is not permissible to give Zakat to one who possesses a nisab except to a student of knowledge, a warrior (ghazi), and one cut off (munqati'), due to his saying, peace be upon him: it is permissible to give Zakat to a student of knowledge even if he has expenses for forty years.'
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage expands on the exception 'or to one more needy than the people of his city' from the matn. It explains that transferring Zakat is actually commendable when the recipient is more deserving in terms of righteousness, piety, benefit, or if he is a refugee from hostile territory. Special attention is given to students of knowledge. The commentator cites Ibn Abidin's research where he permits giving Zakat to a student of knowledge even if he possesses the nisab, provided he has devoted himself to learning and cannot earn a living. The reasoning is analogous to the paid Zakat collector (amil) who is allowed Zakat despite being rich because he serves the Muslim community. This is supported by a narration in al-Mabsut that explicitly allows Zakat for students of knowledge, warriors, and those cut off from resources, even if they have provisions for forty years. Thus, the priority is to support those who benefit the community.

Key Terms
طالب علم (talib 'ilm): Student of Islamic knowledge who is devoted to learning and cannot earn a livelihood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abidin, under what condition may a student of knowledge receive Zakat even if he is rich?
A) He must be poor.
B) He must have devoted himself to learning and cannot earn.
C) He must be in debt.
D) He must be a descendant of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows Zakat to be given to a student of knowledge who is wealthy if he is devoted to learning and unable to earn, by analogy with the amil and supported by hadith.
